PREFACE 
    This Code constitutes a complete recodification of the general and permanent ordinances of the City of Eufaula, Alabama. 
    Source materials used in the preparation of the Code were the 1974 Code, as supplemented through March 5, 1990, and ordinances subsequently adopted by the council. The source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof. The absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the Code. By use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this Code, the reader can locate any section of the 1974 Code, as supplemented, and any subsequent ordinance included herein. 
    The chapters of the Code have been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order, and the various sections within each chapter have been catchlined to facilitate usage. Notes which tie related sections of the Code together and which refer to relevant state law have been included. A table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the Code is included at the back of this Code. 
Chapter and Section Numbering System 
    The chapter and section numbering system used in this Code is the same system used in many state and local government codes. Each section number consists of two parts separated by a dash. The figure before the dash refers to the chapter number, and the figure after the dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter. Thus, the second section of chapter 1 is numbered 1-2, and the first section of chapter 6 is 6-1. Under this system, each section is identified with its chapter, and at the same time new sections or even whole chapters can be inserted in their proper place by using the decimal system for amendments. For example, if new material consisting of one section that would logically come between sections 10-1 and 10-2 is desired to be added, such new section would be numbered 10-1.5. New chapters may be included by using one of the reserved chapter numbers. Care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters. New articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or, in the case of articles, may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject, and, in the case of divisions, may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject. The next successive number shall be assigned to the new article or division. 
Page Numbering System 
    The page numbering system used in this Code is a prefix system. The letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume. The number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion. In the case of a chapter of the Code, the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter. 
CODE CD1:1 CODE COMPARATIVE TABLES CCT:1 STATE LAW REFERENCE TABLE       SLT:1 CODE INDEX CDi:1  
Index 
    The index has been prepared with the greatest of care. Each particular item has been placed under several headings, some of which are couched in lay phraseology, others in legal terminology, and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees. There are numerous cross references within the index itself which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested. 
Looseleaf Supplements 
    A special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication. With this system, the publication will be kept up-to-date. Subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited, and the appropriate page or pages affected will be reprinted. These new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication, with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages. 
    Keeping this publication up-to-date at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication. As revised sheets are received, it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions. It is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and, in addition, that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes. 
Acknowledgments 
    This publication was under the direct supervision of Roger D. Merriam, Supervising Editor, and Jody Wilson, Editor, of the Municipal Code Corporation, Tallahassee, Florida. Credit is gratefully given to the other members of the publisher's staff for their sincere interest and able assistance throughout the project. 
    The publisher is most grateful to former Mayor Sam Slade, City Attorney Jimmy S. Calton, and City Clerk/Treasurer Linda W. Howell, CMC for their cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this publication. It is hoped that their efforts and those of the publisher have resulted in a Code of Ordinances which will make the active law of the city readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the day-to-day administration of the city's affairs. 
MUNICIPAL CODE CORPORATION 
Tallahassee, Florida  
ADOPTING ORDINANCE 
ORDINANCE NO. 1993-3 
An Ordinance Adopting and Enacting a New Code for the City of Eufaula, Alabama; Providing for the Repeal of Certain Ordinances Not Included Therein; Providing a Penalty for the Violation Thereof; Providing for the Manner of Amending Such Code; and Providing When Such Code and This Ordinance Shall Become Effective. 
Be it Ordained by the City Council of the City of Eufaula, Alabama, as follows: 
    Section 1. The Code entitled "Code of Ordinances, City of Eufaula, Alabama," published by Municipal Code Corporation, consisting of Chapters 1 through 98, each inclusive, is adopted. 
    Section 2. All ordinances of a general and permanent nature enacted on or before October 5, 1992, and not included in the Code or recognized and continued in force by reference therein, are repealed. 
    Section 3. The repeal provided for in Section 2 hereof shall not be construed to revive any ordinance or part thereof that has been repealed by a subsequent ordinance that is repealed by this ordinance. 
    Section 4. Unless another penalty is expressly provided, every person convicted of a violation of any provision of the Code or any ordinance, rule or regulation adopted or issued in pursuance thereof, shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $500.00, imprisonment not exceeding six months or any combination thereof. Each act of violation and each day upon which any such violation shall occur shall constitute a separate offense. The penalty provided by this section, unless another penalty is expressly provided, shall apply to the amendment of any Code section whether or not such penalty is reenacted in the amendatory ordinance. In addition to the penalty prescribed above, the city may pursue other remedies such as abatement of nuisances, injunctive relief and revocation of licenses or permits. 
    Section 5. Additions or amendments to the Code when passed in the form as to indicate the intention of the city council to make the same a part of the Code shall be deemed to be incorporated in the Code, so that reference to the Code includes the additions and amendments. 
    Section 6. Ordinances adopted after October 5, 1992, that amend or refer to ordinances that have been codified in the Code, shall be construed as if they amend or refer to like provisions of the Code. 
    Section 7. This ordinance shall become effective immediately upon its passage and approval by the mayor, or upon its otherwise becoming a law. 
    Adopted and approved this 15th day of March, 1993. 
CITY OF EUFAULA, ALABAMA, A MUNICIPAL CORPORATION

SUPPLEMENT HISTORY TABLE 
    The table below allows users of this Code to quickly and accurately determine what ordinances have been considered for codification in each supplement. Ordinances that are of a general and permanent nature are codified in the Code Book and are considered "Includes." Ordinances that are not of a general and permanent nature are not codified in the Code Book and are considered "Omits." 
    In addition, by adding to this table with each supplement, users of this Code of Ordinances will be able to gain a more complete picture of the Code's historical evolution.

Chapter 1 - GENERAL PROVISIONS 
  

Sec. 1-1. - Code designated and cited. 
    The ordinances embraced in this and the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated the "Code of Ordinances, City of Eufaula, Alabama," and may be so cited. 
(Code 1974, § 1-1) 
State Law reference- Authority of city to provide for the revision and codification of its ordinances and for the adoption of a code, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-7. 
Sec. 1-2. - Rules of construction and definitions. 
    In the construction of this Code, and of all ordinances and resolutions passed by the city council, the following rules of construction and definitions apply, unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the council or the context of the provisions. 
    Generally. The provisions of this Code shall be liberally construed to effect the purposes expressed therein or implied from the expression thereof. In case of doubt or ambiguity in the meaning of such provisions, the general shall yield to the particular. Interpretation and construction shall tend to further the accomplishment of the elimination of the particular mischiefs for which the provisions were enacted. 
    Bond. When a bond is required, an undertaking in writing shall be required. 
    City. City means the City of Eufaula, Alabama. 
    City council. Council or city council means the city council of the City of Eufaula, constituting the governing body of the city. 
    City officers and departments. Whenever reference is made to an officer or a department, the reference shall be construed as if followed by the words "of the City of Eufaula, Alabama." Reference to a specific officer shall include his authorized deputies, agents and representatives. 
    Code. Code means the Code of Ordinances, Eufaula, Alabama, as designated in section 1-1. 
    Code of Ala. 1975. Code of Ala. 1975 means the Code of Alabama 1975, as amended. 
    Computation of time. In computing any period of time, the day of the act, event or default from which the designated period of time begins to run shall not be included. The last day of the period so computed shall be included, unless it is a Saturday, a Sunday or a legal holiday, in which event the period runs until the end of the next day which is not a Saturday, a Sunday or a legal holiday. When the period of time prescribed or allowed is less than seven days, intermediate Saturdays, Sundays and legal holidays shall be excluded in the computation. 
    County. County means Barbour County, Alabama. 
    Gender. A word importing the masculine gender only shall extend and be applied to females and to firms, partnerships and corporations as well as to males. 
    Joint authority. Words purporting to give authority to three or more officers or other persons shall be construed as giving such authority to a majority of such officers or other persons, unless it is otherwise declared. 
    May. May is to be construed as being permissive. 
    May not. May not states a prohibition. 
    Month. Month means a calendar month. 
    Must. Must is to be construed as being mandatory. 
    Number. Words used in the singular include the plural, and the plural includes the singular. 
    Oath. Oath is to be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in such cases, the words "swear" and "sworn" are equivalent to the words "affirm" and "affirmed." 
    Owner. Owner, applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or tenant by the entirety, of the whole or of a part of such building or land. 
    Person. Person includes a corporation, a firm, partnership, association, organization or any other group acting as a unit or its agent or assignee, as well as a natural person. 
    Personal property. Personal property includes every species of property except real property. 
    Preceding, following. Preceding and following mean next before and next after, respectively. 
    Property. Property includes real and personal property. 
    Real property. Real property includes lands, tenements and hereditaments. 
    Shall. Shall is to be construed as being mandatory. 
    Sidewalk. Sidewalk means a strip of land in front of or on the sides of a building or lot of land, lying between the property line and the street. 
    Signature or subscription. Signature or subscription includes a mark when the person cannot write. 
    State. State means the State of Alabama. 
    Street. Street includes any street, avenue, boulevard, road, alley, lane, viaduct and other public ways in the city and all parts thereof within the designated right-of-way. 
    Technical and nontechnical words. All words and phrases are to be construed and understood according to the common and approved usage of the language, but technical words and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate meaning in the law are to be construed and understood according to such peculiar and appropriate meaning. 
    Tense. Words used in the present or past tense include the future, as well as the present and past. 
    Writing. Writing or written includes printing on paper. 
    Year. Year means a calendar year. 
(Code 1974, § 1-2) 
State Law reference- Definitions and rules of construction, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 1-1-1, 1-1-2. 
Sec. 1-3. - Catchlines of sections, effect of history notes and references in Code. 
(a)  The catchlines of the sections of this Code printed in boldface type are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the sections and are not to be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections nor as any part of such sections nor, unless expressly so provided, are they to be so deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. 
(b)  The history or source notes appearing in parentheses after sections in this Code are not intended to have any legal effect but are merely intended to indicate the source of matter contained in the section. Cross references and state law references which appear after sections or subsections of this Code or which otherwise appear in footnote form are provided for the convenience of the user of this Code and have no legal effect. 
(c)  All references to chapters, articles or sections are to the chapters, articles and sections of this Code, unless otherwise specified. 
(Code 1974, § 1-5) 
Sec. 1-4. - Police jurisdiction. 
(a)  This Code and all ordinances of the city apply in the police jurisdiction of the city and to all property or rights-of-way belonging to the city to the maximum extent authorized or required by Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-40-10, 11-51-91, and other applicable law. The use of the phrase "in the city" shall include the city's police jurisdiction and all such property and rights-of-way. 
(b)  As provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-40-10 the police jurisdiction covers all adjoining territory within three miles of the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1974, §§ 1-3, 1-4) 
Sec. 1-5. - Effect of repeal of ordinances. 
(a)  The repeal of an ordinance shall not revive any ordinances in force before or at the time the ordinance repealed took effect. 
(b)  The repeal of an ordinance shall not affect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took effect nor any suit, prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the repeal for an offense committed or cause of action arising under the ordinance repealed. 
(Code 1974, § 1-6) 
Cross reference- Manner of repealing ordinances, § 2-38. 
Sec. 1-6. - General penalty; continuing violations. 
(a)  In this section, the phrase "violation of this Code" means: 
(1)  Doing an act that is prohibited or made or declared unlawful, an offense, an offense against the city, or a misdemeanor by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance; 
(2)  Failure to perform an act that is required to be performed by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance; or 
(3)  Failure to perform an act if the failure is declared a misdemeanor, an offense, an offense against the city, or unlawful by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance. 
(b)  In this section, the phrase "violation of this Code" does not include the failure of a city officer or city employee to perform an official duty, unless it is provided that failure to perform the duty is to be punished as provided in this section. 
(c)  Except as otherwise provided, a person convicted of a violation of this Code shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $500.00, imprisonment or confinement at hard labor for a term not exceeding six months, or any combination thereof. The penalty imposed upon a corporation shall consist of the fine only, plus costs of court. No penalty shall exceed the maximum established by state statute for the commission of a substantially similar offense. For violations of this Code that are continuous with respect to time, each day the violation continues is a separate offense. 
(d)  The imposition of a penalty does not prevent revocation or suspension of a license, permit or franchise. 
(e)  Violations of this Code that are continuous with respect to time may be abated by injunctive or other equitable relief. The imposition of a penalty does not prevent equitable relief. 
Cross reference- Municipal court, § 34-26 et seq.; working out fines and costs, § 34-41; court costs, § 34-46. 
State Law reference- Penalty for ordinance violations, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-9. 
Sec. 1-7. - Severability of parts of Code. 
    The sections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of this Code are severable, and if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section of this Code shall be declared unconstitutional by the valid judgment or decree of a court of competent jurisdiction, such unconstitutionality shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs and sections of this Code. 
(Code 1974, § 1-7) 
Sec. 1-8. - Amendments to Code. 
    All ordinances passed subsequent to this Code which amend, repeal or in any way affect this Code may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion therein or, in the case of repealed chapters, sections and subsections or any part thereof, by subsequent ordinances, such repealed portions may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages affected thereby, and the subsequent ordinances as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of such subsequent ordinances until such time that this Code and subsequent ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a new Code by the city council. 
(Code 1974, § 1-8) 
Sec. 1-9. - Supplementation of Code. 
(a)  By contract or by city personnel, supplements to this Code shall be prepared and printed whenever authorized or directed by the council. A supplement to the Code shall include all substantive permanent and general parts of ordinances adopted during the period covered by the supplement and all changes made thereby in the Code. The pages of a supplement shall be so numbered that they will fit properly into the Code and will, where necessary, replace pages that have become obsolete or partially obsolete, and the new pages shall be so prepared that, when they have been inserted, the Code will be current through the date of the adoption of the latest ordinance included in the supplement. 
(b)  In preparing a supplement to this Code, all portions of the Code that have been repealed shall be excluded from the Code by the omission thereof from reprinted pages. 
(c)  When preparing a supplement to this Code, the codifier (meaning the person, agency or organization authorized to prepare the supplement) may make formal, nonsubstantive changes in ordinances and parts of ordinances included in the supplement, insofar as it is necessary to do so to embody them into a unified code. For example, the codifier may: 
(1)  Organize the ordinance material into appropriate subdivisions; 
(2)  Provide appropriate catchlines, headings and titles for sections and other subdivisions of the Code printed in the supplement and make changes in such catchlines, headings and titles; 
(3)  Assign appropriate numbers to sections and other subdivisions to be inserted in the Code and, where necessary to accommodate new material, change existing section or other subdivision numbers; 
(4)  Change the words "this ordinance" or words of the same meaning to "this chapter," "this article," "this division," etc., as the case may be, or to "sections ____________ to ____________ " (inserting section numbers to indicate the sections of the Code which embody the substantive sections of the ordinance incorporated into the Code); and 
(5)  Make other nonsubstantive changes necessary to preserve the original meaning of ordinance sections inserted into the Code, but in no case shall the codifier make any change in the meaning or effect of ordinance material included in the supplement or already embodied in the Code. 
Sec. 1-10. - Provisions considered as continuations of existing ordinances. 
    The provisions appearing in this Code, so far as they are the same in substance as those of ordinances of the city existing at the time of the adoption of this Code, shall be considered as continuations thereof and not as new enactments. 
Sec. 1-11. - Certain ordinances not affected by Code. 
(a)  Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code shall be construed to repeal or otherwise affect the validity of any of the following: 
(1)  Any ordinance promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the city, or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of the city or any evidence of the city's indebtedness. 
(2)  Any appropriation ordinance, including those providing for or related to an annual budget, or prescribing salaries for city officers and employees. 
(3)  Any ordinance describing the boundaries of the city, annexing territory to the city or discontinuing territory as a part of the city. 
(4)  Any ordinance granting any franchise. 
(5)  Any zoning ordinance. 
(6)  Any ordinance adopting or affecting the license code or requiring or related to any privilege or occupational license or tax, including alcoholic beverages. 
(7)  Any ordinance assessing or related to taxes, including any license tax, ad valorem tax, gross receipts tax, cigarette tax, tax on the sale or distribution of gasoline or other liquid motor fuels and kerosene, license tax for taxpaying gas districts or license tax for furnishing rooms or lodging to transients. 
(8)  Any ordinance pertaining to the housing authority. 
(9)  Any ordinance pertaining to natural gas. 
(10)  Any ordinance ordering an election. 
(11)  Any ordinance making appointments to positions, offices or boards. 
(12)  Any ordinance providing for local improvements or levying assessments for public improvements. 
(13)  Ordinances authorizing deeds, leases, contracts or other such instruments. 
(14)  Ordinances under which vested rights may have accrued as to persons in whom such rights may have vested. 
(15)  Any ordinance dedicating, accepting, naming, establishing, locating, relocating, opening, paving, widening or vacating any street or other public way in the city or relating to municipal street maintenance agreements with the state or establishing or prescribing grades for streets in the city. 
(16)  Any ordinance establishing or relating to any public corporation or board not in this Code. 
(17)  Any ordinance which, by its own terms, is effective for a stated or limited term. 
(18)  Any ordinance dedicating or accepting any subdivision plat. 
(19)  Any ordinance adopted for purposes which have been consummated. 
(20)  Any ordinance which is temporary, although general in effect. 
(21)  Any ordinance which is special, although permanent in effect. 
(b)  All such ordinances are recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out at length in this Code. 
(Code 1974, § 1-9) 
Sec. 1-12. - Code does not affect prior offenses, rights, etc. 
(a)  Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code shall affect any offense or act committed or done or any penalty or forfeiture incurred or any contract or right established or accruing before the effective date of this Code. 
(b)  The adoption of this Code shall not be interpreted as allowing any use or the continuance of any use of a structure or premises in violation of any ordinance of the city in effect on the date of adoption of this Code. 
Sec. 1-13. - Issuance of summons and complaint in lieu of arrest for violation of certain ordinances and statutes. 
    Any law enforcement officer of the city or state may, in lieu of placing persons under custodial arrest, issue a summons and complaint to any person charged with violating any ordinances or law specified or mentioned in Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-9.1. It is the intent of the council to exercise the maximum authority granted by Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-9.1, as amended.

(Code 1974, § 2-1) 
Sec. 2-2. - Seal. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-40-2. 
(Code 1974, § 2-2)

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-31. - Filling of vacancies. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-41. 
(Code 1974, § 2-48) 
Sec. 2-32. - Councilmembers not to be appointed to certain other city offices or have interest, etc., in city contracts, etc. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-53. 
(Code 1974, § 2-51) 
Sec. 2-33. - Removal of councilmembers for voting on certain matters or for holding other municipal offices or having prohibited interest in contracts. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-54. 
(Code 1974, § 2-53) 
Sec. 2-34. - Councilmembers not to vote on certain matters. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-54. 
(Code 1974, § 2-52) 
Sec. 2-35. - Compensation. 
    Effective on the first Monday in October, 1996, councilmembers shall be compensated the sum of $500.00 per month. 
(Code 1974, § 2-47.1; Ord. No. 1996-1, 1-8-96) 
State Law reference- Council to fix salary of councilmembers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-2. 
Sec. 2-36. - Councilmembers prohibited from misappropriating funds; impeachment for same authorized. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-162. 
(Code 1974, § 2-247)

    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-2. 
(Code 1974, §§ 1-11, 1-12, 2-100) 
Sec. 2-38. - Repeal of ordinances. 
    Ordinances must be specially repealed. No ordinance shall be repealed by implication. 
Cross reference- Effect of repeals, § 1-5. 
Sec. 2-39. - Publication and recordation of ordinances; effective date of ordinances; adoption of technical codes by reference authorized. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-8. 
(Code 1974, § 1-13) 
Secs. 2-40-2-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - MEETINGS 

Sec. 2-51. - Application of division. 
    The rules or order of procedure contained in this division shall govern deliberations and meetings of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 1, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 1, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-52. - Meetings to be public. 
    All meetings, regular and special, shall be opened to the public. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, §§ 5, 16, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 5, 10-7-96) 
State Law reference- Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-43-49, 13A-14-2. 
Sec. 2-53. - Calling special meetings. 
    Special meetings may be held at the call of the council president by serving notice on each member of the council not less than 24 hours before the time set for such special meeting; or special meetings may be held as provided by Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-50, whenever two aldermen or mayor request in writing that the presiding officer call such meeting; upon the failure or refusal of the council president to call such meeting when requested, the two aldermen or the mayor making the request shall have the right to call such meeting. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 3, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 3, 10-7-96) 
State Law reference- Special meetings, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-50. 
Sec. 2-54. - Days of regular meetings. 
    Regular meetings of the city council shall be held on the following dates: the first and third Mondays at 5:15 p.m. of each month. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 2, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 2, 10-7-96) 
State Law reference- Duty of council to determine time for meetings, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-49; required number of regular meetings, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-50. 
Sec. 2-55. - Place of regular meetings. 
    All regular meetings of the city council shall convene at the city hall. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 5, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 5, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-56. - Quorum. 
    A quorum shall be determined as provided by Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-48, as amended. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 4, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 4, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-57. - Rules of order. 
    Robert's Rules of Order, 9th Edition, to be designated by the presiding officer, will be applied if a situation is not covered in the preceding rules of procedure. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 23, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 23, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-58. - Vote required for altering, amending or temporarily suspending rules. 
    The rules of the city council may be altered, amended or temporarily suspended by a vote of two-thirds of the members present. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 18, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 18, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-59. - Order of business. 
    The order of business at council meetings shall be as follows: 
(1)  Call to order. 
Invocation. 
Roll call. 
Honors and recognition. 
(2)  Approval of the agenda. 
(3)  Consent agenda. 
All items on the consent agenda have been distributed to each member of the city council for reading and study, are considered to be routine, and will be enacted by one motion of the city council with no separate discussion. If separate discussion is desired, that item may be removed from the consent agenda and placed on the regular agenda by request. 
(4)  Report of mayor. 
(5)  Visitors. 
(6)  Ordinances and resolutions. 
(7)  Public hearings. 
(8)  Unfinished business. 
(9)  Regular agenda (new business). 
(10)  Council action/discussion. 
Council committee reports. 
(11)  Adjournment. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 6, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1995-7, 6-5-95; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 6, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-60. - Permission required to speak more than twice. 
    No member of the city council shall speak more than twice on the same subject without permission of the presiding officer. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 7, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 7, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-61. - Permission required to address council. 
    No person, not a member of the city council, shall be allowed to address the city council while in session without permission of the presiding officer. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 8, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 8, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-62. - City officers and employees to attend meetings on request. 
    All officers or employees of the city shall, when requested, attend all meetings of the city council and shall remain in the council room for such length of time as the council may direct. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 21, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 21, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-63. - Motions to reconsider. 
    Motions to reconsider must be by a member of the city council who voted with the majority and at the same or next succeeding meeting of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 11, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 11, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-64. - Requests for recording of votes and division on questions. 
    Whenever it shall be required by one or more members of the city council, the yeas and nays shall be recorded; and any member may call for a division on any question. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 12, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 12, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-65. - Deciding questions of order. 
    All questions of order shall be decided by the presiding officer of the city council, with the right of appeal to the city council by any member. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 13, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 13, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-66. - Presiding officer's request for member to take chair. 
    The presiding officer of the city council may, at his discretion, call any member to take the chair, to allow such presiding officer to address the city council, make a motion or discuss any matter at issue. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 14, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 14, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-67. - Motions and questions first in order. 
    Motions of the city council to lay any matter on the table shall be first in order, and on all questions the last amendment, the most distant day and the largest sum shall be put first. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 15, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 15, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-68. - Standing committees established. 
    The standing committees of the city council are established as follows: 
(1)  Finance. 
(2)  Streets/sanitation/cemetery. 
(3)  Police and fire. 
(4)  Parks/recreation/airport. 
(5)  Education/library/zoning. 
(Ord. No. 1992-15, § 1(2-50), 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-16, § 1, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-69. - Committee reports. 
    The presiding member of each respective committee or the councilmember acting for such presiding member shall submit or make all reports to the city council when so requested by the presiding officer or any member of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 19, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 19, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-70. - Reports by department, board or agency heads who receive funds-Procedure. 
(a)  Oral and written reports. At the first regular meeting of the council of the second month of each quarter, the head of each department, board or agency of the city that receives funds from the city budget shall attend and make an oral and written report for the previous quarter. 
(b)  Contents. Such report shall include but not be limited to expenses incurred by accounts as specified or approved by the mayor and a comparison of expenditures with amounts budgeted by and for such department, board or agency. 
(c)  Presiding member. The councilmember who is the presiding member of any committee, under which such department, board or agency operates, shall also make an oral or written report to the council. 
(Code 1974, § 2-3) 
Sec. 2-71. - Same-Failure to report. 
    Every officer whose duty it is to report at the regular meetings of the city council who shall be in default thereof may be fined at the discretion of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 9, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 9, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-72. - Legislation-Generally. 
(a)  All ordinances, resolutions or propositions submitted to the city council that require the expenditure of money shall lie over until the next regular meeting. Such ordinances, resolutions or propositions may be considered earlier by unanimous consent of the city council. This rule shall not apply to the current expenses of or contracts previously made with or regular salaries of officers or wages of employees of the city. 
(b)  No ordinance or resolution of a permanent nature shall be adopted at the meeting at which it is introduced unless unanimous consent is obtained for the immediate consideration of such ordinance or resolution; such consent shall be by a roll call and the vote thereon spread on the minutes. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, §§ 20, 22, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, §§ 20, 22, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-73. - Same-Writing required. 
    Motions shall be reduced to writing when required by the presiding officer of the city council or any member of the city council. All resolutions and ordinances shall be in writing. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 10, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 10, 10-7-96) 
Sec. 2-74. - Motions for adjournment. 
    A motion for adjournment of the city council shall always be in order. 
(Ord. No. 1992-14, § 17, 10-5-92; Ord. No. 1996-15, § 17, 10-7-96) 
Secs. 2-75-2-85. - Reserved.

ARTICLE III. - OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-121. - Authority to create or abolish offices and positions. 
    The city council may, from time to time, as it may deem best for the interests of the city, create any new or abolish any existing office or position or may change or add to or modify the duties of any officer or employee. 
(Code 1974, § 2-195) 
Sec. 2-122. - Personnel rules. 
    Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code repeals or otherwise affects the validity of the city's personnel rules, being Ord. No. 1987-1, as amended. 
Sec. 2-123. - Qualifications and duties of certain officials. 
    The qualifications and duties of city officials mentioned in this article shall be in addition to those more logically and conveniently enumerated elsewhere in this Code. The duties of city officers and employees which are enumerated generally in this article shall not be deemed to be exclusive, but the duties of such officers and employees shall include such other related work as may be required. 
(Code 1974, § 2-194) 
Sec. 2-124. - Qualification of mayor, councilmembers and officers. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-1. 
(Code 1974, § 2-47) 
Sec. 2-125. - Officers' oaths. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-4-6 and Ala. Const. § 279. 
(Code 1974, § 2-202) 
Sec. 2-126. - Bond required. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-13. 
(Code 1974, § 2-203) 
Sec. 2-127. - Premiums on bonds paid by city. 
    The premiums on all official bonds required of city officers and employees shall be paid by the city. 
(Code 1974, §§ 2-204-2-208) 
Sec. 2-128. - Authority of council to fix salaries. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-43-3, 11-43-7. 
(Code 1974, § 2-201) 
Sec. 2-129. - Payment of salaries. 
    All salaries shall be paid in accordance with the city's personnel rules. 
Sec. 2-130. - Removal of officers generally. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-160. 
(Code 1974, § 2-245) 
Sec. 2-131. - Power of council or committee to subpoena witnesses and documents for impeachment hearings; oaths and order at such hearings; secretary for such committees. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-163. 
(Code 1974, § 2-48) 
Sec. 2-132. - Prohibited interests in contracts. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-12. 
(Code 1974, § 2-196) 
Sec. 2-133. - Exercise of functions of mayor during absence or disability of mayor; filling of vacancies in offices of mayor, president and president pro tempore of council. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-42. 
(Code 1974, § 2-49) 
Sec. 2-134. - Mayor and councilmembers subject to impeachment for acceptance of employment with public service corporation or having prohibited private or personal financial dealings with city. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-161. 
(Code 1974, § 2-246) 
Sec. 2-135. - Inspection of books and papers of officers and agents. 
    Every officer or agent of the city shall at reasonable times submit such officer's or agent's books and papers to the inspection of the city council or to any person or committee appointed or authorized by the council to examine the books and papers. 
(Code 1974, § 2-197) 
Sec. 2-136. - Delivery of materials to successor of officers and agents. 
    Every officer or agent of the city, on going out of office, shall deliver over to his successor or to the city council, as the case may require, all books, papers, accounts, tools, instruments and everything pertaining to his office and shall be entitled to a receipt therefor if requested. 
(Code 1974, § 2-199) 
Sec. 2-137. - Defense and indemnification. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Employee includes all employees of the city, whether classified or not, or employees of any board appointed entirely by the mayor or city council, excluding the board of education. 
    Officer includes any elected or appointed official of the city or member of any board appointed entirely by the mayor or city council, excluding the board of education. 
(b)  Defense in actions. Among the duties of the city attorney shall be that of representing as counsel, with the attorney fees and litigation fees being borne solely by the city, any city officer or employee in connection with any claim, suit for damages or other action against such person arising in connection with the performance by such officer or employee of his public duties. Such officer or employee may have his own counsel to assist in the defense, at the expense of the officer or employee. 
(c)  Indemnification. Any officer or employee who is held liable for the payment of any claims or damages, by way of judgment or settlement, shall be entitled to indemnification by the city, where the acts resulting in such liability were done in good faith, without malice, within the scope of authority of the officer or employee. Any judgment rendered against an officer or employee, whether for compensatory or punitive damages, shall be presumed to have arisen from an act performed in good faith and without malice, provided that the act was performed within the scope of authority, and further provided that the city council does not find by resolution that the act was not performed in good faith or that the act was performed with malice. This indemnification shall be secondary to any insurance coverage from any other source which covers the officer or employee for the same acts giving rise to the officer's or employee's liability. No insurance company shall have any cause of action, direct or indirect, for reimbursement from the city for any expenses or judgments paid in covering such officer or employee for such acts. 
(d)  City's defenses. Nothing in this section shall be construed as waiving the city's defense of governmental immunity to it or its officers or employees in any action brought against the city or such officer or employee or to in any way expand upon the limitation of liability in state courts as set forth in the appropriate sections of state law. 
(e)  Notice. The provisions of this section shall apply only where the city has been given notice of any action brought against any city officer or employee, based upon any action of such officer or employee within the scope of authority as such. 
(f)  Conflict of interest. Nothing in this section or in any ordinance of the city and nothing in any agreement with the city attorney shall be construed to require the city attorney to provide legal services in any manner which would cause the attorney to be involved in a conflict of interest. If the city attorney is not able to participate in the defense of an officer or employee because of a conflict of interest, the city council shall employ another attorney to provide such defense. 
(Code 1974, § 2-209) 
State Law reference- Providing defense council, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-24. 
Sec. 2-138. - Use of city vehicles by certain city personnel; policy established. 
(a)  The city has established an effective take- home vehicle program for designated employees, officers driving marked cars and other law enforcement officials driving unmarked cars for law enforcement purposes. 
(b)  The mayor is directed to have each department within the city government establish a policy for the vehicle take-home program, and such policy shall clearly prohibit personal use (except for commuting or de minimus personal use of the vehicle) outside of the city limits. 
(Code 1974, § 2-210) 
Secs. 2-139-2-150. - Reserved.

DIVISION 3. - CITY ATTORNEY[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference- Municipal court, § 34-26 et seq. 

Sec. 2-166. - Office created. 
    There is created the office of city attorney for the city. 
(Code 1974, § 2-13) 
Sec. 2-167. - Election by council; term of office. 
    The city attorney shall be elected by the city council at its first regular meeting following the city election or as soon thereafter as possible. The city attorney's term of office shall be for four years and until his successor is elected and qualified. 
(Code 1974, § 2-14) 
State Law reference- Election of officers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-3. 
Sec. 2-168. - Retainer and compensation. 
    The city attorney shall receive a salary or retainer to be fixed by the city council, payable monthly, and also such additional compensation as the council may authorize or approve. 
(Code 1974, § 2-15) 
Sec. 2-169. - Powers and duties. 
    The city attorney shall be the legal adviser of the city in all matters in which such attorney's advice may be desired by the city council, mayor or city clerk/treasurer. The city attorney shall advise the city council, mayor and city clerk/treasurer when requested as to all legal questions that may arise before them in relation to their duties or in relation to the interest of the city and shall, from time to time, make such reports in relation to suits or legal proceedings in which the city is interested as may be requested by the mayor or council. The city attorney shall represent the city within the state in all civil judicial proceedings, suits, actions and contests in which it shall have an interest. The city attorney shall attend all regular and special meetings of the council and shall draft all routine ordinances and resolutions and shall perform all other duties as attorney for the city which may be required by the council. The city attorney shall not be required to prosecute or otherwise participate in the trial of criminal or quasi-criminal cases in the municipal court or in the circuit court or any other court on appeal thereto from the municipal court. 
(Code 1974, § 2-16) 
Secs. 2-170-2-180. - Reserved.

Sec. 2-181. - Offices of clerk and treasurer consolidated. 
    The offices of city clerk and city treasurer are created and are consolidated as authorized by Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-3. The bond of the clerk shall include such officer's faithful performance of the duties of the city treasurer and the safe custody of the funds of the city. 
(Code 1974, §§ 2-28, 2-34, 2-111, 2-193)

DIVISION 5. - SUPERINTENDENT OF STREETS AND SANITATION[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Cross reference- Solid waste, ch. 78; streets, sidewalks, and miscellaneous public places, ch. 82. 

Sec. 2-201. - Office created. 
    There is created the office of superintendent of streets and sanitation. 
(Code 1974, § 2-261) 
Sec. 2-202. - Appointment; term; salary. 
    The superintendent of streets and sanitation shall be elected by the city council at its first regular meeting in October of each year. The superintendent's term of office shall be for one year and until his successor is elected and qualified. The superintendent's salary shall be fixed by the city council. 
(Code 1974, § 2-262) 
State Law reference- Election of officers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-3. 
Sec. 2-203. - Powers and duties generally. 
    The superintendent of streets and sanitation shall have the following powers and perform the following duties: 
(1)  Have the charge and control of the street working force of the city consisting of laborers, trucks, road machinery, parts, tools, implements and equipment of all kinds for the cleaning, repair and improvement of streets and handling of solid waste. 
(2)  Devote his whole time and attention to the control and management of such department during working hours, except when absent on the business of the office. 
(3)  Apply that working force to the performance of such work of the city as directed by the committee on streets and sanitation. 
(4)  Keep a correct account of all road machinery, parts, tools, implements, automobiles, trucks, equipment, etc., under his charge, and any deficiency therein not accounted for shall be charged to him and deducted from his wages. 
(5)  Cause to be removed all obstacles, which he may find in the streets, alleys, sewers, drains, ditches, sidewalks and pavements, and if any person creating such obstruction or his agent shall fail or refuse to remove the obstacle, the superintendent shall report such facts to the mayor. 
(6)  Cause to be removed from the streets, public alleys, pavements and sidewalks all nuisances and shall report to the mayor the person causing such nuisance, if known. 
(7)  Report to the mayor and chief of police all persons who refuse to remove dead animals from their premises, and if the owner of a dead animal is unknown, the superintendent shall assist the chief of police in promptly removing the dead animal. 
(8)  Have the power to hire all laborers necessary for conducting the affairs of the department subject to approval of the mayor. 
(9)  Have the power to discharge any laborer who refuses to obey his orders and must immediately report the discharge to the mayor. 
(10)  See that all laborers employed by the street department discharge their duties and keep the time of all laborers employed by the department and report all time lost by such laborers to the mayor. 
(11)  Have charge and control of all persons sentenced to hard labor on the streets of the city and see that they perform the labor required of them and that none escapes from his custody. 
(12)  See that due care is taken of all shade trees in or on the streets of the city and take such steps as are necessary to keep and preserve the trees. It shall be his duty to set out additional trees whenever it is necessary. 
(13)  Enforce all provisions of this Code relating to solid waste and to that end have the authority and power conferred by the provisions of this Code pertaining thereto. 
(14)  In addition, serve as sanitation officer for the city and as such shall do and perform all such duties with regard to the enforcement of the provisions of this Code relative to health and sanitation as the council may direct. 
(15)  Do all other things required of him by the mayor and the council. 
(Code 1974, § 2-263) 
Secs. 2-204-2-215. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - LICENSE INSPECTOR 

Sec. 2-216. - Created. 
    There is created the office of license inspector for the city who shall hold office for such time and at such salary as the city council may designate. 
(Code 1974, § 2-177) 
Sec. 2-217. - Powers and duties. 
    It shall be the duty of the license inspector to see that no person escapes the payment of requisite license, privilege, occupation or similar taxes or pays a smaller amount than the law permits or does business at a different place than that authorized in the license or does business under a transferred license or an assumed name. He shall see that no frauds are perpetrated upon the city by licensees or other persons. 
(Code 1974, § 2-178) 
Sec. 2-218. - Right of inspection and check for undervaluation. 
    The license inspector shall have the right of inspection and examination of all businesses and licenses issued thereon and shall see that such licenses are conspicuously displayed and that the business on all licenses correspond with the entries of the business on the licenses. When the licensee is graduated according to amount of merchandise or a similar method or capital stock, he shall see that no material undervaluations occur. 
(Code 1974, § 2-179) 
Sec. 2-219. - Report of illegal transfers of licenses to council. 
    The license inspector shall report to the city council any license transferred without the consent of the council, together with the names of transferor and transferee, and he shall report to the council all instances of particular businesses being carried on thereunder by other persons than those to whom the licenses were granted. 
(Code 1974, § 2-180) 
Sec. 2-220. - Additional duties. 
    The license inspector shall do and perform all other duties designated and required by the city council. 
(Code 1974, § 2-181) 
Secs. 2-221-2-240. - Reserved.

Footnotes:

Sec. 2-251. - Created; appointment; qualifications. 
    There is created a planning commission for the city. Members shall be appointed for the terms and in the manner set forth as required by law. Of the appointees there shall be at least one and not more than two persons whose vocation or occupation for at least two years prior to such appointment shall have been that of real estate broker, real estate sales person or real estate developer.

DIVISION 3. - TREE COMMISSION 

Sec. 2-266. - Established; appointment of members. 
    There is established a tree commission. The mayor and the city councilmembers who preside over the committee on streets and sanitation and the committee on parks and recreation shall serve as ex-officio members. The mayor shall appoint six additional members from the city. Two shall be appointed for one year; two shall be appointed for two years; and two shall be appointed for three years. Following the initial appointment, two members shall be appointed annually to serve for three years. Members shall serve until their successors are appointed. 
(Code 1974, § 2-225) 
Sec. 2-267. - Meetings. 
    The tree commission shall provide in its minutes for regular periodic meetings. Meetings may also be called by the mayor, by either of the two councilmembers or by any three of the other members, after giving not less than three days' notice of the date, time and place of the special meeting. 
(Code 1974, § 2-226) 
Sec. 2-268. - Duties; recommendations to city council. 
    The tree commission shall: 
(1)  Make recommendations to the mayor and council on the needs of the city in connection with its tree planting program; 
(2)  Recommend the type and kind of trees to be planted upon city streets, parks and other public places within the city; 
(3)  Assist the mayor and council in providing information regarding the protection, maintenance, removal and planting of trees on public property and, where requested by the owner, on private property; 
(4)  Meet with the city planning commission and assist in making a master street plan by recommending the use of species of trees; 
(5)  Recommend to the mayor and council which trees are considered unwanted weed trees and identify and recommend removal of dead, dying, diseased or insect infested trees; and 
(6)  Make studies and report back to the mayor and council with recommendations on matters concerning trees in the city. 
(Code 1974, § 2-227) 
Secs. 2-269-2-290. - Reserved.

ARTICLE VI. - CAPITAL ASSETS 

Sec. 2-321. - Intent. 
    It is the intent of the city council to establish a uniform system of accountability to safeguard the city's considerable investment in capital assets, to demonstrate its stewardship, and to provide assurance to the citizens of the city that the use of public funds entrusted to their government has been fully and properly accounted for. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-322. - Applicability. 
(a)  This policy is applicable to all classes of capital assets. It shall be the responsibility of the mayor, in consultation with the city clerk, to develop procedures necessary to the implementation of this policy statement. 
(b)  Procedures developed to implement this policy shall be binding on all employees of the city and the willful failure to follow those procedures or to carry out the intent of this policy shall constitute grounds for disciplinary action. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-333. - Definitions. 
(a)  The following definitions are applicable to capital assets subject to this policy statement: 
(1)  Land. All real property currently in the possession of the city or acquired in the future and held in fee simple or other conditions of whole or partial ownership, including leasehold interests, shall constitute land holdings for purposes of this policy except as hereinafter exempted. The cost or value of structures and improvements on city land, whether constructed or otherwise acquired, shall be separately accounted for in appropriate categories. 
(2)  Improvements to land. "Improvements to land" shall constitute all nonstructure improvements to land including, but not limited to, such improvements as fencing, sidewalks, access drives, outdoor seating, lighting systems, utility services and similar improvements with individual costs or values in excess of $2,500.00 except as hereinafter exempted. 
(3)  Structures. "Structures" represent buildings and permanently attached fixtures and equipment including, but not limited to, office buildings, meeting halls, maintenance facilities, warehouses and other buildings constructed or acquired by the city with a cost or value in excess of $5,000.00 except as hereinafter exempted. 
(4)  Construction in progress. "Construction in progress" shall mean the cost or added value to date of structures and improvements to land which are incomplete but which are expected to meet the criteria established for the recording of such assets when completed. 
(5)  Tangible personal property. "Tangible personal property" shall mean property consisting of fixtures and other tangible personal property of a nonconsumable nature the value of which is $200.00 or more and the normal expected life of which is one year or more. 
(6)  Intangible personal property. "Intangible personal property" shall, for the purposes of this policy statement, include the cost or value of copyrights, patents and similar items which the city is licensed to use in the pursuit of its public business, which licenses or permissions were acquired at a cost of more than $100.00 and which licenses for periods of more than one year. Intangible personal property, for purposes of this policy statement, shall include computer software licensed to the city, but shall not include depository balances or the claims on financial assets evidenced by financial instruments such as certificates of deposit, notes, bonds, or similar evidences of indebtedness. 
(b)  Exemptions. 
(1)  The following capital assets are specifically exempted from the provisions of this policy statement: 
a.  Land used by the city without charge or at nominal cost but title to which is vested in agencies of the federal, state or county governments. 
b.  Improvements to land commonly classed as "infrastructure assets." Typically, right-of-way, roads, utility easements, docks, statues, park improvements and similar assets are categorized as "infrastructure assets." Generally, the public's access to and enjoyment of such assets is relatively unrestricted, other than for public health and safety considerations. 
c.  Intangible personal property commonly accounted for as current, rather than capital, assets of the city. Examples include financial claims against banks and other depositories, and investments in private or other governmental debt offerings. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-334. - Land. 
(a)  All land, as defined in subsection 2-333(a)(1), shall be cataloged and recorded in the public records of the city at the acquisition cost or estimated historical cost at the date of acquisition. Land donated to city purposes shall be valued at its fair market value at the date of acquisition. 
(b)  The city's public records shall include, at a minimum, the legal description of the property, its acquisition cost or value, the method of acquisition, the date of acquisition (if known), references identifying the location of the deed or other evidence of title supporting the city's claim of ownership or use, appropriate recording references to the public records of Barbour County, Alabama, or other governmental jurisdiction for the public recording of title, the nature of any encumbrances of title and, as appropriate, the date of satisfaction of such encumbrances. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-335. - Improvements to land. 
(a)  Improvements to land, as defined in subsection 2-333(a)(2), shall be cataloged and valued at cost or estimated historical cost at the date of acquisition. Improvements donated to the city shall be valued at fair market value as of the date acquired. Cost shall include, but not be limited to, engineering design, architectural, construction and associated landscaping costs associated with the improvements. 
(b)  The city's public records shall include, at a minimum, a description of the improvements and their locations, the method of acquisition, the cost or value of the improvements, serial numbers for any equipment incorporated into the improvements, the date of acquisition of the improvements and a notation as to their current condition. The public records shall also note any encumbrances against the improvements and, as appropriate, the date the encumbrances were satisfied. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-336. - Structures. 
(a)  Structures, as defined in subsection 2-333(a)(3), shall be cataloged and valued at cost or estimated historical cost at the date of acquisition. Structures donated to the city shall be valued at fair market value as of the date acquired. Cost shall include, but not be limited to, engineering design, architectural, construction and associated equipment and site improvement costs associated with the structures. 
(b)  The city's public records shall include, at a minimum, a description of the structures and their location, method of acquisition, the cost or value of the structures, serial numbers and descriptions for any equipment incorporated into the structures, the date of acquisition of the structures, and a notation as to the structures' current condition. The public records shall also note any encumbrances against the improvements and, as appropriate, the date the encumbrances were satisfied. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-337. - Construction in progress. 
(a)  The city clerk shall keep records, by project, identifying capital assets subject to recording in accordance with this policy statement, in the process of construction. The assets shall, upon completion, be transferred to the appropriate asset categories. 
(b)  The records shall, at a minimum, include descriptions of the assets under construction, appropriate references to construction contracts and related cost records, the date of commencement of the construction, the costs incurred to date including, but not limited to, permitting and inspection costs, architectural and engineering design costs, site improvement costs, construction and permanent equipment costs, date of completion of the construction, the city official or employee accepting the asset on behalf of the city and such other information as the city clerk may deem appropriate. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-338. - Tangible personal property. 
(a)  Tangible personal property, as defined in subsection 2-333(a)(4), shall be recorded at cost, including the amount received as credit for exchanged items or estimated historical cost if actual cost is not determinable. Tangible personal property items donated to the city and items constructed by city personnel shall be valued at their fair market value at the date of acquisition or construction. 
(b)  Each item of tangible personal property, as defined in subsection 2-333(a)(4), which it is practicable to identify by marking shall be marked in the manner required by the procedures promulgated by the mayor in consultation with the city clerk. 
(c)  The city clerk shall maintain adequate records of the city's tangible personal property, which records shall contain such information as shall be required by the mayor as set forth in adopted written procedures. 
(d)  The city clerk shall be responsible for annually inventorying the city's tangible personal property or whenever there is a change in custodians. Each inventory date shall be entered on the property records. The inventory shall be compared with the property records, and all discrepancies shall be traced and resolved. 
(e)  Each city department head shall be primarily responsible for the supervision and control of assigned property but may delegate to a custodian its use and immediate control and may require custody receipts. A department head may assign to or withdraw from a custodian the custody of any of its property at any time; provided, 
that if the custodian is an officer elected by the people, the property may not be withdrawn from his custody without his consent. Each custodian shall be responsible to the department head or mayor, as appropriate, for the safekeeping and proper use of the property entrusted to his care. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-339. - Intangible assets. 
(a)  Intangible assets, as defined in subsection 2-333(a)(5), shall be recorded at cost or estimated historical cost if the actual cost is not determinable. The value of the assets purchased by a governmental type fund shall not be amortized; however, when the use of the intangible asset is discontinued, the value shall be removed from the city's general fixed asset accounting records. 
(b)  Licensed intangible assets shall be used solely for the city's public purposes and the unauthorized use, copying or similar conversion of licensed material to other uses shall be grounds for disciplinary action. 
(c)  The city's public records shall contain, at a minimum, a description of the rights licensed to the city, the name and proprietary owner of any computer software, the acquired, the cost or other value, the locations of use, including the serial numbers of machines in which installed, and the location of the licensing agreement. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-340. - Renovations and repairs. 
(a)  Renovation and repair costs shall not be capitalized unless the affected structures and improvements to land are: 
(1)  Substantially expanded in capacity or the basic construction status of the structure or improvement changes; or, 
(2)  The life of the structure or improvement is substantially extended and 
(3)  The original costs of the structural elements or improvements replaced can be removed from the recorded value of the structures or improvements. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-341. - Property acquisition. 
(a)  It is the intent of the city council that the following procedures will be observed when acquiring capital assets: 
(1)  Land. Purchases of land must be approved by the city council after appropriate review of the proposed acquisition by the city attorney. Land acquisitions, the exchange of city property, or any combination thereof, may be made only after securing an independent appraisal, from a qualified appraiser, of the property to be acquired and, if applicable, the property to be exchanged. 
(2)  Structures and improvements to land. Decisions to acquire structures and other improvements shall, for existing improvements, be based on competent written independent appraisals when the cost exceeds $10,000.00. Acquisitions of existing structures and improvements valued at less than $10,000.00 shall be based on determinations of value compiled by the city engineer or city clerk as appropriate. Procurement of acquisitions to be constructed shall be based on competitive bids to the greatest extent practicable. 
(3)  Tangible personal property. Whenever acquiring tangible personal property, the mayor may pay the purchase price in full or may exchange similar property with the seller as a trade-in and apply the exchange allowance to the cost of the property acquired. If, whenever acquiring property, the mayor may best serve the public interest of the city by outright sale of the property to be replaced, rather than by exchange as a trade-in, he may make the sale in the manner otherwise prescribed in this policy statement for the disposal of property. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-342. - Disposition of property. 
(a)  All dispositions of property belonging to the city, must be approved by the city council. The determination of property to be disposed of by the city council shall be at the election of the city council in the reasonable exercise of its discretion. 
(b)  Authority for the disposal of property shall be recorded in the minutes of the city. The disposal of tangible personal property shall be recorded in the records required by that section. 
(c)  The minimum procedures for disposing of property in the following categories shall be as follows: 
(1)  Land. The city council, in open meeting, may determine that certain land is surplus to the city's needs or should be exchanged for other land in the best interests of the city. Land so identified may be disposed of through competitive bids through public auction to the highest bidder. Land shall be exchanged or disposed of only after securing an independent appraisal from a qualified appraiser. Such appraisal shall become a public record of the city. 
(2)  Other tangible property. The city council shall have discretion to classify as surplus any of its property, which property is not otherwise lawfully disposed of, that is obsolete or the continued use of which is uneconomical or inefficient, or which serves no useful function. 
a.  Within the reasonable exercise of its discretion and having consideration for the best interest of the city, the value and condition of property classified as surplus, and the probability of such property being desired by the prospective bidders to whom offered, the city council first shall offer surplus property to other governmental units in the county. If no acceptable offer is received from a governmental unit, the property may be disposed of by competitive bid or by public auction. Such offer shall disclose the value and condition of the property. 
b.  Property, the value of which the city council estimates to be between $200.00 and $999.99, shall be sold only to the highest responsible bidder after a request for at least three bids, or by public auction. Any sale of property the value of which the city council estimates to be $1,000.00 or more shall be sold only to the highest responsible bidder, or by public auction, after publication of notice not less than one week nor more than two weeks prior to sale in a newspaper having a general circulation in the county and in additional newspapers if, in the judgment of the city council, the best interests of the city will be better served by the additional notices. 
c.  If the property is without commercial value it may be donated, destroyed, or abandoned. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Sec. 2-343. - Accounting principles. 
(a)  It is the intent of city council that the public records of the city's capital assets provide an adequate basis for financial reporting purposes and for identifying insurable city capital assets. 
(b)  To carry out its intent, city council herewith adopts those generally accepted principles promulgated by the Government Accounting Standards Board as the accepted methodology for accounting and reporting on the city's capital assets. These accounting principles are currently defined in the Codification of Governmental Accounting and Financial Reporting Standards as of July, 1992, published by the Governmental Accounting Standards Board. 
(Ord. 1993-8, § 1, 6-21-93) 
Secs. 2-344-2-360. - Reserved.
