Chapter 6 - ADVERTISING[1] 
  

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 22. 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Billposter includes all persons who engage in the business or occupation of posting, by tacking, posting, painting or otherwise, or circulating from house to house or distributing upon the streets any advertising matter, bills, posters, samples, pictures or any other thing, matter or device whatsoever advertising the business of any firm or occupation, whether that of merchant, manufacturer, publisher, or persons engaged in any business or industrial pursuit or of any operas, theaters, shows, circuses or other exhibitions. Nothing in this definition shall be construed to apply to the painting of store, office or other signs by sign painters nor the posting of legal notices by public officers or attorneys in the manner and in the places prescribed by law. This shall not prohibit any resident of this city from distributing his own advertising matter or causing the distribution by any responsible parties. 
(Code 1974, § 3-13) 
Sec. 6-2. - Restrictions on billposters. 
    No billposter, while distributing, shall walk across lawns or gardens or ring door bells. 
(Code 1974, § 3-16) 
Sec. 6-3. - Temporary signs or banners. 
    The erection of temporary signs or banners for advertising purposes over or across any public street, alley or other public property or any part thereof, without permission of the city, is prohibited. 
(Code 1974, § 3-1) 
Sec. 6-4. - Posting on public property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to paint, print or post or in any way affix any picture, bill, banner or advertising matter of any kind upon any post, public utility pole, shade tree, hydrant, curb, sidewalk or any other public structure, building or property or to erect any pole on any public property for such purposes or to cause any of such to be done, unless express consent therefor shall first be obtained from the city council. This shall not apply to the posting of legal or official notices. 
(Code 1974, § 3-14) 
Sec. 6-5. - Unauthorized posting of advertising matter. 
    No person shall paint, post or in any way affix any pictures, bills, signs or advertising matter of any kind upon any post, tree, fence, billboard or signboard or upon any building or erection or structure of any kind within the city or cause such to be done, unless the building, lot or object upon which the advertising matter may be placed is the property or under the control of the person so doing or unless the consent of the owner or the person in control thereof shall be first obtained for advertising purposes. 
(Code 1974, § 3-15) 
Sec. 6-6. - Maintenance of premises near posting. 
    No billposter shall scatter, daub or leave any paste, glue or other like substance used for affixing bills upon any public sidewalk or pavement nor scatter or throw any old bills or waste material removed from billboards on the surface of any public street or alley or on the surface of any private grounds or in the rear of any billboards or signboards. 
(Code 1974, § 3-18) 
Chapter 10 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
  

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 22; health and sanitation, ch. 50; dispensing alcoholic beverages at Lakepoint Resort State Park on Sundays, § 70-27. 
State Law reference- Alcoholic beverage control law, Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3-1 et seq.; alcoholic beverage licensing code, Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3A-1 et seq. 

Sec. 10-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Licensee means any person who holds a license to sell alcoholic beverages. 
    Malt or brewed beverages, wine or liquor, alcoholic beverages or intoxicating beverages and other terms used in this chapter mean the same as in Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3-1 et seq. 
(Code 1974, § 4-1) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 10-2. - Disposition of seized liquor or wine. 
    Whenever any person has been convicted in the municipal court of possession or custody of any liquor or wine contrary to the provisions of this chapter and it appears that the police department has seized such liquor or wine and has the liquor or wine in custody as evidence or otherwise, the municipal court shall enter an order declaring such seized liquor or wine to be contraband and ordering the chief of police to destroy the liquor or wine or to sell the liquor or wine to the state alcoholic beverage control board for account of the city, as the mayor may determine in the light of the quantity and marketability of such liquor or wine. An appeal from any conviction upon which any such order depends shall carry with it an appeal from such order. 
(Code 1974, § 4-29) 
Sec. 10-3. - Drinking in public. 
    Except as may be allowed in an entertainment district created and designated by the city pursuant to the authority of Act No. 2012-438 as it now exists or may hereafter be amended, it shall be unlawful for any person to drink or have in open or unconcealed possession or custody for drinking any liquor, wine, malt beverage or brewed beverage at or in any public place in the city, other than a licensed liquor place or licensed beer place. 
(Code 1974, § 4-30; Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014) 
Sec. 10-4. - Sales to minors. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 28-3A-25(a)(3). 
(Code 1974, § 4-6) 
Sec. 10-5. - Giving liquor to minors. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to give liquor to persons under the age of 21 years. 
(Code 1974, § 4-6) 
Sec. 10-6. - Minimum age for purchase or consumption; employment of underaged persons in licensed establishments; misrepresentation of age by minor. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 28-1-5, 28-3A-25(a)(19). 
(Code 1974, §§ 4-4, 4-5, 4-7(a)) 
Sec. 10-7. - False representation of minors. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person, directly or indirectly, to falsely represent or attempt to falsely represent that a minor person is not a minor or is not under 21 years of age and by means of such false representation to aid or abet or attempt to aid or abet such minor person to buy, receive or otherwise obtain or aid or abet such minor person to buy, receive or otherwise obtain any alcoholic beverage. 
(b)  It shall be considered a false representation under the provisions of this section that a person is not a minor or is not under 21 years of age if the purchaser fails to disclose that the person making the purchase, obtaining or securing such alcoholic beverage is a minor person or has not reached the age of 21 years. 
(Code 1974, § 4-7) 
Sec. 10-8. - Selling, giving or serving to intoxicated person or drunkard. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, give or serve liquor to any visibly intoxicated person or a habitual drunkard. 
(Code 1974, § 4-8) 
Sec. 10-9. - Consumption of malt or brewed beverages on premises of wholesalers or distributors. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to consume malt or brewed beverages sold by a wholesaler, distributor or jobber on the premises of such wholesaler, distributor or jobber. 
(Code 1974, § 4-17) 
Sec. 10-10. - Retail sale of malt or brewed beverages in public areas. 
    It shall be unlawful for any retailer to sell any malt or brewed beverage for consumption on the licensed premises, except in a room or place on the licensed premises at all times accessible to the use and accommodation of the general public. This section shall not be interpreted to prohibit a hotel or club licensee from selling malt or brewed beverages in any room of any such hotel or clubhouse occupied by bona fide registered guests or members entitled to purchase of the malt or brewed beverages. 
(Code 1974, § 4-23) 
Sec. 10-11. - Prostitutes in licensed places. 
    It shall be unlawful for a person in charge or control of any liquor licensed or beer licensed place to knowingly permit to loiter in such place any prostitute. 
(Code 1974, § 4-32) 
Sec. 10-12. - Shows/performances depicting nudity or sexual conduct prohibited in licensed establishments. 
(a)  The following words and terms when used in this section shall, for the purpose of this section, have the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section. 
(1)  Nudity means the showing of the human male or female genitals, pubic area or buttocks with less than a fully opaque covering, or the showing of the female breast with less than a fully opaque covering of any portion thereof below the top of the darkened area surrounding the nipple, or the depiction of covered male genitals in a discernibly turgid state. 
(2)  Sexual conduct means the performance of acts, or simulated acts, of masturbation, homosexuality, sodomy, sexual intercourse, or physical contact with a person's clothed or unclothed genitals, pubic area, buttocks or, if such person be a female, breast. 
(3)  Knowingly means having actual or constructive knowledge of the character and content of the subject matter. A person has constructive knowledge if a reasonable inspection under the circumstances would disclose the nature of the subject matter and the failure to inspect for the purpose of avoiding such disclosure. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any manager, officer, agent, servant, employee, or person in charge of any establishment within the city licensed to sell spirituous or vinous liquors or malt or brewed beverages under the laws of the state, knowingly to exhibit, allow, engage in, participate in, or be connected with, any motion picture, show, performance, or other presentation upon the licensed premises, which, in whole or in part, depicts nudity or sexual conduct. 
(Ord. No. 1994-5, 2-21-94) 
Sec. 10-13. - Sunday sales. 
(a)  Restaurants and hotels properly licensed by the alcoholic beverage control board and the City of Eufaula located within the corporate limits of the City of Eufaula are allowed to sell alcoholic beverages for on-premises consumption between 12:00 p.m. (noon) to 9:30 p.m. on Sundays and on Sundays on which New Year's Eve (December 31) occurs, after 12:00 p.m. 
(b)  The sale of beer and table wine by retailers properly licensed by the alcoholic beverage control board and the City of Eufaula with a retail table wine and/or retail beer license for on-premises and/or off-premises consumption is permitted between 12:00 p.m. (noon) to 9:30 p.m. on Sundays and on Sundays on which New Year's Eve (December 31) occurs, after 12:00 p.m. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for licensees licensed by the alcoholic beverage control board and the City of Eufaula as lounge retail, lounge package stores, or club liquor class I and class II, within the corporate limits of the City of Eufaula to sell alcoholic beverages on Sunday except as already permitted by the Code of Alabama and on Sundays on which New Year's Eve (December 31) occurs sales are permitted after 12:00 p.m. (noon). Nothing herein shall be interpreted as local legislation authorizing Sunday sales at lounge retail, lounge package stores, or club liquor class I and class II, under Alabama Code § 28-3A-25 (19), (20). 
(Ord. No. 2017-7 , 7-3-2017; Ord. No. 2017-13 , 12-18-2017) 
Chapter 10A - ENTERTAINMENT DISTRICT 

Sec. 10A-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms, and phrases when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Alcoholic beverages means any alcoholic, spirituous, vinous, fermented or other alcoholic beverage, or combination of liquors and mixed liquor, a part of which is spirituous, vinous, fermented or otherwise alcoholic, and all drinks or drinkable liquids, preparations or mixtures intended for beverage purposes, which contain one-half of one percent or more of alcohol by volume, and shall include liquor, beer and wine, both fortified and table wine. 
    Approved container means a paper or plastic container not exceeding a volume of 16 fluid ounces, which is provided by a designated licensee and approved by Main Street Eufaula. Inc. that bears the commercially printed name and/or logo of the designated licensee, the event sponsor(s), Main Street Eufaula, Inc., the district or any combination of the above. 
    Board means the alcoholic beverage control board. 
    City means the City of Eufaula. 
    Container means any bottle, can, glass or other receptacle suitable for or used to hold any liquid. 
    District means the downtown entertainment district established by this chapter. 
    Licensee means any person or business within the district which holds a license issued by the board and the city. 
    License means any retail license authorized by Chapter 3A of Title 28, Code of Alabama, which allows the licensee to sell alcoholic beverages for consumption on the licensed premises. 
    Outdoor dining area , unless otherwise defined in a licensee's use agreement with the city, means a licensee's outdoor dining area that is situated on the sidewalk between the licensee's storefront and the street where it fronts. With respect to licensed premises located on a corner, any exterior wall that fronts a public street is considered a storefront. 
    Public place shall mean and include any street, sidewalk, rights-of-way, parking lots, or outdoor public areas located within the district. (Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014; Ord. No. 2015-7 , 12-7-2015) 
Sec. 10A-2. - District description. 
    An entertainment district as provided in Act No. 2012-438 of the Legislature of the State of Alabama is hereby established in downtown Eufaula with the areas and boundaries as set forth and designated on the map which is attached hereto as exhibit I and incorporated herein. 
(Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014) 
Editor's note- Exhibit I has been incorporated herein by reference and a copy is on file and available in the offices of the city. 
Sec. 10A-3. - Rules and regulations. 
    The following regulations shall be in effect in the district: 
(1)  Outside consumption of alcoholic beverages permitted-Conditions . 
a.  Within the district, the Alabama Alcoholic Beverage Control Board may issue an entertainment district designation for any on-premises retail alcohol beverage license which allows the licensee to sell alcohol beverages for consumption on the licensed premises. Patrons may not exit licensed premises with more than one open container of alcoholic beverages. All alcoholic beverages sold for consumption outside the licensed premises shall be contained in a paper or plastic container that bears the commercially printed name and/or logo of the designated licensee, the event sponsor(s), Main Street Eufaula, Inc., the district or any combination of the above. 
b.  No licensee shall allow a person to exit such licensed premises with more than one such open approved container and, and it shall be unlawful for any person to exit such licensed premises with more than one such open approved container. 
c.  During special events. During special events the district or a portion thereof shall be open for public possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages anywhere within the confines of the district or a portion of the district as provided in the permit. Public possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages shall be allowed as provided herein on dates specified on an assembly permit lawfully issued by the city for events approved by Main Street Eufaula, Inc. A request for an assembly permit for events where public possession and consumption of alcohol within the district is to be considered must include all the information required by section 82-73 of the Eufaula Code of Ordinances and be submitted to Eufaula Main Street, Inc. for approval prior to consideration by the city. Eufaula Main Street, Inc. may establish a fee for review and processing applications for permits. Events that include such activities as the sale of alcoholic beverages outside of licensed premises, street closures, entertainment using amplified sound, or other regulated activities must comply with all laws, ordinances or regulations governing such activities. Applications for such assemblies or special events shall be forwarded by the city clerk to the chief of police, the fire chief, city planner or their respective designees for review prior to final approval by the city. 
d.  Outdoor dining areas. The district shall be open for public possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages between the hours of 11:00 a.m. to 11:00 p.m. Monday through Saturday only in a licensee's outdoor dining areas that are situated on a sidewalk or other right-of-way where the licensee has a right-of-way use agreement with the City of Eufaula. 
e.  City-sponsored opening of the district. At any time and from time to time the city may elect to sponsor the opening of all or a portion of the district. 
(2)  Right to enter restricted . During any such special event, patrons or guests of a licensee with an entertainment district designation may exit that licensee's licensed premises with one open container of alcoholic beverage in an approved container and consume such alcoholic beverage anywhere within the confines of the district, but may not enter another licensed premises with an open container of alcoholic beverages acquired elsewhere. 
(3)  All applicable laws in effect . A licensee who is within the district shall comply with all laws, rules and regulations which govern its license type. 
(4)  Size limited to 16 ounces . No container in which an alcoholic beverage is dispensed and removed from the licensed premises shall exceed 16 fluid ounces in size. No person shall be in possession of any above prescribed alcoholic beverage container which exceeds 16 fluid ounces in size on the streets and sidewalks, in parks, or in other public places within the defined district. 
(5)  Drinking from can, bottle, or glass is prohibited . It shall be unlawful for any person within the confines of the district to drink or attempt to drink any alcoholic beverage from a can, bottle, or glass or to possess in an open can, bottle, or glass any alcoholic beverage on the streets, sidewalks, rights-of-way, and parking lots, whether public or private; other than as duly licensed by the State of Alabama and the city. It shall also be unlawful for any person within the confines of the district to drink or attempt to drink any alcoholic beverage on the streets, sidewalks, rights-of-way, and parking lots, whether public or private from a container other than an approved container. 
(6)  Open container laws applicable . Open container laws of the State of Alabama and the City of Eufaula still govern to the extent that the respective provisions are not strictly modified by either section 28-3A-17.1 of the Code of Alabama 1975, section 28-3A-20.1 of the Code of Alabama 1975 or the provisions of this chapter. 
(7)  Hours for special events . Special events permitted within the district shall only be allowed between the hours of 11:00 a.m. to 11:00 p.m. Monday through Saturday. 
(8)  Consumption of alcoholic beverages in a motor vehicle prohibited . It shall be unlawful for any person to consume any alcoholic beverages in a motor vehicle parked or in motion within the district, with the exception of a common carrier vehicle licensed by the board to serve alcoholic beverages. 
(9)  Refill prohibited . It shall be unlawful for any person to refill a container from a licensed premises with alcoholic beverages not purchased at a licensed premises within the district. It shall be unlawful for any person to re-use or to knowingly allow the re-use of an approved container for an alcoholic beverage and nothing in this chapter shall be construed to authorize the same. 
(10)  Alcoholic beverage from another licensed premises prohibited . It shall be unlawful for any person to enter a licensed premises with alcoholic beverages acquired at another licensed premises or outside the district. 
(11)  Under-age drinking prohibited . Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to authorize any person to violate the state and city's laws against under-age drinking. 
(12)  Churches and excluded areas . No church shall be considered part of the district. Any public building, facility, garage, or parking lot that is posted with signage at each entrance or in conspicuous places that no open containers of alcoholic beverages are allowed on the premises shall be excluded from the district. Property privately owned or controlled that is posted with signage at each entrance or in conspicuous places that no open containers of alcoholic beverages are allowed on the premises shall also be excluded. 
(Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014; Ord. No. 2015-7 , 12-7-2015) 
Sec. 10A-4. - Violations. 
    Any violation of any provision of chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable by a fine of not less than $100.00 nor more than $1,000.00 per violation. To which, at the discretion of the court or judge trying the case, may add imprisonment or a sentence to hard labor for not more than three months or may be punished by both such fine and imprisonment. The city council may also consider suspension or revocation of the business license of any licensee who violates any provision of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014) 
Sec. 10A-5. - Signage. 
    Boundary maps of the district with the hours of operation of the district shall be clearly marked with fixed signage at all entrances/exits of licensed premises within the district. Signs shall indicate the prohibition of removing beverages from the district. The boundary of the district shall be clearly marked with signs for pedestrians entering the district during special events displaying the hours of operation and indicating the prohibition on removing alcoholic beverages from the area. 
(Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014) 
Sec. 10A-6. - Temporary closure of the district. 
    At any time and from time to time, the chief of police or his designee shall have the authority to temporarily close the district, or portions of the district, which includes authority to require individuals to disperse from the area, should he, in his sole discretion, determine it is appropriate to do so in order to protect the public health, safety, or general welfare. The district shall remain closed until the chief of police or his designee allows the district to be re-opened. The city shall not be responsible for any costs incurred by any person or business as a result of the closing. 
(Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014) 
Sec. 10A-7. - Amendments. 
    The city council may amend, modify or revoke the designation of any area as an entertainment district upon finding that the operation of the district has become a nuisance or is otherwise not being operated in the best public interest, including lack of adequate security. The city council may also require that the licensees located within the district provide additional security at their own expense. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to create any right or entitlement to entertainment district designation. 
(Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014) 
Sec. 10A-8. - Severability. 
    The provisions of this chapter are severable. If any part of this chapter is declared invalid or unconstitutional, that declaration shall not affect the part which remains. 
(Ord. No. 2014-9 , § I, 8-11-2014) 
Chapter 14 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Health and sanitation, ch. 14. 
State Law reference- Animals generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-1-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 14-1. - Right of entry for enforcement. 
(a)  The animal control officer and persons authorized by him as assistants and all law enforcement officers shall have the right for the public health, welfare and safety to enter upon any property within the city for the purpose of: 
(1)  Capturing any animal running at large; 
(2)  Capturing any animal upon written complaint that such animal has bitten a human being; or 
(3)  Capturing any rabid animal. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to hinder, molest or interfere with any such officer who is authorized or empowered to perform any duty under this chapter. 
(Code 1974, § 6-1.1) 
Sec. 14-2. - Destruction of injured animals. 
    An owner's request that such owner's injured animal be destroyed by the animal control officer shall be in writing. The animal control officer is authorized to destroy badly injured animals when it would be inhumane not to do so. 
(Code 1974, § 6-1.2) 
Sec. 14-3. - Bird sanctuary. 
(a)  The entire area embraced within the corporate limits of the city is designated as a bird sanctuary. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to trap, shoot, hunt or attempt to shoot or molest in any manner any wild bird or wild fowl or to rob wild bird nests or wild fowl nests. However, if starlings or similar birds are found to be congregating in such numbers in a particular locality that they constitute a nuisance or menace to health or property in the opinion of the health authorities of the city, such health authorities shall meet with the representatives of the Audubon Society, garden club or humane society or as many of such clubs as are found to exist in the city, after having given at least three days' actual notice of the time and place of such meeting to the representatives of such clubs. 
(c)  If, as a result of such meeting, no satisfactory alternative is found to abate such nuisance, such birds may be destroyed in such numbers and in such manner as is deemed advisable by such health authorities under the supervision of the chief of police. 
(d)  This section does not prohibit lawful hunting. 
(Code 1974, §§ 6-10, 6-11) 
Sec. 14-4. - Killing or injuring animal of another. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-1-10. 
(Code 1974, § 6-42) 
Sec. 14-5. - Animal fights. 
    Any person who fights or causes to fight any dog or other animal or chicken or other fowl or who bets money or other thing of value on the result of such fight shall, on conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 6-5) 
State Law reference- Fighting of dogs, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-1-29. 
Sec. 14-6. - Keeping wild or vicious animals. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the owner or other person in charge thereof to harbor or keep in the city a wild or vicious animal unless the animal is securely confined or bound in such a manner as to prevent such animal from biting or attacking a person or another animal. 
(b)  It shall be prima facie evidence that an animal is a vicious animal if it shall bite or fiercely attack any person whatever or any other animal, when such person or other animal at the time of such biting or attack is not on the owner's premises. 
(Code 1974, §§ 6-2, 6-63) 
State Law reference- Liability for permitting vicious animal to be at large, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-1-3. 
Sec. 14-7. - Noise. 
    It shall be unlawful to confine, harbor or keep on a lot, place or premises any animal or fowl which habitually, continuously or intermittently makes or emits sounds or noises of such volume, nature and extent as to be a public nuisance by reason of being obnoxious or annoying to the ordinary persons in that neighborhood. 
(Code 1974, § 6-3) 
Sec. 14-8. - Poultry running at large. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or allow chickens, ducks, geese, turkeys, guineas or pigeons, except homing pigeons, to run or fly at large inside the corporate limits of the city. In this section "at large" means off the premises of the owner or keeper and not under such person's effective control. 
(Code 1974, § 6-8) 
Sec. 14-9. - Sale of animals in public places prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to sell, offer for sale, barter, or give away, any animal along a public right-of-way or in a public place. Any person convicted of violating the provisions of this section shall be penalized in accordance with section 14-95. This section shall not apply to legally organize humane societies or governmental entities. 
(Ord. No. 1996-7, 5-6-96; Ord. No. 2003-10, 4-21-03) 
Secs. 14-10-14-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LIVESTOCK 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 14-36. - Running at large. 
    It shall be unlawful for the owner or other person in charge of any horse, mare, jack, mule, hog, sheep, goat, bull, cow or other such livestock to cause, permit or allow any such animal to be at large. In this section "at large" means off the premises of the owner or keeper and not under such person's effective control. 
(Code 1974, § 6-89) 
State Law reference- Estrays and livestock running at large, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-2-1 et seq.; stock laws, Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-5-1 et seq. 
Sec. 14-37. - Pound established; impoundment. 
(a)  A public pound for the impounding of stock running at large is established. The animal control officer, under the supervision of the police chief, shall be the keeper of the pound and shall be responsible for the proper care and control of all impounded animals. 
(b)  All stock found running at large shall be taken up and impounded in accordance with the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 3-5-1 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 1990-19, § 6-1, 12-3-90) 
Secs. 14-38-14-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ENCLOSURES 

Sec. 14-51. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Animal means any animal of the equine, bovine, sheep or swine species or type. 
    Corral means any uncovered, enclosed parcel of land where animals are kept. 
    Keeping means harboring or confining. 
    Stable means any building, structure or shed in which animals are kept. 
(Code 1974, § 6-22) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 14-52. - Floor and drainage of stables, buildings or sheds. 
    It shall be unlawful to keep any animal in any stable, building, structure or shed unless such stable, building, structure or shed is provided with at least a four-inch floor of concrete or other impervious material constructed to be easily flushed with water and to readily drain to suitable outlets connected to a sanitary sewer or to a septic tank or concrete gutter trough trapped by a sanitary sump when the nearest sanitary sewer is greater than 200 feet distant from such enclosure. 
(Code 1974, § 6-23) 
Sec. 14-53. - Distance from dwellings, schools or public places. 
(a)  Corrals. It shall be unlawful to keep any animal of the equine or bovine species or type in any corral in the city, any part of which is within 100 feet of a dwelling, school, church, hospital, public building, public park, public playground or public thoroughfare. 
(b)  Stables or other buildings. It shall be unlawful to keep any animal of the equine or bovine species or type in any stable, building, structure or shed in the city, any part of which is within 30 feet of a dwelling, school, church, hospital, public building, public park, public playground or public thoroughfare. 
(c)  Pigpens and sheep pens. It shall be unlawful to keep, harbor or confine any swine or sheep in any building, structure, shed, corral, pen or enclosure, any part of which is within 300 yards of a dwelling, school, church, hospital, public building, public park, public playground or public thoroughfare. 
(d)  Fowl pens. It shall be unlawful to keep, harbor or confine any duck, goose, chicken, guinea, peacock or other fowl in any stable, building, structure, corral, pen or enclosure in the city, any part of which is within 30 feet of a dwelling, church, hospital, school, public building, public park or public thoroughfare. There shall be provided for each fowl an area, pen or enclosure having a minimum of 15 square feet of space for each fowl so confined or kept on any premises. 
(Code 1974, §§ 6-9, 6-27-6-29) 
Sec. 14-54. - Minimum area of corrals. 
    It shall be unlawful to keep any animal in any corral unless such corral shall have a minimum area of 2,500 square feet for one such animal and 1,000 square feet for each additional animal there kept, to every portion of which such animal shall have free and unrestricted access. 
(Code 1974, § 6-24) 
Sec. 14-55. - Maintenance of premises. 
    All places and premises in the city where horses, mules, cattle, hogs, dogs or other animals or fowl are kept, harbored or confined shall be kept clean, sanitary and free of obnoxious odors and shall be maintained in such a manner as will effectually prevent the reproduction or propagation in or about such places or premises of flies. The presence on or about such places or premises of the live larvae of flies under conditions which permit or favor growth or development shall be prima facie evidence of the reproduction or propagation of flies and of the keeping or maintaining of such places or premises used for such purposes in violation of the provisions of this section. 
(Code 1974, § 6-4) 
Sec. 14-56. - Cleaning floors and appliances in stables or other buildings. 
    The base or floor of every stable or other building in which any animal is kept, together with the sanitary sump and all appliances used in connection therewith, shall be cleaned at least once each day by the removal of manure and other material soiled by manure and by washing. The water supply used for flushing and washing as provided in this section must be of sufficient pressure and in sufficient quantities to properly and adequately flush and wash the troughs and floors daily. 
(Code 1974, § 6-25) 
Sec. 14-57. - Disposal of manure. 
    All accumulations of manure and material soiled by excreta in and about every stable, corral or pen where any animal is kept shall be collected at least once each day and immediately deposited in substantial flyproof containers. All such collections may be kept stored in substantial flyproof containers for a continuous period of two weeks from date of collection. Sawdust, shavings, straw and other material used as animal bedding and unsoiled by excreta shall be collected at least once each week and deposited and stored as provided in this section. In lieu of storage, manure and other material, when collected in accordance with the provisions of this section, being free of live fly larvae, may be disposed of within 24 hours from time of collection by burial at least six inches underground or by spreading the manure and other material thinly upon the surface of the ground at some place distant from human habitation or any place where animals are kept, so that the collections shall be and remain fully exposed to sunshine. 
(Code 1974, § 6-26) 
Secs. 14-58-14-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DOGS AND RABIES CONTROL[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 1993-17, § 1, adopted Oct. 18, 1993, amended art. III in its entirety to read as herein set out. Former art. III, §§ 14-81-14-92, pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Code 1974, §§ 6-54-6-62, §§ 6-75-6-77, and Ord. No. 1993-4, adopted March 1, 1993. 

Sec. 14-81. - Heading. 
    This article shall be known as the city animal control ordinance and shall be applicable within all zones 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 2001-4, § I, 7-2-01) 
Sec. 14-82. - Definitions. 
    For the purposes of this article, the following words and phrases shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section unless the context otherwise requires: 
    Animal means dogs and cats. 
    Animal control officer means any agent designated by the mayor or, if so delegated by the mayor, the city chief of police to enforce this article. 
    Animal shelter means any facility maintained by the city and any facility maintained by a non-profit humane organization or municipal agency as approved by the city council for the confinement, care, control or disposition of animals that come into its custody. 
    ACO means any agent designated by the mayor or, if so delegated by the mayor, the city chief of police to enforce this article. 
    Cat means the domestic cat, felis catus. 
    Dangerous animal means any animal which represents to a reasonable person physical danger to any person or any other animal and includes but is not limited to the following: 
(1)  Any animal which, without provocation, shall bite any person who is lawfully on the premises where such animal is kept; 
(2)  Any animal which, without provocation, shall bite any person engaged in a lawful activity; 
(3)  Any animal that on two or more occasions, without provocation approaches within 20 feet of any person engaged in a lawful activity in such a manner as a reasonable person would under the circumstances deem to be vicious or terrorizing and perceived by such person as likely to attack him whether or not the attack is consummated. 
The definition of "dangerous animal" shall not include any animal wherever located which acted aggressively if the actual or intended victim has intentionally provoked the aggressive behavior of the animal or if the intended victim is in the pursuit of an unlawful activity. 
    Division means the animal control division of the city police department. 
    Dog means the domestic dog, canis familiaris. 
    Owner means any person, partnership or corporation owning, keeping, maintaining, harboring or having custody of one or more animals. This definition shall not include veterinarians or the any agent designated by the mayor or, if so delegated by the mayor, the city chief of police to enforce this article when keeping animals at their place of business or at the pound. 
    Physical control means the immediate, continuous physical control of an animal at all times such as by means of a leash, or appropriate tether of such strength to restrain the same; or in the case of trained or obedient dogs, "physical control" shall also include visual signals or voice commands by the owner of a dog which responds to such signals or commands, if such dog is at all times in the immediate presence of and under the voice control of the owner or handler. Immediate presence, for the purpose of this article, shall be defined as a radius of 50 feet from the owner. 
    Running at large means any animal which is not controlled by any adequate leash or tether, or otherwise under the owner's physical control, as defined in this section, while the animal is off the owner's premises. No animal shall be deemed "running at large" when such animal is upon the property of the owner or upon property which the owner has permission for the dog to be on. Any words not specifically defined herein shall have their usual and common meanings. 
    A dog shall not be deemed to be "running at large" if any of the following apply: 
1.  The dog is confined in a building or fenced pen or yard on its owner's property or on the property of another person with the other person's consent. 
2.  The dog is leashed and securely tied on its owner's property or on the property of another person with the other owner's consent, in such position that the dog cannot gain access to public property or other private property. 
3.  The dog, whether on leash or not, is under the immediate and effective control of a responsible person; provided that the dog shall not be considered under restraint if it is on the property of a person other than its owner, without the consent of the other person. 
4.  The dog, though not meeting any of the conditions stated in 1, 2, and 3 above, is in a peaceful attitude on the property of its owner, and is wearing license and vaccination tags as prescribed in section 14-83 below; provided that the dog shall not be considered under restraint in this case if the dog was chased to its owner's property by the animal control officer or other agent of the city, or if the dog is the subject of an outstanding written complaint duly filed with the police division and/or municipal court. The dog shall not be considered under restraint for purposes of this section during "sweep periods" as described in section 14-82(5) and 14-84(c). 
5.  "Sweep periods" are periods designated by the chief of police, or the chief's designee, with prior notification being given to the mayor and city council during which all dogs must be kept leased when not in a private building, fenced in run, or fenced yard. These periods shall be instituted as necessary to ensure that all stray dogs may more easily be apprehended. "Sweep periods" shall not be longer than seven days in duration and shall not be of greater frequency than four times in any calendar year. Any dog apprehended during "sweep periods" not under leash restraint or in a private building, fenced run or fenced yard shall be subject to the provisions of section 14-95 of this article. 
    Tethering or chaining . These terms are commonly defined as fastening a dog to a stationary object or stake with a chain, rope or other such device that is attached to the dog's collar. This is often used as the sole means of keeping the animal restrained and under control. It does not refer to the periods when an animal is being walked on a leash. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 2001-4, § II, 7-2-01; Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-82A. - Tethering and chaining. 
(a)  Dogs and small animals are prohibited from being tethered or chained to a stationary or fixed point. Dogs and small animals are allowed to be confined by a trolley system, provided the owner is on the premises and certain requirements are met. 
(1)  No owner, keeper, harborer or maintainer of a dog may tether, fasten, chain or tie a dog to any permanent or temporary structure; any post attached to the ground or to any weight designed to restrict the dog's freedom of movement to a limited area of space. 
(2)  Dogs and small animals may be restrained by a trolley system or a tether attached to a pulley on a cable run, provided that the owner is on the premises and the following conditions are met: 
a.  Only one dog or small animal may be tethered to each cable run. 
b.  The tether must be attached to a properly fitting collar or harness worn by the dog or small animal, with enough room between the collar and the animal's throat through which two fingers may fit. Choke collars and pinch collars are strictly prohibited for purposes of tethering a dog or small animal to a cable run. The use of any collar too small for the size and age of the animal, or by any rope, chain or cord directly attached to the animal's neck is prohibited. 
c.  There must be a swivel on both ends of the tether to minimize tangling of the tether. 
d.  The tether and cable run must be of adequate size and strength to effectively restrain the dog or small animal. The size and weight of the tether must not be excessive, as determined by the enforcement officer, considering the age, size and health of the dog. In general, the use of a tether that exceeds 25 percent of the body weight of the dog or small animal is prohibited. 
e.  The cable run must be at least 15 feet in length and mounted at least four feet and no more than seven feet above ground level. 
f.  The length of the tether from the cable run to the animal's collar should allow access to the maximum available exercise area and should allow continuous access to food, water and shelter. 
g.  In no case shall it be permitted that a dog or small animal be confined so as to be forced to stand, sit or lie in its own excrement or on ground that is not well drained. 
h.  The trolley system must be of appropriate configuration to confine the dog or small animal to the owner's property, to prevent the tether from extending over an object or an edge that could result in injury or strangulation of the dog or small animal, and to prevent the tether from becoming entangled with other objects or animals. 
i.  Dogs and small animals shall not be confined through the use of a trolley system between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. 
j.  Unsterilized female dogs shall not be tethered attached to a trolley or cable run unless monitored by a competent adult for the duration of such tethering. 
k.  Dogs and small animals should never be tethered during natural disasters such as floods, fires, tornadoes, blizzards, or other severe weather. 
(Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-83. - Rabies vaccinations; rabies vaccination tag required. 
(a)  Every person who owns, harbors, or keeps or maintains a dog or cat over the age of four (4) months shall secure on an annual basis a rabies vaccination for such animal, including the proper certificate and tag from a licensed veterinarian as long as the dog or cat is within the city. 
(b)  Each dog over the age of four months shall wear a substantial durable collar or harness, to which the vaccination tag shall be attached, provided however, that this requirement is exempted while such dog is confined to the property of the owner and provided further the owner shall be required to produce evidence of a rabies vaccination tag upon request of the ACO. It shall be unlawful to attach such tag by wire, rope or by any inhumane means. No person shall remove the collar or vaccination tag from any animal without the consent of the owner. It shall be a defense to any prosecution under this section for any dog owner to produce a written letter from a veterinarian stating that due to the size and shape of any properly vaccinated dog, a collar or harness will not stay on the particular dog without running the risk of undue injury to the dog or if it can be shown that such dog routinely wears a collar but the owner is unaware that the collar is off of the dog. 
(c)  Cats are not required to wear the rabies vaccination tag. If the rabies vaccination tag is not worn, the owner shall be required to produce evidence of the rabies vaccination tag upon request of the ACO. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or allow any dog or cat in his charge or control to wear a rabies vaccination tag issued for a different animal. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 1995-12, § 1, 8-21-95; Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-84. - Animals at large. 
(a)  Constant physical control required. A dog owner shall keep his or her dog under "physical control" at all times. Any dog that is not under "physical control" shall be considered an "animal at large". 
(b)  Special requirements for designated areas. Including both sides of the street; the area bounded on the north by Browder Street and Highland Avenue, on the south by Barbour Street, on the west by Colby Avenue, and on the east by North Randolph Avenue, all the Central Business District and Old Creek Town. A dog owner shall keep his or her dog leashed whenever the dog is in these designated areas. 
(c)  Special requirements during sweep periods. The city council may, by duly adopted resolution, designate a "sweep period" for the apprehension of stray dogs. These periods shall not leave longer than seven days duration and shall not be of greater frequency than four times in any calendar year. 
(d)  Violation of this article. On the first incident, the ACO may return the dog to its owner, if ownership is known, and issue a warning or a citation to the owner in violation of this article. A citation shall be issued for subsequent violations. Penalties for violation of this article are prescribed in section 14-95. 
(e)  [Applicability.] This section shall not apply to police dogs when such dogs are engaged by a law enforcement agency in an official capacity. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 2001-4, § III, 7-2-01) 
Sec. 14-85. - Problem animals. 
(a)  Without regard to other provisions of this article or other sections of this Code, it shall be unlawful for owners of dogs and cats to allow, permit or by negligence fail to prevent such animals from acting or performing in such a manner as to cause damage or unsanitary conditions to the property of another, without the property owners' permission, public streets, public parks and recreation areas, or otherwise to cause a problem in the city. Acts deemed to be problems shall include, but are not limited to, the following: 
(1)  Any dog or cat entering any place where food is stored, prepared, served, or sold to the public except seeing-eye dogs while in the company of a blind person. 
(2)  Any dog while off its owner's property or off of property which the owner has permission for the dog to be on chases, runs after, or jumps at pedestrians or vehicles moving on public streets, sidewalks, public ways, and alleys. 
(3)  Any dog or cat urinating or defecating or defacing or digging up property not owned by the dog or cat's owner. 
(4)  Any dog frequently howling, yelping, whining, or barking in such manner as to unreasonably disturb any person or neighborhood. 
(5)  Any dog or cat feeding from, turning over, or otherwise disturbing garbage containers not on its owner's property. 
(6)  Any dog snapping, growling, snarling, jumping upon, or otherwise threatening persons lawfully using public sidewalks, streets, alleys, or public ways. The snapping, growling, snarling provisions shall not apply to dogs that are securely fenced in on the owner's property so that a reasonable person passing by would not perceive such conduct as an immediate threat to his safety or well being. 
(b)  A person who is offended by a "problem animal" shall call the ACO and report such offending animal. The ACO shall, upon receiving a complaint of a problem animal, investigate the report and if same is well founded, notify the animal owner of the complaint and request voluntary compliance of this article and report back to the person making the complaint. If requested by the complaining party, the ACO shall not divulge the name of the complaining party to the animal's owner. 
(c)  Any owner who has custody of or owns an animal whose conduct would be classified as a problem under this section and who has previously been notified by the ACO that his dog is a problem dog shall be dealt with in the same manner as provided for a violation of subsection 14-84(a). Any problem dog found running at large whose owner cannot be reasonably ascertained shall be taken directly to the pound. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93) 
Sec. 14-85A. - Odor from dogs. 
    It shall be unlawful and a nuisance for any person to keep on any tract, lot, or premises within the city any dog or group of dogs, whether the same is housed in a fence, pen, kennel, building, or otherwise, under such circumstances that the odor from such keeping interferes with the reasonable use and enjoyment of adjacent or neighboring premises. 
(Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-85B. - Duty of owner for removal of feces. 
    It shall be the duty of the owner or person-in-charge of any dog to immediately remove and properly dispose of any feces deposited by said dog upon the grounds of any property within the city except for private property owned or controlled by the owner or person-in-charge of any such dog. 
(Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-85C. - Confinement of female dogs in heat. 
    The owner shall keep leashed any female dog in heat or confine the dog within a building, in such manner that the dog will not attract male dogs and will not be accessible to other dogs except for planned breeding. 
(Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-85D. - Dogs causing damage. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to own or harbor a dog that habitually trespasses on the property of persons other than the owner or person harboring the dog, and causes damage thereto. 
(Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-85E. - Owner liable for damages. 
    If the owner of a dog carelessly manages the dog or permits it to go at large, and another person, without fault on such other person's part, suffers damage thereby, such owner shall be liable for such damages. 
(Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-85F. - Dog owner's duty to remove overturned or scattered garbage. 
    It shall be the duty of the owner of any dog which has been allowed or suffered by such person to run at large, to pick up and remove to a secure authorized container any garbage or refuse which such dog has caused to be overturned, spilled, or scattered upon any public or private property, or upon any right-of-way adjacent thereto, upon demand from the owner or occupant thereof, or upon demand of an animal control officer, and it shall be unlawful for any such person to fail or refuse to do so; provided, however, that no prosecution shall be commenced, and no arrest made pursuant to this section except upon affidavit made before and warrant issued by a duly appointed municipal judge or magistrate of the city. 
(Ord. No. 2017-1 , 3-20-2017) 
Sec. 14-86. - Classification of dangerous animals. 
(a)  When any person claims that an animal is "dangerous" as defined under section 14-82, he shall make a sworn statement before a sworn police officer of the city. Such statement shall specify the address or location of the alleged violation, the nature, time and date of the incident or acts, the name and address of the owner, if known, and a description of the animal, if known. Such statement shall be transmitted to the ACO. Upon receipt of such statement, the ACO shall immediately make an investigation, which such investigation must include an interview with the animal's owner if the owner can be located. The ACO is also authorized to initiate investigation for violations under this section arising under other circumstances. 
(b)  Upon a determination by the ACO that an animal is dangerous, the ACO shall make a summary of findings which shall be incorporated in writing in a classification document. The classification document shall order the owner to confine the animal in a substantial enclosure, or to securely muzzle the animal and otherwise contain it in a reasonable manner as specified by the ACO. 
(1)  The classification document shall be served upon the owner of the animal together with a copy of the procedure for appealing the classification. Service can be accomplished by hand delivery or by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(2)  The owner of any animal which is classified as "dangerous" may appeal the classification or any of its provisions to an appeals committee comprised of the police chief, the ACO, and a licensed veterinarian designated by the mayor, by notifying the chief in writing within 20 days of having been served such classification. The ACO shall within 20 days of receipt of such appeal, notify the owner of the time and place of a hearing before the committee. After conducting a hearing the committee shall take one of the following actions: uphold, modify, or revoke the classification. The decision shall be made in writing and a copy of the decision shall be mailed or personally delivered to the owner of the animal. 
(3)  Any appeal of this decision must be made by written appeal within ten days of the date of such decision to the city council who shall hold a hearing at a designated time to decide whether to uphold, modify or revoke the classification. The owner shall have the right to appear in person with or without legal counsel, and to put on any witnesses in defense to such classification. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93) 
Sec. 14-87. - Dangerous animals. 
(a)  Violation. It shall be a violation of this article for any person to own, keep, maintain, harbor, or have custody of in the city any animal which the ACO or, upon appeal, the hearing committees or the city council, has classified dangerous, as defined under this section, unless such animal is securely muzzled or under restraint of a person by such means as specified in the classification document. 
(b)  Notification. All owners of animals classified dangerous shall immediately notify the ACO when such animal is loose or unconfined; has bitten a human being or attacked another animal; was sold; given away; died or moved to another address. 
(1)  Prior to a dangerous animal being sold or given away, the present owner shall provide the name, address, and phone number of the new owner to the ACO. The new owner shall execute a document to be supplied by the ACO acknowledging that such owner shall comply with the requirements of this article. 
(2)  As a condition to each animal's classification, each owner of a dangerous animal shall allow the ACO to enter and inspect the owner's premises to determine compliance with the classification document and this section. 
(c)  Subsequent violation by an animal classified as dangerous. 
(1)  Upon the written, sworn affidavit of any person or upon a written finding of the ACO setting forth that an animal previously classified as dangerous has actually bitten another animal or a person, while in violation of the provisions of the classification document, the ACO may impound and subsequently destroy such animal whether such animal shall then be at large or in its owner's custody. 
(2)  Prior to the actual impoundment of any dog securely confined to an owner's property and prior to any destruction of any animal classified as dangerous under this article, the ACO shall seek from the circuit court of Barbour County, Alabama, a court order permitting the destruction of the animal. The complaint shall be an In Rem proceeding, with notice given to the dog's owner at least seven days prior to the date set for the hearing. The owner can appear at the hearing to produce evidence to show why such dog should not be destroyed. Appeal from the court order shall be as other appeals from the circuit court. The requirement to obtain a court order can be waived in writing by the owner, thus allowing the immediate destruction of the dog. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93) 
Sec. 14-88. - Cruelty to animals. 
(a)  Whoever: 
(1)  Impounds or confines any animal in any place and fails to supply the animal during such confinement with a sufficient quantity of good and wholesome food and water; 
(2)  Keeps any animal in any enclosure without wholesome exercise and change of air; 
(3)  Abandons to die any animal that is maimed, sick, infirmed, or diseased 
shall be in violation of this section. 
(b)  A person who unnecessarily overloads, overdrives, tortures, torments, deprives of necessary sustenance or shelter or unnecessarily or cruelly beats, mutilates, or kills any animal or causes the same to be done, or carries in or upon any vehicle, or otherwise, any animal in a cruel or inhumane manner, shall be in violation of this section. 
(c)  Whoever exposes, deposits, or puts out upon his or her own premises, or upon the premises of another, or upon property owned by the city, or any other governmental unit or agency, or upon any street, alley, lane, highway and thoroughfare of any kind, any substance known to be poisonous to animals, which is poured over, wrapped in, or otherwise combined with food, with the intent of enticing such animals to eat such poisonous substance and become poisoned thereby, shall be in violation of this section. Intent to poison shall be presumed as a matter of law where poison is found mixed with any type of food. The finding of such poisonous substance or poisoned food, together with the proof as to the identity of the person exposing, depositing, or putting out same, shall be prima facie evidence of the intent to poison and destroy such animals. This section shall not apply where insect or rodent poison is used on a person's own premise for control of insects, mice or rodents in accordance with the manufacturer's instructions. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93) 
Sec. 14-89. - Abandonment of animals. 
(a)  Any person who is the owner or possessor or has charge or custody, of any animal or who abandons any animal in a street, road, or public place without providing for the care, sustenance, protection and shelter of such animal shall be in violation of this section. 
(b)  Upon an affidavit of any person or a law enforcement officer stating an animal appears to have been abandoned, the ACO will investigate the matter and thereupon is authorized to impound and dispose of the animal in the manner provided by this article, with the assistance of a law enforcement officer if necessary. The ACO shall cause written notice, bearing the address where the animal may be claimed by the owner thereof and the time by which the animal must be claimed, to be sent to the owner, if known, at the last known address. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93) 
Sec. 14-90. - Animals in vehicles. 
(a)  No vehicle owner, passenger, or operator shall place or confine an animal or allow it to be placed or confined or to remain in an unattended motor vehicle without sufficient ventilation or under conditions or for such a period of time as may reasonably be expected to endanger the health or well-being of such animal due to heat, lack of water or such other circumstances as may be expected to cause suffering, disability or death. 
(b)  No operator of a motor vehicle shall allow an animal to be unattended while in the vehicle unless the animal is securely restrained so that a reasonable person passing by would not perceive such animal as an immediate threat to his safety or well-being. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93) 
Sec. 14-91. - Impoundment. 
(a)  Animals of the following classes may be captured and impounded immediately wherever located within the areas of the city subject to this article: 
(1)  Subject to the restrictions contained in subsection 14-87(c)(2), dangerous animals of all kinds; 
(2)  Any dog or cat whose owner cannot produce evidence of the rabies vaccination tag upon request of the ACO; 
(3)  Abandoned animals and animals whose ownership is unknown and are commonly referred to as strays, whether running by itself or in a pack; 
(4)  Any animal running at large in violation of section 14-84; 
(5)  Female dogs and cats in breeding season not confined to the premises of the owners in such manner as to avoid nuisances and to prevent access to other animals; 
(6)  Any animal that is infected or reasonably believed to be infected with a contagious or infectious disease to humans or animals. 
(b)  The ACO and its animal control officers, law enforcement officers and humane officers or state charted nonprofit humane organizations shall, subject to the procedural requirements in this article, have authority to pick up, catch, or procure and impound any animal in violation of this chapter, or any animal infected or believed to be infected with rabies or other contagious or infectious disease to humans or animals, in such a manner as is reasonably necessary to effectuate its capture. Impounded animals shall be confined in a human manner at an animal shelter. 
(c)  An impounded animal with a name plate, current license or rabies tag shall be held for at least five days; without a name plate, current license or rabies tag or collar an impounded animal shall be held for three business days, including the day of impoundment, except that a sick or injured animal which poses a threat to the safety of the personnel responsible for the care of such animal may be euthanized at the discretion of the impounding agency. A reasonable effort shall be made by the ACO to locate the owner of any impounded dog or cat. However, if any impounded dog has a rabies tag on its collar, and the owner cannot be contacted, the ACO shall contact the dog's veterinarian and, with the veterinarian's permission, deliver the animal to him for boarding, with the owner being responsible to the veterinarian for the boarding bill. The depositing of a letter of notification by First Class U.S. Mail shall constitute adequate notification of impoundment. The owner shall also be notified by phone, if reasonably feasible. This section shall not apply to animals surrendered by the owner or an agent of the owner, in which case disposition may be made as provided in this article without notification or a holding period and without obtaining a court order. At the expiration of the holding period, the animal may be disposed of in a manner provided in this chapter. 
(d)  A registry shall be maintained by the impounding agency. The registry shall contain identifying characteristics of each animal impounded along with the location, date and reason of each pickup. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 1994-13, 10-3-94; Ord. No. 1995-12, § 2, 8-21-95) 
Sec. 14-92. - Redemption and disposition of animals. 
    All animals which have been impounded in accordance with the provisions of this article may be disposed of as provided below. Every attempt shall be made by the animal control division to treat animals in the city's care in a humane manner and to strive toward the adoption of animals whenever possible. 
(1)  Within the holding period, animals, except dangerous and vicious animals, may be redeemed by the owner or his agent upon the payment of those fees or costs associated with the impoundment, as established by the city council. The owner entitled to possession of an impounded dog or cat which does not have the required rabies inoculation certificate and tag shall be able to take possession of the animal after presenting proper identification. The city will provide the rabies inoculation whenever possible and the owner will remit the cost of such to the city along with payment of other associated costs for impoundment of the animal. 
(2)  If not redeemed within the holding period, animals may be disposed of by humane euthanasia. 
(3)  Those animals which would otherwise be disposed of by euthanasia may be offered to state chartered nonprofit humane organizations for the purpose of providing adoption of such animals. Fees and costs shall be waived for the disposition of animals in this manner. All dogs and cats placed with this organization shall be vaccinated before the organization offers each animal for adoption. 
(4)  Animals remaining in the pound for ten days which have not been redeemed by their owners, shall be available for private sale or adoption by the animal control officer by after having first given notice of the date such animal is available for sale or adoption. A full description of the animal for sale shall be posted for at least seven days. No animal shall be sold for less than $15.00. Any dog or cat not sold through private sale or adoption may be sold to the Auburn University of Veterinary Medicine for $15.00. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93) 
Sec. 14-93. - Fees and charges; administration. 
    Any cat or dog, except a dangerous dog impounded hereunder, may be reclaimed as herein provided upon payment by the owner of the following fees: 
(1)  Boarding fee charged by the city at the rate of $4.00 for each day of impoundment, plus a ten-dollar impoundment fee or the actual costs of boarding charged by an other state chartered nonprofit organization or veterinarian or kennel designated by the city council. 
(2)  The amount of vaccination fee, if necessary. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 1995-12, § 3, 8-21-95) 
Sec. 14-94. - Enforcement. 
(a)  The mayor shall, through the police department, appoint an ACO to take charge of the animal control division. The ACO shall, along with his assistants, enforce the provisions of this article. The ACO shall have the authority to issue a citation to aid in the enforcement of the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Subject to the limitations and restrictions contained in this article, the ACO, his assistants and members of the police division shall have the right, for the protection of public health, welfare and safety, to enter upon any property within the city for the purpose of capturing and impounding any animal which is in violation of this chapter. 
(c)  Any expense incurred in the handling of any animal under the provisions of this chapter shall be borne by the owner or custodian of such animal if same can be ascertained. 
(d)  It shall be a violation of this section to interfere with any animal control officer while in the lawful performance of his duties or with anyone who may be assisting in the performance of such duties. 
(e)  Any person who willfully refuses to sign and accept a citation issued by a law enforcement officer shall be in violation of this chapter. 
(f)  The city council may contract with any state chartered nonprofit humane organization or veterinarian to carry out all or part of the duties herein. Such organization or individual shall carry out the duties pursuant to the provisions prescribed in this article. Failure to do so shall result in the city council assuming the duties or contracting with another organization or individual to assume the duties. Compensation may be provided in an adequate amount to fulfill the prescribed duties. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 2001-4, § III, 7-2-01) 
Sec. 14-95. - Enforcement of penalties for violation. 
(a)  Enforcement of this chapter shall be by summons and complaint as provided for in section 1-13. 
(b)  Any person convicted of violating any provision of this chapter within a 12-month period shall be guilty of a violation and shall be guilty of a violation and shall be punished as follows: 
(1)  For a first violation, a fine of $20.00 
(2)  For a second violation, a fine of $50.00 
(3)  For a third violation, a fine of $100.00 
(4)  For a fourth or any subsequent violation, a fine in an amount not exceeding $500.00, or imprisonment of not more than six months, or both such fine and imprisonment, at the discretion of the municipal judge trying the case. 
Any person who has been charged with the violation of any provision of this article, except those offenses identified in section 14-87, 14-88, and 14-89, and who desires to waive trial of the question of his guilt or innocence of such alleged offense, may pay the fine prescribed above to the municipal court of the city and the municipal court magistrate is hereby authorized and instructed to receive such amount. Voluntary settlement shall not be permitted to any person who has been twice convicted of the same offense prior to the date of the instant alleged offense, and such person shall be required to stand trial in municipal court. Offenses not settled as provided in this subsection prior to the court appearance date shown on the notice of violation will be disposed of in the same manner as is any other case appearing on the regular municipal court docket. This provision shall be considered as part of the City of Eufaula's extended schedule of fines pursuant to Rule 20(c) ARJA. 
(c)  Any person who is alleged to have committed any of the following offenses listed in this chapter shall be required to stand trial in municipal court: 
Section 14-87-Harboring dangerous animals. 
Section 14-88-Cruelty to animals. 
Section 14-89-Abandonment of animals. 
    Any person convicted of any act listed in this subsection (b) shall be punished by a fine of not more than $500.00 or imprisonment of not more than six months, or both such fine and imprisonment at the discretion of the municipal judge trying the case. 
(d)  In addition to the penalties provided in this section, the city council is hereby authorized to institute any appropriate action or proceeding including suit for injunctive relief in order to abate violations of this chapter. 
(Ord. 1993-17, § 1, 10-18-93; Ord. No. 2001-4, § III, 7-2-01; Ord. No. 2002-5, 4-1-02) 
Sec. 14-96. - Confinement of animals known or suspected to have rabies. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, harbor or maintain on or about any place or premises in the city a dog or other animal which is known to have or reasonably suspected of having rabies, unless such animal is securely confined in such a manner as to effectively prevent contact with or injury to persons or other animals. Any such animal not so confined shall either be destroyed or removed to the city pound or other appropriate place by the chief of police or other person designated for that purpose by the city and there securely confined. 
(Ord. No. 1994-13, 10-3-94) 
Sec. 14-97. - Confinement of animals bitten by suspected animals. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, harbor or maintain on or about any place or premises in the city a dog, cat or any other animal whatsoever which has been or is reasonably suspected to have been bitten or otherwise injured by or in contact with another animal afflicted with or suspected of being afflicted with rabies in such a manner as to permit or favor transmission of such disease, unless such dog, cat or other animal so bitten, injured or in contact shall be securely confined for not less than six months thereafter. 
(Ord. No. 1994-13, 10-3-94) 
Sec. 14-98. - Authority to confine suspect animals; interference; duty to destroy afflicted animals. 
(a)  The animal control officer shall have the right at any time to move or cause to be moved to the city pound or other place designated by him, for observation or examination, any dog, cat or other animal which is reasonably suspected to be afflicted with rabies or which has bitten or otherwise injured a human being in such a manner as would permit or favor the transmission of the virus of rabies, if such animal should be afflicted with rabies, or which has been or is reasonably suspected to have been bitten or injured or in contact with another animal afflicted or reasonably suspected of being afflicted with rabies. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to hinder, obstruct or interfere with the animal control officer or any authorized agent or deputy in the exercise of the authority conferred upon him in this section. 
(c)  It shall be the duty of the animal control officer to destroy or cause to be destroyed any animal found to be afflicted with rabies. 
(Ord. No. 1994-13, 10-3-94) 
Chapter 18 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Fire prevention code, § 42-76 et seq.; flood damage prevention, § 46-26 et seq. 
State Law reference- Building regulations authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-59. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 18-1. - Liability of city. 
    This chapter and the codes adopted by reference in this chapter shall not be construed as imposing upon the city any liability or responsibility for damages to any person injured by any defect in any building or structure or appurtenance connected or attached to such building or structure, nor shall the city or any official or employee thereof be held as assuming any such liability or responsibility by reason of the inspection authorized under this chapter or a certificate of approval issued by the city. 
(Code 1974, §§ 8-17, 8-57, 8-101, 8-114, 8-127) 
Sec. 18-2. - Maintenance of vacant buildings. 
    It shall be the duty of the owner, proprietor or other person in charge or control of a vacant building, house or other structure to keep all openings into such building, house or structure securely closed in such manner as to exclude animals and fowl and the trespass of persons therein and to maintain the building or structure in a sanitary condition. 
(Code 1974, § 8-3) 
[Sec. 18-3. - Appendices.] 
    [The appendices to various codes are on filed in the office of the building department and are adopted by reference and incorporated in this section as fully as if set forth at length in this section.] 
International Building Code-2006 Edition, Appendices B, C, D, E, F, G, H, I, J, K, K1-K13. 
International Fire Code-2006 Edition, Appendices A, B, C, D, E, F, G. 
International Fuel Gas Code-2006 Edition, Appendices A, B, C, D. 
International Mechanical Code-2006 Edition, Appendices A and B. 
International Plumbing Code-2006 Edition, Appendices A, B, C, D, E, F, G. 
International Residential Code-2006 Edition, Appendices A, B, C, D, E, F, G, H, J, K, L, M, N, O, P, Q. 
International Existing Building Code-2006 Edition, Appendices A and B, and Resource A. 
International Property Maintenance Code-2006 Edition, Chapter 8 Referenced Standards. 
International Energy Conservation Code-2006 Edition, Chapter 6 Referenced Standards. 
(Ord. No. 2005-14, § 2, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2008-3, § 2, 3-17-08) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2005-14, § 2, adopted November 21, 2005, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion as § 18-3 was at the discretion of the editor. 
[Sec. 18-4. - Official designated.] 
    Within said codes when reference is made to the duties of certain officials named herein that designated official of the City of Eufaula, the Building Official shall be deemed to be the responsible official in so far as enforcing and interpretation of the provisions of said codes with exception of the International Fire Code. When the International Fire Code refers to a designation official of the City of Eufaula, the Fire Chief or representative appointed by the Fire Chief shall be the responsible official for interpreting and enforcing the provision of the International Fire Code. 
(Ord. No. 2005-14, § 5, 11-21-05) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2005-14, § 5, adopted November 21, 2005, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion as § 18-4 was at the editor's discretion. 
Sec. 18-5. - Construction industry craft training fee. 
    In addition to the local permit fees set forth in Chapter 18, a Construction Industry Craft Training (CICT) Fee, as authorized, established, and required by Alabama Act 2015-308, in the amount of $1.00 per $1,000.00 cost or value of construction shall be paid for all permits issued on non-residential construction effective October 1, 2016. Such state required fees may be adjusted from time to time as required by state law or regulation. 
(Ord. No. 2016-5 , 9-19-2016) 
Secs. 18-6-18-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BUILDING CODE 

Sec. 18-31. - Adopted. 
(a)  The International Building Code, 2006 edition, published by the Southern Building Code Congress International, Inc., and the whole thereof, including all appendixes, of which not less than three copies have been and are now filed in the office of the building department, is adopted by reference and incorporated in this section as fully as if set forth at length in this section. The provisions in such code shall be controlling in the construction, alteration, repair, equipment, use and occupancy, location, maintenance, removal and demolition of every building or structure or any appurtenance connected to or attached to such building or structure within the corporate limits of the city. 
(b)  As soon as practical after the publication of a later edition of the International Building Code, 2006 edition, the city council shall review and adopt the code with such amendments and modifications as it deems practical. 
(Ord. No. 1992-9, § 1, 6-1-92; Ord. No. 2002-3, §§ 1-3, 3-4-02; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 1, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2008-3, § 1, 3-17-08)
