ARTICLE III. - AMUSEMENT DEVICE CODE 

Sec. 18-56. - Adopted; enforcing official designated. 
(a)  The Standard Amusement Device Code, 1985 edition, published by the Southern Building Code Congress International, Inc., is adopted by reference and incorporated in this section as fully as if set forth at length in this section. 
(b)  When reference is made to the duties of certain officials named in the amusement device code, that designated official of the city who has duties corresponding to those of the named official in the code shall be deemed to be the responsible official insofar as enforcing the provisions of the code are concerned. 
(c)  As soon as practical after the publication of a later edition of the Standard Amusement Device Code, the city council shall review and adopt the code with such amendments and modifications as it deems practical. 
(Ord. No. 1992-9, § 1, 6-1-92) 
State Law reference- Adoption by reference, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-8. 
Secs. 18-57-18-75. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ELECTRICAL CODE 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 18-76. - Purpose; scope. 
(a)  The purpose of this article is the practical safeguarding of persons and of buildings and their contents from hazards arising from the use of electricity. 
(b)  The provisions of this article shall apply to every electrical installation, including alterations, repairs and equipment, within or connected to the electrical system of the city, except as may be specifically exempted in this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-27) 
Sec. 18-77. - Penalties. 
    Any person who violates the provisions of this article shall be subject to punishment as prescribed in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 8-31(c)) 
Secs. 18-78-18-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 
Subdivision I. - General Provisions 

Sec. 18-91. - Obedience to inspector's orders. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse to obey any order of the electrical inspector issued under the provisions of this article, and such person shall be subject to the penalty prescribed in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 8-48) 
Sec. 18-92. - Denial of entry for inspector. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to refuse entry to the electrical inspector when he is performing the duties prescribed in this article, and such person shall be subject to the penalty prescribed in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 8-46) 
Sec. 18-93. - Conflict of interest of inspectors. 
    No officer or employee connected with the electrical inspector's office shall be financially interested in the furnishing of labor, materials or appliances for the construction, alteration or maintenance of electrical installations or in the making of plans or specifications therefor, unless such person is the owner of such building. No employee shall engage in any work which is inconsistent with his duties or with the interest of the inspector's office. 
(Code 1974, § 8-39) 
Sec. 18-94. - Disputes; appeals. 
    Any dispute between the electrical inspector, while in the performance of his duties, and any person shall be presented to the electrical board for settlement. If no settlement is made, either party may request a board of arbitration to be formed, in which case each party to the dispute shall select one arbitrator and these two shall select a third member. The decision of the board of arbitration shall be final and binding upon all parties unless appealed to the city council. Decisions of the city council may be appealed to courts having jurisdiction. Any action shall stand, unless and until reversed by a higher authority. 
(Code 1974, §§ 8-29, 8-30) 
Sec. 18-95. - Discontinuance of electrical service for noncompliance. 
    For failure to comply with this article, the electrical inspector shall, after due notice, order discontinuance of electrical service to the locality of the building concerned and shall enforce such discontinuance until there is compliance with the requirements of this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-31(a)) 
Secs. 18-96-18-105. - Reserved. 
Subdivision II. - Electrical Board[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Boards, commissions, and authorities, § 2-241 et seq. 

Sec. 18-106. - Created; membership. 
(a)  There is created for the city an electrical board to be composed of five members. 
(b)  The board shall be composed of a representative of the power supply company, two master electricians, one electrical engineer (registered professional) and the electrical inspector for the city, such members to be appointed by the mayor and council. The members shall be citizens of the city, at least 25 years of age and, in addition, electricians shall have had at least five years' experience as master electricians. 
(c)  The members shall serve staggered terms of four years each, except for position number 1. The positions, qualifications and terms of office shall be as follows: 
(1)  Position number 1, city electrical inspector, term to expire November 1 of each year. 
(2)  Position number 2, master electrician, term to expire November 1, 1986, and November 1 of each fourth year thereafter. 
(3)  Position number 3, representative of the power supply company, term to expire November 1, 1987, and November 1 of each fourth year thereafter. 
(4)  Position number 4, master electrician, term to expire November 1, 1988, and November 1 of each fourth year thereafter. 
(5)  Position number 5, electrical engineer, term to expire November 1, 1989, and November 1 of each fourth year thereafter. 
(d)  The members may at any time be removed by the city council. Initial terms of office shall begin immediately upon the city council's appointment of initial members. Whenever a vacancy shall occur, the city council shall appoint a new member to the board to fill the unexpired term. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.21) 
Sec. 18-107. - Secretary. 
    The electrical inspector shall serve as secretary of the electrical board. He shall advise the board in all matters under discussion, and he shall have the same voting power as any other member of the board. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.22) 
Sec. 18-108. - Organization. 
    The electrical board shall establish all rules and procedures necessary to conduct the business of the board. The board shall elect one member to serve as chairman, and all proceedings shall be subject to approval by the city council. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.23) 
Sec. 18-109. - Compensation. 
    The members of the electrical board shall serve without compensation. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.24) 
Sec. 18-110. - Meetings. 
    The electrical board shall meet at least twice yearly and shall meet at any time on 24 hours' notice by the chairman. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.25) 
Sec. 18-111. - Filling vacancies. 
    Any vacancy on the electrical board shall be filled in the manner prescribed for the member so vacating. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.26) 
Sec. 18-112. - Quorum. 
    Three members of the electrical board shall constitute a quorum for the conduct of business. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.27) 
Sec. 18-113. - Powers and duties. 
(a)  Administration. The electrical board shall be considered as the administrative authority supervising the enforcement of this article. 
(b)  Certification. 
(1)  Application for certificate. The board shall prescribe the manner and form of application for a certificate to engage in the installation and maintenance of electrical wiring and equipment. 
(2)  Examination. An examination for electrical certification shall be held on the date set by the board and not less than once every three months, if requested. 
(3)  Issuance of certificate. The board shall, if satisfied with the results of such examination, issue a certificate of a style and form determined by the board, in the name of the person so examined. 
(c)  Hearings on charges of violations. The board shall have the power and duty to receive and consider all charges of violation of this article and to conduct hearings on all such matters. Charges shall be in writing, and a copy of the charges shall be attached to a notice to appear before the board and be served to the person so charged at least 48 hours before such hearing. Both the city and the person charged shall have the right to introduce evidence and to appear by counsel. If the person filing the charges or the person so charged is also a member of the board, the member shall have no vote in the proceedings. 
(d)  Interpretations of technical matters in disputes. Charges arising from disputes over interpretation of technical sections of this article shall be dealt with in the manner described in sections 18-94 and 18-197. 
(e)  Suspension of certificates. The board may either suspend or revoke the certificate of the person charged if it, after such a hearing, deems him guilty of the charges preferred. 
(f)  Recommendation of amendments. The board shall consider and recommend all matters relating to any amendment of this article to the city and the members of the city council. 
(g)  Grants of special permission. The board shall meet and pass or deny on all matters related to special permission contemplated by the electrical code. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.28) 
Secs. 18-114-18-125. - Reserved. 
Subdivision III. - Permits, Inspections and Certificate 

Sec. 18-126. - Permit required. 
(a)  No person shall install or repair any electrical wiring or equipment, except repairs which do not alter or change the original wiring or equipment, nor shall the load be increased until a permit therefor has been secured from the electrical inspector. 
(b)  Any person who shall commence any work within the scope of this article without first having obtained a proper permit therefor shall pay an additional fee in the amount of $25.00, in addition to the regular inspection fee for the work. For repair work requiring a permit, the person should notify the inspector and get a permit by the end of the next working day. 
(Code 1974, §§ 8-31(b)(5), 8-40, 8-42) 
Sec. 18-127. - Application for permit. 
    All applications for electrical permits shall be written on forms supplied by the electrical inspector's office and shall be dealt with as provided in this division. 
(1)  Permit valuation. 
Residential new construction: Total square footage × $100.00 = Value of construction. 
Accessory structures/detached garage/etc.: Total square footage × $50.00 = Value of construction. 
Commercial new construction: Total square footage × $127.50 = Value of construction. 
(Code 1974, § 8-41; Ord. No. 2009-2, 4-6-09) 
Sec. 18-128. - Obtaining permit by misrepresentation or false statement. 
    The electrical inspector shall revoke any electrical permit or approval issued by his office when, in his opinion, such permit or approval was obtained by misrepresentation of material fact or by false statement. 
(Code 1974, § 8-31(b)(1)) 
Sec. 18-129. - Inspection required. 
    All new electrical work and equipment and such portions of existing systems as may be affected by new work shall be inspected to ensure compliance with all the requirements of this article and to ensure that the installation of the electrical system and equipment is in accordance with approved plans. 
(Code 1974, § 8-43) 
Sec. 18-130. - Failure to notify inspector. 
    Any person who shall fail to notify the inspector's office of readiness for inspection, as required by this division, shall pay a penalty of $5.00, in addition to the regular inspection fee for such work. 
(Code 1974, § 8-31(b)(6)) 
Sec. 18-131. - Inspection fees. 
(a)  Fee schedule. The following electrical inspection fee schedule is adopted: 
RESIDENTIAL 
New services: 
Home, up to 200-amp, main switch ..... $ 30.00 
Apartments, per apartment, up to 150-amp switch ..... 15.00 
Change services ..... 15.00 
Wiring additions: 
One room ..... 5.00 
Two rooms ..... 8.00 
Three rooms or more ..... 10.00 
Alterations ..... 5.00 
Inspection fee for temporary services ..... 15.00 
Electrical permit issuing fee ..... 25.00 
Minimum permit fee ..... 25.00 
All rewiring permits will be based on job value. 
COMMERCIAL AND INDUSTRIAL 
New services, per amp of main switch ..... $0.25 
Change services, per amp of added switch ..... 0.25 
Minimum fee will be $25.00. New service $0.25 per amp. Any additional fees will be determined by the electrical inspector. 
Inspection fee for temporary services ..... 15.00 
Electrical permit issuing fee ..... 25.00 
All rewiring permits will be based on job value. 
(b)  Additional inspections. Such inspection fee shall include a second inspection where defects or violations are noted in the first inspection. If additional inspections are required because of defects or violations, there shall be a charge of $25.00 per trip added to the inspection fee. 
(c)  Payment. Inspection fees shall be on a cash basis, as enumerated in subsection (a) of this section. 
(d)  Temporary service. Inspection fee for temporary service: $15.00. 
(Code 1974, § 8-44; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 2.2, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2009-2, 4-6-09) 
State Law reference- Electrical fees authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-59. 
Sec. 18-132. - Covering electrical system prior to inspection. 
(a)  Generally. No part of the electrical system shall be covered until it has been inspected and approved as prescribed in this division. 
(b)  Uncovering system. If any part of the electrical system has been covered in violation of this section, it shall be uncovered upon order from the electrical inspector, at the expense of the party so violating this section. 
(Code 1974, § 8-45) 
Sec. 18-133. - Notice of defects; discontinuance of use until corrected. 
    Upon notice from the electrical inspector to any owner, agent or person responsible for any wiring or equipment that it is in violation of the provisions of this article or that has become unsafe, such owner, agent or person shall cease to use the wiring or equipment until he has completed such changes as may be ordered by the electrical inspector and the changes have been approved by the electrical inspector. Failure to comply shall subject such owner, agent or person to the penalty prescribed in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 8-47) 
Sec. 18-134. - Removal of inspection notice. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to remove, deface or damage any inspection notice posted as required by this division. 
(Code 1974, § 8-49) 
Sec. 18-135. - Certificate of approval required after disconnection. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to make connection from a source of electrical energy to any electrical wiring, device or equipment which has been ordered to be disconnected by the electrical inspector until a certificate of approval has been issued by the electrical inspector authorizing the reconnection and use of such wiring, device or equipment. It shall be unlawful for any commercial or industrial firm (nonresidential) that has had electrical service disconnected for any reason to connect to a source of electrical energy until a certificate of approval has been issued by the electrical inspector authorizing the reconnection of electric service. 
(Code 1974, § 8-49.1) 
Sec. 18-136. - Responsibility of utility companies. 
(a)  Before any meter is set on a new electrical installation within the city limits by any utility company or such company's authorized representative or agent, the company setting such meter must first receive the approval of the installation from the office of the building official or electrical inspector. New installations include moving mobile home meter poles from one location to another location. 
(b)  In case of emergency, power may be restored, subject to the approval by the electrical inspector, on the next following normal working day. 
(Code 1974, § 8-49.2) 
Sec. 18-137. - Reconnection of disconnected wiring. 
    Any person who shall make a connection from a source of electrical energy to any electrical wiring, device or equipment which has been ordered to be disconnected by the electrical inspector, unless a certificate of approval has been issued by the electrical inspector authorizing the connection and use of such wiring, device or equipment, shall be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 8-31(b)(7)) 
Secs. 18-138-18-150. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - INSTALLATION STANDARDS AND REQUIREMENTS 

Sec. 18-151. - Maintenance of electrical system. 
    All electrical systems and all devices, appliances or equipment attached therein shall be maintained in a safe manner. All devices and safeguards which are required by this article shall be maintained in good working order. The owner or the owner's agent shall be responsible for the maintenance of such system, devices, appliances and equipment. 
(Code 1974, § 8-28) 
Sec. 18-152. - Ordering illegal work. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to order any wiring or equipment installed which violates the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-32) 
Sec. 18-153. - Workmanlike manner of installation, supervision by master electrician. 
    Except as otherwise provided in this article, the installation and maintenance of all electrical wiring and equipment within the scope of this article shall be done in a workmanlike manner, by competent electricians under the direction of a master electrician certified under the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-33) 
Sec. 18-154. - Electrical code-Adopted. 
(a)  The National Fire Protection Association Pamphlet No. 70, commonly known as the National Electrical Code, 2008 edition, as published by the National Fire Protection Association, is adopted and shall, subject to the amendments contained in section 18-155, constitute the minimum standards for the installation, use, maintenance and sale of electrical wiring and equipment within the scope of this article. Interpretations of the electrical code shall, when required, be obtained as provided in section 90-6 of the electrical code. Current copies of the electrical code shall be made available to all persons who hold the required licenses. 
(b)  As soon as practical after the publication of a later [latest] edition of the National Electrical Code, the city council shall review and adopt the code with such amendments and modifications as it deems practical. 
(Ord. No. 1992-13, § 1(8-35), 7-6-92; Ord. No. 2002-3, §§ 1-3, 3-4-02; Ord. No 2005-14, § 2.3, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2008-3, § 1, 3-17-08) 
State Law reference- Adoption by reference, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-8. 
Sec. 18-155. - Same-Amendments, modifications, additions and deletions. 
(a)  Certain sections and articles of the electrical code adopted in this division require amendment for application under local conditions and certain sections require or contemplate application by special permission or action of the authority enforcing the code. In the interest of clarity and uniformity, such sections shall be predecided and shall have full effect as if published in the National Electrical Code itself, and shall take precedence over the edition of the electrical code adopted in section 18-154. 
(b)  The electrical code is amended as follows: 
(1)  Conductors. 
a.  Conductors of aluminum may be used on services and on individual branch circuits of 30 amperes and above. 
b.  Conductors, whether solid or stranded, shall not be smaller than no. 12 A.W.G., except as provided for in sections of the National Electrical Code as follows: 400-7, 410-18, 430-22, 610-14, 620-12 and 725-13. 
c.  Open wiring on insulators shall not be permitted in or on buildings, except by special permission. 
d.  Concealed knob-and-tube wiring provided for in article 324 of the National Electrical Code will not be permitted. 
e.  Nonmetallic sheathed cable (Romex) shall not be used in any nonresidential structure within the scope of this article. All wiring shall be installed in metal raceways. 
f.  Nonmetallic sheathed cable run exposed will be permitted only in private residences or apartments where the joists are bored for the installation of the cable, except for no. 4 or larger. Where cable is run at right angles to a joist in the attic, the joist need not be bored if the cable is installed in a clearance space three feet or less in the attic or run within one foot of the outside wall under the house. 
g.  The minimum size conductor for grounding a service shall be no. 4 A.W.G. copper, and provisions for no. 8 in table 250-94 are not applicable. Conductors of aluminum shall not be used for grounding or bonding. 
h.  Nonmetallic surface extensions shall not be used. Wiring as provided in article 342, National Electrical Code, shall not be installed as part of any work within the scope of this article. 
i.  All service entrance conductors for nonresidential installation originating from an overhead electrical system must be in rigid metallic conduit up to the distribution panel. Service entrance conductors from an underground electric supply system may be either rigid metallic conduit or PVC conduit up to the distribution panel. All other conductors must be in metallic or PVC conduit, except that service entrance cable may be installed as a service conductor in apartment houses, residences and farm buildings. Additional appropriate size copper grounding conductor must be used when PVC or metallic conduit is being utilized. All conduit runs shall contain a green grounding conductor of appropriate size. Complete and continuous grounding must be maintained for the total installation. 
(2)  Switchboard and panel boards. 
a.  Each lighting and appliance branch circuit panel board shall be individually protected on the supply side by not more than one main circuit breaker or set of fuses. 
b.  Service equipment shall not be permitted in clothes closets, bathrooms, kitchen cabinets or inaccessible places. 
c.  The service disconnecting means for all structures, residential and non-residential shall be installed at a readily accessible location on the outside of the building. 
(3)  Signs and outline lighting. 
a.  All circuit wiring from a distribution panel for signs shall be done by registered electricians, qualified by the provisions of this article. 
b.  All electric signs shall be inspected for compliance with the National Electrical Code on the sidewalk or on the premises where the sign is to be installed. 
(4)  Remodeling and renovation. 
a.  When a house or other building is moved or transported from one location to another, such house or other building shall be wired to code standards. 
b.  When occupancy of a house or other building is being changed from a residential occupancy to a nonresidential occupancy, such house or other building shall be required to conform to nonresidential occupancy wiring in that portion not used as a residence when the service has to be changed. 
c.  When rewiring a building that is being renovated, all wiring for new construction additions shall conform to this article. 
(5)  Low voltage circuits. 
a.  [Reserved.] 
b.  So-called electric fences, consisting of an electrically charged conductor or other electrically charged device intended to enclose, exclude or restrict persons or animals by electric shock, shall not be installed or used, regardless of its source or supply, except by special permission granted after written application to the electrical board. 
(6)  Modular or manufactured homes. The electrical contractor, in the presence of the city electrical inspector, shall subject modular or manufactured homes to a 1,000-volt DC test for a five-minute period on each phase with all other phases grounded to ascertain the quality and standards of the wiring installation. This test shall be performed after branch circuits are complete and after fixtures or appliances are installed. Hand-operated testers may not be used. Fixtures or appliances which are approved and installed shall not be required to withstand the test. Wiring systems failing to meet the standards established in this article will not be approved until the corrections are made and a satisfactory retest accomplished. The fee for the test will be $25.00. 
(Code 1974, § 8-36; Ord. No. 1992-13, § 2, 7-6-92; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 2.4, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2011-4, § 1, 9-19-2011) 
Sec. 18-156. - Standards for electrical materials. 
    All wire, devices, appliances and apparatus installed, used, sold or offered for sale within the city shall conform to the rules and regulations of this article, and, for the purpose of this article, they shall bear the label of Underwriters' Laboratories, Inc., or shall be approved by the authority enforcing this article. Such label or listing shall be prima facie evidence that such item conforms to this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-34) 
Sec. 18-157. - Items reserved for the electrical distribution companies. 
    All items not covered by the electrical code and this article, i.e., power distribution poles, transformers, etc., are reserved for electrical distribution companies of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 8-37) 
Sec. 18-158. - Clearance for service drops. 
    No person shall build, alter or erect any building or structure that will affect the clearance required for service drops and points of attachment of the drops. Upon discovery of violation of this section, the person responsible shall be required to remove the building or structure or to bear all expense involved in altering the service drop to obtain the necessary safe clearance. 
(Code 1974, § 8-38) 
Secs. 18-159-18-170. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - ELECTRICAL CONTRACTORS AND ELECTRICIANS[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 22. 

Subdivision I. - General Provisions 

Sec. 18-171. - Standards for master electrician. 
    A master electrician shall be a person who is competent to engage in all electrical matters within the scope of this article and to supervise others in such matters. 
(Code 1974, § 8-50) 
Sec. 18-172. - Duties and responsibilities of master electricians. 
(a)  Supervision. Master electricians shall install or supervise the installation of all electrical wiring and equipment, and alterations to wiring and equipment within the scope of this article. 
(b)  Compliance. Master electricians employed by an electrical contractor, duly qualified under this article, shall have final responsibility for compliance with or violations of all provisions of this article for all work done or equipment installed. 
(c)  Reporting the ordering of work in violation. If an owner, employer or any person of authority over a master electrician shall order work done or equipment installed that violates the provisions of this article, it shall be the duty of the master electrician to immediately notify, in writing, the electrical inspector of all particulars concerning the violation. 
(d)  Application for permit. It shall be the duty of the master electrician to apply for all permits to install or alter electrical wiring or equipment within the scope of this article, and before applying for such permit, the master electrician shall determine that the work or equipment contemplated is in compliance with the provisions of this article and shall furnish with his application all information requested by the electrical inspector. 
(e)  Request for inspection. The master electrician shall determine when work, as required by the electrical inspector, is ready for inspection and shall notify the electrical inspector's office for the inspection. The master electrician shall further notify the electrical inspector's office at the completion of any electrical installation within the scope of this article. 
(f)  Compliance with notice from inspector. Upon notice from the electrical inspector that any part of the wiring or equipment inspected is not acceptable under the provisions of this article, the master electrician in charge or the owner or the owner's agent shall, upon completion of such changes, so notify the inspector. 
(Code 1974, § 8-51) 
Sec. 18-173. - License fees. 
    Every person qualifying under this article shall be subject to paying such license fee as may be prescribed in the license and tax ordinance of the city. All license fees shall be as prescribed in the license and tax ordinance of the city. 
(Code 1974, §§ 8-52, 8-52.9(d)) 
Sec. 18-174. - Use of name or certificate by another. 
    No certificate issued under the provisions of this division is transferable or assignable, and no person who holds a certificate shall allow his name or certificate to be used by any other person, directly or indirectly, to obtain a permit to do anything within the scope of this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.8(f)) 
Secs. 18-175-18-185. - Reserved. 
Subdivision II. - Certification of Masters 

Sec. 18-186. - Certificate required. 
    Before any person shall engage in the installation and maintenance of any electrical wiring or equipment within the scope of this article or act as a master electrician, such person shall secure a certificate under this subdivision. 
(Code 1974, §§ 8-52.2, 8-52.4) 
Sec. 18-187. - Exemptions. 
(a)  The exemptions enumerated as follows shall constitute the sole and only exemptions to this subdivision. Such exemptions shall apply only to the portions of this subdivision concerning the requirement for a certificate: 
(1)  Master electricians; electrical contractors. Persons holding a valid certificate as a master electrician or electrical contractor issued by the state shall be exempt from the requirements of this subdivision concerning qualifications for a certificate. 
(2)  Public utility employees. Employees of the public utilities are exempt while performing the duties required in the operation of such utility. 
(3)  Telephone and telegraph company employees. Employees of telephone and telegraph companies are exempt, except for the installation of wiring and equipment solely for electrical heat, light or power. 
(4)  Plant maintenance electricians. Plant maintenance electricians in industrial plants which maintain departments for the maintenance of wiring and equipment are exempt, except that such plant maintenance electricians shall register with the electrical board. In addition, the electrical inspector may, at his discretion, issue a continuing permit for such maintenance and incidental alterations or additions as may be required for operation of the plant. Such permit shall not entitle the plant to engage in wiring or installations as a part of an expansion, remodeling or rebuilding program. All work and equipment installed under such permit shall be subject to inspections and shall conform to all provisions of this article. An industrial plant may engage in all matters related to this article on the property occupied by it if one or more of its maintenance electricians are certified as required by this subdivision. It may be exempt from the bond and license requirement of this subdivision so long as its personnel work only within the confines of the property. 
(5)  Electrical appliance repair. Persons engaged solely in the business of repairing electrical appliances or equipment shall have all of the duties and responsibilities prescribed in this article. Such person is exempt from the requirements for a certificate, bond and insurance as specified in this subdivision. 
(6)  Individuals. A certificate will not be required for an individual personally doing electrical work for his own use on residential premises owned and occupied by him or being built for occupancy by him. Such person may be granted a permit by the electrical inspector for such work only by him, upon his satisfying the electrical inspector that such work can be capably performed on such premises, and that the premises is or will be occupied by him. Work done under such permit shall be inspected and shall conform to all the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Nothing in this subdivision shall be construed to prohibit any person or plant from employing apprentice electricians under the direct supervision of duly certified or registered electricians. 
(c)  No exemption granted under this section shall be construed as exempting such person, plant or owner from paying the required permit and inspection fee provided in section 18-131. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.5) 
Sec. 18-188. - Certified electrician required for electrical work by firm or corporation. 
    Any firm or corporation that desires to engage in the installation and maintenance of electrical wiring and equipment shall do all such work through persons duly qualified under this subdivision. If one or more members of such firm or corporation is a master electrician who has passed the examination provided in this subdivision, a certificate may be issued to the firm or corporation as such. If no member of the firm or corporation is a master electrician, no permit shall be issued to such firm or corporation unless the work is laid out and installed under the supervision of a master electrician in the regular and full-time employment of the applicant for the permit. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.3) 
Sec. 18-189. - Certificate application procedure. 
(a)  Fee receipt to be filed with application. Persons desiring to obtain a master, residential, or journeyman's electrical certificate for a city business license shall first pay to the city clerk/treasurer the fee provided in section 18-190 and obtain a receipt therefor. With this receipt, he or she may file his application with the electrical inspector for a certificate. The application fee shall be $50.00. The applicant must also provide the city with documentation as required by the Board reflecting a minimum of four years practical electrical experience in the category sought to be examined. 
(b)  Application form. The application shall be on such form as may be Adopted by the Electrical Board and shall state whether the applicant desires a certificate as a masters or residential electrician. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.6; Ord. No. 2008-1, 5-19-08) 
Sec. 18-190. - Examination. 
(a)  Upon compliance with section 18-189 applicant shall make his or her own arrangements either with the International Code Council for the ICC Masters Exam, ICC Journeymans Exam, or ICC Residential Exam, or the State of Alabama Electrical Board, in order to be eligible to obtain a city electrical license in the category examined. Upon satisfactorily passing the appropriate electrical license exam and review and approval of the City of Eufaula Electrical Board, the applicant shall be entitled to a city electrician's license for his or her appropriate category upon the payment of the prescribed license fees. 
(b)  In order to be eligible to annually renew any electrical license, the applicant must provide the City of Eufaula with documentation of 8 professional development course hours attended during the 12 calendar months preceeding the date of the license renewal application in order to renew an active masters or residential or journeymans only certificate. This shall be effective January 1, 2009. 
(c)  Anyone licensed in the city prior to December 31, 1990, and who has kept his license continually in force up to December 31, 2007, will be certified without examination. The applicant will comply with all other pertinent requirements of this subdivision. 
(Code 1974, §§ 8-52.7, 8-52.9(a); Ord. No. 2005-14, § 2.5, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2008-1, 5-19-08) 
Sec. 18-191. - Insurance. 
    Before any master electrician's certificate is issued, the applicant must first deliver to the city clerk/treasurer a public liability and property damage insurance policy with liability limits in an amount of not less than $100,000.00 for each claim, written by an insurance company authorized to do business in the state, which policy shall make provision for the following: 
(1)  The city shall be named as an insured in the policy, and the policy shall cover and protect against all liability of the city for personal injury and property damage of any kind. 
(2)  In the policy, the applicant and the insurance company shall agree to indemnify and hold harmless the city from and against all loss or expense, including costs and attorney fees, because of liability imposed by law upon the city for damages because of bodily injury, including death at any time resulting therefrom, sustained by any person or on account of damage to property, including loss of use thereof, arising out of and in consequence of the performance of work, whether due to the negligence of the contractor, his subcontractors, employees or agents or the city. 
(3)  The policy shall contain the following provision: 
     "In addition to all other coverage afforded by this policy, the company agrees to indemnify the City of Eufaula, or any customer of the named insured contractor on account of any loss or damage sustained by them or either of them as a result of the failure of said contractor to install or maintain wiring and equipment in conformity with his contract and the requirements of the codes, laws and ordinances of the City of Eufaula." 
(4)  The policy shall also insure and indemnify the contractor against liability imposed by law upon the contractor because of negligence. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.1; Ord. No. 2009-5, 5-18-09) 
Sec. 18-192. - Issuance. 
    Upon compliance with and completion of the requirements in this subdivision, the person shall receive from the electrical board a certificate of competency as requested in his application. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.8(a)) 
Sec. 18-193. - Expiration. 
    All master electrician certificates shall expire on March 31 of each year. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.8(c)) 
Sec. 18-194. - Renewal. 
(a)  Master electrician certificates shall be renewed annually without further examination unless as otherwise prescribed in this subdivision. If a certificate is not renewed within 12 months from the date of expiration, it shall become void, and the holder thereof shall be required to requalify as provided in this subdivision. 
(b)  If any certificate is not renewed by March 31, the holder shall pay a late charge of $10.00. 
(Code 1974, §§ 8-52.8(b), (d), 8-52.9(b), (c)) 
Sec. 18-195. - Availability of certificate. 
    A person who holds a master electrician's certificate shall keep the certificate or evidence of the certificate available at all times. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.8(e)) 
Sec. 18-196. - Suspension or revocation of certificate. 
(a)  Any person certified as prescribed in this subdivision who fails to correct any defect in such person's work after having been duly notified for a period of ten days shall receive no further permit until such defects have been corrected. 
(b)  The electrical board may, after notice and opportunity to be heard, suspend or revoke any certificate issued by virtue of this subdivision if the board shall determine that the work done by the holder of the certificate is of an inferior quality because of incompetency or neglect and that such action is in the interest of the public. 
(c)  Any person holding a city certificate as required by this subdivision who fails or refuses to correct any such violation shall be subject to forfeiture of such certificate, and the certificate may be revoked by the electrical board. When the revocation of such certificate is to be considered at any meeting, that person to whom the certificate has been issued shall have at least three days' notice, in writing, of the time and place of such meeting, together with a statement of the grounds upon which it is proposed to revoke such certificate. 
(Code 1974, § 8-31(b)(2)-(b)(4)) 
Sec. 18-197. - Charges made to electrical board; effect of revocation of certificate upon business license. 
    All charges of violation of this article against persons certified under this subdivision shall first be made with the electrical board. Revocation of any certificate by the board shall automatically condition the license of the holder, unless, in the case of a firm or corporation, more than one member shall immediately cause his name to be registered on the license. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.10) 
Sec. 18-198. - Recertification following revocation. 
    Any person holding a certificate under this subdivision who shall have his certificate revoked may apply six months from the time of such revocation for another examination by complying with the provisions of this article. Upon successfully passing the examination, he shall receive a new certificate. 
(Code 1974, § 8-52.11) 
Secs. 18-199-18-220. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - GAS CODE 

Sec. 18-221. - Title. 
    This article shall be known as the gas code of the city and may be cited as such. 
(Code 1974, § 8-53) 
Sec. 18-222. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Certain appliances means conversion burners, floor furnaces, central heating plants, vented wall furnaces, water heaters and boilers. 
    Certificate of approval means a document or tag issued or attached by the inspector to the inspected material, piping or appliance installation, filled out, together with date, address of the premises, and signed by the inspector. 
    Gas company means any person distributing gas within the corporate limits of the city or authorized and proposing to so engage. 
    Inspector means the person appointed as gas inspector and includes each assistant inspector, if any, from time to time acting as such under this article by appointment of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 8-54) 
Sec. 18-223. - Purpose; conformance required. 
    The purpose of this article is to provide minimum standards, provisions and requirements for safe installation of consumers' gas piping and gas appliances. All such gas piping and gas appliances installed, replaced, maintained or repaired within the corporate limits of the city shall conform to the requirements of this article and to the specifications, rules and regulations of the gas code adopted by reference in this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-55) 
Sec. 18-224. - Use of existing piping and appliances. 
    Notwithstanding any provision in this article to the contrary, consumer's piping installed prior to August 20, 1969, or piping installed to supply other than natural gas may be converted to natural gas, if the inspector finds, upon inspection and proper tests, that such piping will render reasonably satisfactory gas service to the consumer and will not in any way endanger life or property; otherwise, such piping shall be altered or replaced, in whole or in part, to conform with the requirements of this article. 
(Code 1974, § 8-58) 
Sec. 18-225. - Gas code adopted. 
(a)  The International Fuel Gas Code, 2006 edition, published by the Southern Building Code Congress International, Inc., including all appendixes, is adopted and incorporated in this section by reference and made a part of this article as if fully set forth in this section. Three copies of such code shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk/treasurer. 
(b)  When reference is made in the gas code to the duties of certain officials named therein, that designated official, the building official, who has duties corresponding to those of the named official in the code shall be deemed to be the responsible official insofar as enforcing the provisions of the code are concerned. 
(c)  As soon as practical after the publication of a later edition of the Standard Gas Code, the city council shall review and adopt the code with such amendments and modifications as it deems practical. 
(Ord. No. 1992-9, § 1, 6-1-92; Ord. No. 2002-3, §§ 1-3, 3-4-02; Ord. No. 2005-14, § 1, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2008-3, § 1, 3-17-08) 
State Law reference- Adoption by reference, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-45-8. 
Secs. 18-226-18-245. - Reserved.

DIVISION 2. - DEMOLITION OF UNSAFE STRUCTURES 

Sec. 18-341. - Generally. 
    The city shall have authority, after notice provided for in this division, to move or demolish buildings and structures, or parts of buildings and structures, party walls and foundations, when the same are found by the governing body of the city to be unsafe to the extent of being a public nuisance from any cause. 
(Ord. No. 1997-13, Art. III(1), 10-20-97) 
Sec. 18-342. - Meaning of "appropriate city official"; duties; notice of unsafe or dangerous condition. 
    The term "appropriate city official" as used in this article shall mean any city building official or deputy and any other city official or city employee designated by the mayor or other chief executive officer of the city as the person to exercise the authority and perform the duties delegated by this article to "appropriate city official." Whenever the appropriate city official of the city shall find that any building, structure, part of building or structure, party wall or foundation situated in any city is unsafe to the extent that it is a public nuisance, the official shall report the findings to the city governing body. At that time the city governing body shall determine whether the building, structure, part of building or structure, party wall, or foundation constitutes a public nuisance. Should the city governing body find by resolution that the building, structure, part of building or structure, party wall, or foundation is a public nuisance, then the appropriate city official shall give the person or persons, firm, association, or corporation last assessing the property for state taxes, by certified or registered mail to the address on file in the revenue commissioner's office, notice to remedy the unsafe or dangerous condition of the building or structure, or to demolish the same, within a reasonable time set out in the notice, which time shall not be less than 30 days unless an extension is granted by the appropriate city official or suffer the building or structure to be demolished by the city and the cost thereof assessed against the property. The mailing of the certified or registered notice, properly addressed and postage prepaid, shall constitute notice as required in this division. The city shall place a sign or placard within 15 feet of the entrance of the building or structure, indicating that the city had declared the building or structure to be a public nuisance; however, if there is no entrance in which to place the sign or placard, then the sign or placard may be posted at any location upon the building or structure. 
(Ord. No. 1997-13, Art. III(2), 10-20-97) 
Sec. 18-343. - Hearing procedure; order; appeal. 
(a)  Within the time specified in the notice, but not more than 30 days from the date the notice is given, any person, firm or corporation having an interest in the building or structure may file a written request for a hearing before the governing body of the city, together with the objections to the finding by the city governing body that the building or structure is unsafe to the extent of becoming a public nuisance. The filing of the request shall hold in abeyance any action on the finding of the city governing body until a determination thereon is made by the city governing body. The hearing shall be held not less than five nor more than 30 days after the request. In the event that no hearing is timely requested, the governing body shall order the building or structure to be demolished. The demolition may be accomplished, at the option of the city, by the use of its own forces or it may provide by contract for the demolition. For purposes of this article, compliance with the competitive bid laws are not required. The city shall have authority to sell or otherwise dispose of salvaged materials resulting from the demolition. 
(b)  Any person aggrieved by the decision of the governing body at the hearing may, within ten days thereafter, appeal to the circuit court upon filing with the clerk of the court notice of appeal and bond for security of costs in the form and amount to be approved by the circuit clerk. Upon filing of the notice of appeal and approval of the bond, the clerk of the court shall serve a copy of the notice of appeal on the clerk of the city and the appeal shall be docketed in the court, and shall be a preferred case therein. The clerk of the city shall, upon receiving the notice, file with the clerk of the court a copy of the findings and determination of the governing body in proceedings, and trials shall be held without jury upon the determination of the governing body that the building or structure is unsafe to the extent that it is a public nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 1997-13, Art. III(3), 10-20-97) 
Sec. 18-344. - Report of cost of demolition; adoption of resolution fixing costs; proceeds of sale of salvaged materials; objections to findings of cost; notice. 
    Upon demolition of the building or structure, the appropriate city official shall make an itemized written report to the governing body of the cost thereof. The cost of the demolition shall be the actual cost the city incurs in the demolition should the city use its own forces, including administrative costs the city incurs in abating the nuisance. Should the city contract for demolition, the cost shall be the actual cost the contractor charges the city for the demolition, including administrative costs the city incurs in abating the nuisance. Upon the report of the costs by the appropriate city official, the governing body shall adopt a resolution fixing the costs which it finds were incurred in the demolition and assessing the same against the property; provided, however, the proceeds of any moneys received from the use of salvaged materials from the building or structure shall be used or applied against the cost of the demolition; and provided, further, then any person, firm, or corporation having an interest in the property may be heard at the meeting concerning the fixing of the costs or the amounts thereof. The city clerk shall give at least ten days' notice of the meeting at which the fixing of the costs is to be considered by first-class mail to all entities having an interest in the property whose address and interest is determined from the revenue commissioner's records on the property or is otherwise known to the clerk. The fixing of costs by the governing body shall constitute a special assessment against the lot or lots, parcel or parcels of land upon which the building or structure was located, and thus made and confirmed shall constitute lien on the property for the amount of the assessment. The lien shall be superior to all other liens on the property except liens for taxes, and shall continue in force until paid. A certified copy of the resolution shall be filed in the office of the Judge of Probate of Barbour County. Upon filing, the revenue commissioner of the county shall add the amount of the lien to the ad valorem tax bill on the property and shall collect the amount as if it were a tax and remit the amount to the city. The county revenue commissioner shall retain ten percent of the amount of each lien collected to be used for operational purposes. 
(Ord. No. 1997-13, Art. III(4), 10-20-97) 
Sec. 18-345. - Assessment of costs; sale and redemption of lots. 
    The city shall have the power to assess the costs authorized for in this division against any lot or lots, parcel or parcels of land purchased by the state at any sale for nonpayment of taxes, and where any assessment is made against the lot or lots, parcel or parcels of the land, a subsequent redemption thereof by any person authorized to redeem, or sale thereof by the state, shall not operate to discharge, or in any manner affect the lien of the city for the assessment, but any redemptioner or purchaser at any sale by the state of any lot or lots, parcel or parcels of land upon which an assessment has been levied, whether prior to or subsequent to sale to the state for the nonpayment of taxes, shall take the same subject to the assessment. The assessment shall then be added to the tax bill of the property, collected as a tax, and remitted to the city. 
(Ord. No. 1997-13, Art. III(5), 10-20-97) 
Sec. 18-346. - Payment of assessments. 
    Payment of any assessment, or if delinquent, the collection of the assessment, shall be made in the manner and as provided for the payment of municipal improvement assessments as provided for the payment of and delinquent collection of municipal improvement assessments pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-48-1 et seq. The city may, in the latter notice, elect to have the revenue commissioner collect the assessment by adding the same to the tax bill; upon the election the revenue commissioner shall collect the assessment using all methods available for collecting ad valorem taxes. Ten percent of the amount of each assessment collected by the county revenue commissioner shall be retained by the county revenue commissioner and used for operational purposes. 
(Ord. No. 1997-13, Art. III(6), 10-20-97) 
Secs. 18-347-18-360. - Reserved.

Chapter 19 - CONSTRUCTION SITE STORMWATER MANAGEMENT[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 18. 

Sec. 19-1. - General. 
(a)  The provisions of this chapter are adopted to provide minimum standards to ensure effective construction stormwater management, drainage control, and erosion and sediment control measures for all new construction, additions, and alterations. It is the contractor's responsibility to ensure that the requirements of this chapter are met. No final inspection shall be made until the requirements of this chapter are met. 
(b)  It shall be the contractor's responsibility to ensure compliance with applicable Alabama Department of Environmental Management (ADEM) Construction Stormwater Management Administrative Code Chapter 336-6-12, as amended, and/or any applicable ADEM construction site permit requirements, which are designed to prevent/minimize to the maximum extent practicable the discharge of sediment and other potential pollutants in construction stormwater runoff to ensure the protection of water quality in accordance with applicable federal and state law. 
(c)  It shall be the contractor's responsibility to ensure that all Best Management Practices (BMPs) implemented pursuant to the requirements of this chapter are implemented and maintained in accordance with established, industry standard, good engineering practices, and ADEM requirements. 
(d)  Upon notice, the contractor shall promptly implement effective BMPs and/or repair/improve any deficient BMPs pursuant to the requirements of this chapter. Land disturbing activities shall not commence without prior approval and the installation of BMP's. 
(e)  Failure to comply with the requirements of this chapter may subject the contractor to fines, and suspension and/or termination of City of Eufaula approval for continued construction, as may be authorized by the City of Eufaula Code, and may result in notification of such to ADEM, as appropriate. 
(f)  Upon request, the contractor shall promptly provide proof of compliance with ADEM Construction Stormwater Management Administrative Code Rules, as amended, and/or applicable ADEM construction site permit requirements. 
(Ord. No. 2005-11, 9-19-05) 
Sec. 19-2. - Erosion and sediment control. 
(a)  Roadside ditches and embankments in right-of-way shall be stabilized to prevent erosion. 
(b)  It shall be contractor's responsibility to provide the necessary measures to ensure that clearing, grubbing, grading, landscaping, and other construction activities do not adversely affect the drainage structures important to overall storm water management and control. 
(c)  It shall be the contractor's responsibility to ensure proper implementation, regular inspection, and continual maintenance of effective best management practices (BMPs) for construction site erosion and sediment control. 
(d)  It shall be the contractor's responsibility to promptly remove and/or remediate to the extent practicable sediment deposited offsite onto the City of Eufaula right-of-way, property, or stormwater drainage system. 
(Ord. No. 2005-11, 9-19-05) 
Sec. 19-3. - Lot drainage. 
(a)  Positive slope of finish grade shall be provided to direct water away from all foundations. 
(b)  Side lot swales shall be utilized, as necessary, to direct lot drainage to right-of-way or other drainage easements. 
(c)  Roof drains shall be directed away from structures and into swales or other means shall be used to prevent soil erosion and to direct water from the building foundation. 
(d)  Driveway pipe shall be of the proper size to accept drainage waters. Minimum diameter of pipe shall be 18 inches, and be class three concrete pipe. Metal pipe or HDPE may be substituted for concrete pipe. If HDPE pipe is used, the ends shall be protected by concrete headwalls. 
(e)  All driveway and service drive piping shall be installed on appropriate elevation and grade to prevent standing water. 
(Ord. No. 2005-11, 9-19-05) 
Chapter 22 - BUSINESSES[1] 

Footnotes:
