Cross reference- Finance, § 2-291 et seq.; advertising, ch. 6; alcoholic beverages, ch. 10; electrical contractors and electricians, § 18-171 et seq.; charitable solicitations, ch. 26; smoking in public places, § 50-26 et seq.; fair housing practices, § 54-26 et seq.; secondhand goods, ch. 74; taxation, ch. 86; vegetation, ch. 98. 

Sec. 22-1. - Daily reports for pawnshops required. 
    Every person who owns or operates a pawnshop shall file a report with the city clerk/treasurer or chief of police every day, listing all property received by the pawnshop that day and all other such information required by the form of such report, which shall be provided by the city. Violation of this section shall be deemed an offense and punishable on conviction as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 16-41) 
State Law reference- Pawnbrokers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 8-1-80 et seq. 
Sec. 22-2. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2003-3, adopted April 21, 2003, repealed § 22-2 in its entirety. Formerly said section pertained to bond for peddlers. 
Chapter 23 - HORSE-DRAWN CARRIAGES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Livestock, ch. 14, art. II. 

Sec. 23-1. - Definitions. 
    [The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:] 
    Business license means the right and privilege granted by the city for the operation of a business incorporating the use of one or more horse-drawn carriages within the corporate limits of the city. 
    Chauffer's license means the written authority granted by the city for an individual to drive or operate a horse-drawn carriage within the city. 
    City shall mean the City of Eufaula, Alabama, a municipal corporation. 
    Company means the holder of a business license to operate a horse-drawn carriage business under the provisions of this article whether a person, firm, partnership or corporation. 
    Driver means any person who drives or operates a horse-drawn carriage on the streets of Eufaula for an authorized carriage company. 
    Horse; animal shall include all draft animals used to draw vehicles such as, but not limited to: horses or mules. The term "horse" and "animal" are interchangeable. 
    Horse-drawn carriage means any hack or carriage which is operated by being drawn by a horse, mule, or other beast of burden, for the transportation for hire of passengers. 
    Stand means a public place alongside the curb of a street or elsewhere which has been designated by the mayor as reserved exclusively for the use of horse-drawn carriages. 
    Street shall mean and include any street, alley, lane, avenue, court, or public place in the city's entertainment district. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-2. - Licensing of horse-drawn carriage companies; headquarters. 
(a)  Business license required . 
(1)  No person, firm, or corporation shall operate a business involving the use of one or more horse-drawn carriages on the streets of the city unless a business license for such business has first been granted by the city in accordance with the provisions of city ordinances. The business license shall be $50.00 per carriage and be effective only for the calendar year stated in the document, unless suspended or revoked sooner as provided by ordinance. 
(2)  Application for the business license shall be made on forms provided by the city clerk and shall provide such information as is required for other business license applications, and such additional information as may be necessary to define completely the business operation. Renewal of the business license shall be required prior to January 31 of each year. 
(b)  Fixed place of business required . Each horse-drawn carriage company, as a condition for holding a license under the provisions of this article and the business license ordinance, shall establish and maintain a fixed headquarters on private property for the operation of the company's business; the headquarters to conform to the ordinances of the city, and shall provide adequate off-street parking space for all horse-drawn carriages not in service on the streets. The company headquarters shall not be moved except by the approved transfer of the company's license to another location. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-3. - Records. 
(a)  Each animal-drawn carriage operator shall maintain at a single location business records of its animal-drawn carriage business. The records must contain the following information at a minimum: 
(1)  An identification of the carriage used for each trip; 
(2)  The number of trips made by each carriage on a daily basis; 
(3)  The number of passengers per trip on a daily basis; and 
(4)  An identification of the animal used for each trip and a statement of the periods of work and rest for each. 
(b)  Records shall be made available for inspection when requested by the city. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-4. - Insurance. 
(a)  Indemnity for benefit of city . Any horse-drawn carriage company operating under this article shall hold the city, its officers, agents, servants, and employees, harmless against any and all liability, loss, damages, or expense which may accrue to the city by reason of negligence, default or misconduct of the company in connection with the rights granted to such company hereunder. The city shall be named as an additional insured on all public liability insurance instruments. Nothing in this article shall be considered to make the city, its officers, agents, servants, or employees liable for damages because of any negligent act or omission or commission by any horse-drawn carriage business or operation by the company of a horse-drawn carriage business or service, either in respect to injury to persons or with respect to damage to property which may be sustained. 
(b)  Insurance for benefit of passengers and/or the general public . Any horse-drawn carriage company desiring a business license to do business shall give and maintain a policy of indemnity from an insurance company authorized to do business in the state for each vehicle in use as a horse-drawn carriage. The minimum coverage shall be $100,000.00 for bodily injury to any one person, $300,000.00 for injury to more than one person which are sustained in the same accident, and $25,000.00 for property damage resulting from one accident. The indemnity insurance shall insure to the benefit of any person who shall be injured or who shall sustain damage to property caused by the negligence of a horse-drawn carriage company, its servants, or agents. 
(c)  Blanket policy . Any company or person operating a horse-drawn carriage in the city shall obtain a separate horse-drawn carriage policy of indemnity insurance, except where such company or person actually owns or holds legal title to more than horse-drawn carriage, in which event such company or person may give one policy of indemnity insurance covering all the horse-drawn carriages who may be jointly operating or doing business under a licensed horse-drawn carriage name. 
(d)  Notice when policy of insurance is changed or voided . Before any policy of insurance required by this article is voided for any cause, nonpayment of premium or otherwise, notice thereof shall be given, in writing to the city clerk at least five days before the same shall take effect. Any change in the policy or insurer requires immediate notification in writing to the city clerk. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-5. - Chauffer's license. 
(a)  License required . No person shall operate a horse-drawn carriage for hire upon the streets of the city, and no person who owns or operates a horse-drawn carriage company shall permit a horse-drawn carriage to be driven, and no horse-drawn carriage operating under a horse-drawn carriage company approved by the city shall be driven at any time for hire, unless the driver of the horse-drawn carriage shall first have obtained and shall have then in force a chauffer's license issued under this article and a current motor vehicle operator's license issued by the state, except out of state students and military, and that the license is not under suspension or revocation. To that end, applicant must provide a recent motor vehicle operator record of convictions at the time of application. 
(b)  Examination of applicant; issuance or denial of license . It shall be the duty of the risk manager or his/her designee to examine the applicant, his/her reference, police and traffic record, and the other vouchers, and thereafter, to either grant or refuse the license. 
(c)  License to be displayed in horse-drawn carriage . The chauffer's license issued under the provisions of this article shall be placed on display in the horse-drawn carriage to be operated by the holder of the license, where the license will be in clear view of the passengers at all times when the horse-drawn carriage is for hire. 
(d)  Alteration of license prohibited . It shall be prohibited for any person to willfully alter, deface, obliterate, or destroy a chauffer's license, or cause or allow the same. 
(e)  License not transferable . Any chauffer's license issued under this article is not transferable, and is to be used solely by the person to whom it is issued and the company for which it is issued. 
(d)  Duration of license . The chauffer's license is $25.00 and is renewable on an annual basis effective on January 31 of each year. License may be renewed, upon presentation of a current motor vehicle record, physician's statement and criminal background investigation report or sworn statement, unless the license for the preceding period has been revoked or is under suspension. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-6. - Drug testing. 
    Each horse-drawn carriage company or operator shall establish and maintain a drug testing program for all employees in safety-sensitive positions, to include all drivers. The program shall include pre-employment, random, post-accident, and probable cause testing. Records of testing shall be maintained by the employer and shall be made available for inspection by the risk manager or his/her designee or any state or federal regulatory enforcement officials. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-7. - Vehicle requirements. 
(a)  Identification and marking generally . Every horse-drawn carriage shall have a permanent sign on the vehicle, either painted or adhesive-backed decals, containing the full name of the horse-drawn carriage company operating the vehicle. 
(b)  Safe mechanical condition of horse-drawn carriage required . Every horse-drawn carriage operated on the streets of the city shall be maintained in a safe mechanical condition, with all safety related equipment remaining intact and operable at all times when the horse-drawn carriage is in service. 
(c)  Carriage lubrication; wheels . Carriages must be kept properly lubricated and wheels must spin freely and straight. 
(d)  Cleanliness of horse-drawn carriage required . Each vehicle operating under this article shall be kept painted, and in a clean and sanitary condition, free of litter and debris and at all times suitable for public transportation of passengers. 
(e)  Vehicle inspection required . Each horse-drawn carriage shall be inspected by the risk manager or his/her designee for the compliance with the provision of the article and shall pass the inspection before the vehicle may be used as a horse-drawn carriage in the city. Periodic inspections will be required twice a year at a time and place as directed by the risk manager or his/her designee. Each horse-drawn carriage shall be subject to random inspections without notice to insure continued compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(f)  Rates of fare; rate posting required . No owner or driver of a horse-drawn carriage shall charge a greater sum for the use of the horse-drawn carriage than in accordance with rates authorized by the city. Rates shall be displayed so as to be conspicuous at the stand and/or on the vehicle. 
(g)  Safety equipment required . Each horse-drawn carriage shall be equipped with electrically powered lights or lanterns and reflectors which shall be in use when operating during the hours of darkness and when raining. The lights and reflectors shall be mounted so that they are visible from a distance of 500 feet in any direction. Reflective devices are to be worn by the horse. 
(h)  Brakes . Carriages are to be equipped with a working mechanical brake that will prevent movement when slowing, stopping, and parked. 
(i)  Slow-moving vehicle emblem . Each carriage shall be equipped with a rear-facing "slow-moving vehicle emblem" that can be seen from a minimum distance of 500 feet. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-8. - Requirements for animals in service. 
    Operating regulations . In addition to the business license imposed herein and by the business license ordinance, no license shall be permitted any carriage operator unless the operator complies with division II of the animal ordinance [Ch. 14] and the following regulations: 
(1)  A licensed veterinarian shall certify, after due and proper inspection, the good health of each draft animal before it is placed into service. A minimum of two such health inspections shall be required for each animal each calendar year; to be performed during the months of January and July with copies submitted to the city risk management department. 
(2)  No single animal shall pull a carriage holding more than ten people, including the driver. Two horses cannot pull more than the seating capacity of the carriage. 
(3)  Animals shall wear properly attached and fitted blinders while pulling carriages. 
(4)  Carriages shall not be pulled by stallions or pregnant mares. 
(5)  Unless written approval is given by a licensed veterinarian, no animal having open sores or wounds or any disease or ailment shall be permitted to be in service on the streets of the city. 
(6)  Each draft animal shall have its hooves properly trimmed and shod for street surfaces being maintained by a farrier at least every eight weeks, or as necessary. A record of farrier service shall be maintained for inspection. 
(7)  Temporary shoes can only be used if the horse has thrown a shoe during a tour and then only to get the horse back to the barn to be shoed. 
(8)  Each animal shall be groomed daily and not have fungus, dandruff or a dirty coat. 
(9)  Flies and other insects must be controlled through general sanitation and other necessary means. 
(10)  Harnesses shall be properly fitted, maintained and oiled so that no irritating material will come in direct contact with the animal. 
(11)  No driver may use more than a light touch of the whip upon any animal, and no driver or other person may forcefully strike an animal, or make movements or noise intended to frighten or harm an animal. No animal shall be made to perform by means of any prod, stick, electrical shock, physical force, or by causing pain or discomfort. 
(12)  No driver shall permit an animal to pull a carriage at a speed faster than a slow trot, except in emergency situations. 
(13)  No animal shall be subject to any condition or treatment, whether in service or out of service, which will impair the good health and physical condition of that animal. 
(14)  No animal shall be worked more than eight hours in any 24-hour period without ten minutes of rest for each 50 minutes of work and with a minimum of 12 consecutive hours of rest. 
(15)  Animals shall not be overridden or driven to overheating or exhaustion. 
(16)  The risk manager or his/her designee shall be empowered to inspect all stables and operating facilities of any carriage company without notices, and to examine operating practices of any carriage company to ensure continuous compliance with this article. 
(17)  Any applicant who refuses or fails to comply with the requirements of this article shall not be issued a business license until proof of compliance is presented by the applicant and certified by the risk manager. The foregoing licensing requirements shall be ongoing as requirements for continuous operation. 
(18)  The mayor may, upon recommendation of the risk manager or his/her designee, temporarily suspend a license or carriage company operation for violation of the provisions of this article, and may be subject to revocation action as provided by the business license ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-9. - Stands generally. 
(a)  No parking shall be permitted in the corporate limits of the city except at such stands as may be established by the city. Horse-drawn carriage stands shall be designated by signs. Fees for the use of the stands may be established by the mayor or his/her designee. 
(b)  Drivers of horse-drawn carriages operated under this article shall maintain stands in a sanitary condition at all times. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-10. - Driver requirements generally. 
(a)  Driver not to leave vehicle while waiting to be hired . It is prohibited for any driver of any horse-drawn carriage to leave the vehicle, or the immediate premises thereof, while the vehicle is parked while waiting to be hired. 
(b)  Use of alcohol or drugs . Any driver of any horse-drawn carriage is prohibited from consuming or being under the influence of alcohol or illegal drugs while operating a carriage, while waiting to operate a carriage or while on-duty generally. Use of prescription and over-the-counter drugs which affect the driver's ability to operate a horse-drawn carriage is prohibited during on-duty hours. 
(c)  Operation with animals under control . Due to the nature of operating animal-drawn vehicles in areas of congestion and heavy traffic within the city, it shall be prohibited to operate the animal-drawn vehicles except when the animals are under complete control at all times and shall be operated with extra caution and due care for the safety of others. 
(d)  Obeying traffic laws . The operation of the animal-drawn vehicles shall be in accordance with all state and local traffic laws and ordinances. Animal-drawn carriages shall be prohibited from stopping on any street for the purpose of loading or unloading passengers during the course of a tour, except when stopping to allow other vehicles to pass or pedestrians to cross unless directed to stop by a police officer. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-11. - Hours of operation. 
(a)  No horse-drawn carriage shall be operated on the city streets between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 8:30 a.m. on any day. No carriage shall be operated for hire between the hours of 4:30 p.m. and 6:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, except that such restriction shall not apply on legal holidays. 
(b)  When weather conditions are adverse or inclement which could harm either animals or passengers, carriages shall not be operated. 
(c)  While in motion, carriage lights must be lit from one-half hour before dusk until such time as night operations cease. Carriage lights shall be lit during inclement weather. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-12. - Sanitation requirements. 
(a)  Manure and urine must be immediately treated with a chemical deodorizing solution, and manure must be removed immediately from the street by the carriage company. 
(b)  Horse diapers or other sanitary devices, which prevent excrement from being deposited on the street surface, must be approved for efficiency by the risk manager or his/her designee. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-13. - Impediment of traffic flow. 
    It shall be prohibited for any animal-drawn carriage to willfully impede the normal flow of traffic on any city street, alley, or thoroughfare, at any time. Animal-drawn carriages will be required to pull immediately to the nearest curb area when one or more vehicles are unable to safely pass or continue in normal traffic flow. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-14. - Accidents. 
(a)  The driver of an animal-driven carriage shall report any accident involving such carriage to the police department at the time of the accident. 
(b)  No animal or carriage involved in an accident where structural damage to the carriage or injury to the animal has occurred shall be operated again until the carriage has been inspected by the risk manager or his/her designee and the horse has been certified for service by a veterinarian licensed in the state. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 23-15. - Safe operation required. 
(a)  Unsafe acts by the horse-drawn carriage driver and/or passengers are prohibited. 
(b)  The horse-drawn carriage company acknowledges that its drivers, property and operations shall be and remain subject at all times to such reasonable regulation by the city as is or may be necessary to protect the interests of the general public. 
(Ord. No. 2017-12 , 12-18-2017) 
Chapter 26 - CHARITABLE SOLICITATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 22. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 26-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Charitable or religious purpose means the use of money or property for the benefit of: 
(1)  Charity or philanthropy or underprivileged, needy, refugee, diseased, disabled or handicapped persons or persons in need of rehabilitation; 
(2)  A church, religious society or other religious sect, group or order; 
(3)  Patriotism, that is, for the teaching of patriotism or the relief or assistance of veterans or veterans' organizations; or 
(4)  Existing educational institutions or for the establishment or endowment of educational institutions or in aid of the education of any person or group of persons. 
    Conduct a solicitation means to manage, organize, direct, administer or be responsible for a solicitation on behalf of any person. 
    Cost of the solicitation means the amount of funds collected in excess of the amount spent for the direct benefit of the stated purpose of the solicitation, including but not limited to information materials and activities, recruitment, training and compensation of solicitors and management and administration of the solicitation and disbursement of the funds. 
    Funds spent for the direct benefit of the stated purpose of the solicitation means money expended directly for the specific purpose stated in the registration. 
    Solicit or solicitation means to request property, financial aid, money or anything of value; or to sell or offer to sell a product, article, tag, service, publication, document, advertising space, membership, subscription or ticket; or to hold, promote or participate in an entertainment, sports event, benefit dance, fair, bazaar or other type of organized social entertainment. 
(Code 1974, § 18-15) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 26-2. - Violation; penalties. 
    Any person who violates any provision of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 18-23) 
Sec. 26-3. - Purpose; intent. 
    The regulations and prohibitions set forth in this chapter are necessary for the legitimate governmental interest in protecting citizens from fraud, through the registration and identification procedure, and from undue interference from strangers importuning citizens in their homes after dark and during the early morning hours. The city council recognizes that these regulations operate to restrain First Amendment rights but determines that such restraints are reasonable and necessary for the protection set forth in this section. 
(Code 1974, § 18-14) 
Sec. 26-4. - Hours for soliciting. 
(a)  No person shall solicit by door-to-door or telephone canvass at the place of residence of anyone from whom a solicitation is sought or within a residential neighborhood later than 9:00 p.m. or earlier than 9:00 a.m., unless the solicitor has prior approval therefor from such resident. 
(b)  This section does not apply to the following: 
(1)  A person who solicits solely from its own membership or from foundations. 
(2)  A person who solicits solely through the use of the public broadcasting media. 
(3)  United Way. 
(Code 1974, § 18-19) 
Sec. 26-5. - Receipts for contributions. 
    Any solicitor receiving money or anything having a value of $10.00 or more from any contributor shall give the contributor a written receipt containing the name and authorization number of the soliciting organization and the name of the solicitor signed on the receipt, the date, the amount received and the portion of the contribution which is tax deductible. 
(Code 1974, § 18-20) 
Sec. 26-6. - Financial reports; availability of records. 
(a)  Every person authorized to conduct a solicitation under this chapter shall file a financial report under oath with the city clerk/treasurer within 30 days after the solicitation has been completed. 
(b)  The report shall state in detail the amount of funds collected, the cost of any tangible property given to contributors, the expenses incurred in management and administration of the solicitation and the distribution of the balance of the funds collected. 
(c)  The report shall state the name, address and social security number of each person receiving any wages, fees, commissions or expenses either independently from or based on the funds collected. 
(d)  All books, records and papers relating to the solicitation shall be available to the city clerk/treasurer at the city hall upon written request to the person authorized to conduct the solicitation. 
(Code 1974, § 18-22) 
Secs. 26-7-26-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - REGISTRATION 

Sec. 26-31. - Required. 
(a)  No person shall solicit or conduct a solicitation within the boundaries of the city on the plea or representation, express or implied, that the proceeds from the solicitation are for a charitable or religious purpose, unless the person is properly registered with the city and is prominently displaying identification provided by this article. 
(b)  This section does not apply to the following: 
(1)  A person who solicits solely from its own membership or from foundations. 
(2)  A person who solicits solely through the use of the public broadcasting media. 
(3)  United Way. 
(Code 1974, § 18-16) 
Sec. 26-32. - Procedure; issuance of identification badge. 
(a)  Registration shall be complete when the person seeking to solicit or conduct a solicitation pays the registration fee and files with the city clerk/treasurer the following information under oath, on forms furnished or approved by the city: 
(1)  The name, local and permanent address, and telephone number and headquarters of the person registering. 
(2)  If the registrant is not an individual, the names and addresses of the registrant's principal officers and managers and a copy of the resolution, if any, authorizing such solicitation, certified as a true and correct copy of the original by the officer having charge of the registrant's records. 
(3)  The purpose for which such solicitation is to be made, the total amount of funds proposed to be raised thereby and the use or disposition to be made of any receipts therefrom. 
(4)  The names and addresses and official positions of the persons by whom the receipts of such solicitations shall be disbursed for the stated purpose. 
(5)  The name, address and telephone number of the person who will be in direct charge of conducting the solicitation and the names and addresses of all promoters connected or to be connected with the proposed solicitation. 
(6)  An outline of the method to be used in conducting the solicitation. 
(7)  The time when such solicitations shall be made, giving the preferred dates for the beginning and ending of such solicitations, and, if such period shall exceed 30 days, the specific reasons for the need of such excess time. 
(8)  The estimated cost of the solicitation. 
(9)  The amount of any wages, fees, commissions, expenses or emoluments to be expended or paid to any person in connection with such solicitations and the names, addresses and social security numbers of all individual solicitors to be used in the solicitation. 
(10)  A financial statement for the last preceding fiscal year of any funds collected for charitable purposes by the registrant within the city, such statement giving the amount of money so raised, together with the cost of raising it and the final distribution thereof. 
(11)  A full statement of the character and extent of the charitable work being done by the registrant within the city. 
(b)  Upon receipt of the information required by subsection (a) of this section, the city clerk/treasurer shall designate and approve an identification badge containing the name of the organization conducting the solicitations, the name or photograph of the authorized solicitor, the purpose of the solicitation and an authorization number. The identification badge shall be nontransferable, valid only during the period of the solicitation and shall in no way constitute an approval by the city of the purpose of the solicitation. Each solicitor shall display this identification badge in a prominent position on the outer clothing, clearly visible to the person from whom solicitations are sought. The identification badge shall be provided at the expense of the solicitor. 
(Code 1974, § 18-17) 
Sec. 26-33. - Investigation; revocation. 
(a)  Following registration to solicit under this article, the city clerk/treasurer shall forthwith submit the registration information to the chief of police or his designated agent for investigation into the truth and accuracy of the registrant and a preliminary determination of whether the registrant qualifies as an approved solicitor. 
(b)  If the police chief determines that the registrant is in accordance with the standards set forth in this article, no further action shall be taken. If the police chief makes a preliminary determination that the registrant does not so qualify or has materially violated a provision of this article or has made a material misstatement of fact in his registration information, he shall so notify the registrant in writing, giving his reasons therefor and advising the registrant of the next regular city council meeting, not sooner than four days after mailing of the notice, at which time the questions of revocation of the registration shall be on the council agenda and all interested parties heard for the city council to determine whether the registrant qualifies as a solicitor under this article or whether such registration should be revoked, suspended or modified. Misstatements of material fact which could mislead the police are grounds for revocation. The decision of the city council shall be final. 
(Code 1974, § 18-18) 
Chapter 30 - CIVIL EMERGENCIES 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 30-1-30-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MAYOR'S EMERGENCY POWERS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Mayor, § 2-151 et seq.; offenses against public peace, order, and safety, § 66-21 et seq. 
State Law reference- Authority of mayor to close certain places in case of riot, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-82. 

Sec. 30-26. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Civil emergency means: 
(1)  A riot or unlawful assembly characterized by the use of actual force or violence or any threat to use force if accompanied by immediate power to execute by three or more persons acting together without authority of law. 
(2)  Any natural disaster or manmade calamity including a flood, conflagration, cyclone, tornado, earthquake or explosion within the corporate limits of the city resulting in the death or injury of persons or the destruction of property to such an extent that extraordinary measures must be taken to protect the public health, safety and welfare. 
    Curfew means a prohibition against any person from walking, running, loitering, standing or motoring upon any alley, street, highway, public property or vacant premises within the corporate limits of the city, excepting persons officially designated to duty with reference to the civil emergency. 
(Code 1974, § 9-36) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 30-27. - Proclamation. 
    When in the judgment of the mayor a civil emergency is deemed to exist, he shall forthwith proclaim in writing the existence of the emergency. Such a proclamation shall be effective for five days unless extended by the council. 
(Code 1974, § 9-37) 
Sec. 30-28. - Order of curfew following proclamation. 
    After proclamation of a civil emergency by the mayor and while the emergency is in effect, he may order a general curfew applicable to such geographical areas of the city or to the city as a whole as he deems advisable, and the curfew shall be applicable during such hours of the day or night as he deems necessary in the interest of the public safety and welfare. 
(Code 1974, § 9-38) 
Sec. 30-29. - Orders authorized after proclamation. 
    After proclamation of a civil emergency and while the emergency is in effect, the mayor may also in the interest of public safety and welfare make any or all of the following orders: 
(1)  Order the closing of all retail liquor stores. 
(2)  Order the closing of all beer taverns. 
(3)  Order the closing of all private clubs or portions thereof wherein the consumption of intoxicating liquor or beer is permitted. 
(4)  Order the discontinuance of the sale of beer. 
(5)  Order the discontinuance of selling, distributing or giving away gasoline or other liquid flammable or combustible products in any container, other than a gasoline tank properly affixed to a motor vehicle. 
(6)  Order the closing of gasoline stations and other establishments, the chief activity of which is the sale, distribution or dispensing of liquid flammable or combustible products. 
(7)  Order the discontinuance of selling, distributing, dispensing or giving away of any firearms or ammunition of any character whatsoever. 
(8)  Order the closing of any or all establishments or portions thereof, the chief activity of which is the sale, distribution, dispensing or giving away of firearms or ammunition. 
(9)  Issue such other orders as are imminently necessary for the protection of life and property. 
(Code 1974, § 9-39) 
Sec. 30-30. - Violations; penalty. 
    Any person found guilty of violating any provision of this article or any executive order issued by the mayor pursuant to the authority contained in this article shall be guilty of an offense against the city and shall be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 9-40)

ARTICLE II. - MUNICIPAL COURT[1]

    Upon each conviction in municipal court for a violation of any ordinance of the city, there shall be taxed against the defendant as court costs the sum of $10.00, and there shall also be taxed as costs the additional costs and fees imposed by state law, and the latter such costs and fees shall be remitted pursuant to the statutes. All costs taxed for the city shall be paid into the city treasury. 
(Code 1974, § 10-23(d))

Sec. 34-47. - Special court costs and fees. 
(a)  An additional municipal court cost of $28.00 and fees shall be added to each municipal court traffic case with the exception of DUI, which shall carry a court cost of $53.00 and fees; and $83.00 and fees shall be added to each municipal court non-traffic case in Eufaula Municipal Court, and a witness subpoena fee of $8.00. 
(b)  An account shall be established to be known as the City of Eufaula Corrections Fund, and the all proceeds from this court cost and fees shall be deposited into this fund. 
(c)  The funds contained in the corrections fund shall be expended only as needed for the operation and maintenance of the Eufaula Municipal Jail or Eufaula Municipal Court, or any other city correctional facility established after July 6, 1999. 
(Ord. No. 1999-8, §§ 1-3, 7-6-99) 
ARTICLE III. - PRETRIAL DIVERSION PROGRAM 

Sec. 34-48. - In general. 
(a)  Pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-90, The City of Eufaula, Alabama may establish a pretrial diversion program. 
(b)  All discretionary powers endowed by common law and provided by statutes and acts of this state or powers or discretion otherwise provided by law for the city shall be retained. 
(c)  The pretrial diversion program shall be under the direct supervision and control of the presiding judge for the municipality pursuant to any rules and regulations established by the city council. The municipal judge, with approval of the city council and the city prosecutor, may contract with any agency, person, or corporation for services related to this act. The city may employ necessary persons to accomplish this act and those persons shall serve at the pleasure of the city. 
(d)  The presiding municipal judge, acting in consultation with the municipal prosecutor, shall have the authority to establish all rules and terms necessary for the implementation of a pretrial diversion program. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-49. - Definitions. 
    For the purposes of this act, the following terms shall have the following meanings: 
    Application fee means a one-time administrative fee imposed by the city as a condition precedent to participation in a pretrial diversion program. 
    City prosecutor means the prosecutor appointed by the city council or any legal staff employed by the city prosecutor. 
    Law enforcement as defined in Code of Ala. 1975, § 41-8A-1(1). 
    Law enforcement officer as defined in Code of Ala. 1975, § 36-25-1(15) whether employed in the State of Alabama or elsewhere. 
    Offender means any person charged with a criminal offense, including, but not limited to, any misdemeanor, violation, or traffic offense, as defined by the Code of Alabama 1975, which was allegedly committed in the corporate limits or police jurisdiction of the city. 
    Pretrial diversion program or program means a program that allows the imposition of the city or by a designated agency of certain conditions of behavior and conduct for a specified period of time upon an offender which allow the offender to have his or her charges reduced, dismissed without prejudice, or otherwise mitigated should all of the conditions be met during the time frame set by the city prosecutor. 
    Serious physical injury as defined in Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-1-2(14). 
    Supervision fee means any fee other than the application fee imposed by any agency providing supervision of treatment of the offender. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-50. - Participation. 
(a)  An offender may apply to the court for admittance into the pretrial diversion program. Admittance into the pretrial diversion program is in the sole discretion of the municipal court judge. Upon receipt of the application and recommendation of the city prosecutor, the judge shall determine whether to grant the individual admittance to the program. An offender deemed by the municipal judge or the city prosecutor to be a threat to the safety or well-being of the community shall not be eligible for the program. 
(b)  An offender charged with any of the following types of offenses shall be ineligible for admittance: 
(1)  Any offense involving violence or aggression resulting in injury to a law enforcement officer. 
(2)  Any offense involving eluding or attempting to elude a law enforcement officer. 
(3)  Any offense involving violence where weapons are used or where children are victims. 
(4)  Any driving under the influence charge where serious physical injuries are involved. 
(5)  Any offense wherein the offender is a public official and the charge is related to the capacity of the offender as a public official. 
(6)  The person may not hold a commercial driver license (CDL) issued in any U.S. state, and U.S. possession, any U.S. territory, or any U.S. insular area, or has no conviction for which a commercial driver license was required. 
(c)  The city judge may consider an offender for the pretrial diversion program based on any of the following circumstances: 
(1)  There is a probability justice will be served if the offender is placed in the program. 
(2)  It is determined that the needs of the state, city, and of the offender can be met through the program. 
(3)  The offender appears to pose no substantial threat to the safety and well-being of the community. 
(4)  It appears the offender is not likely to be involved in further criminal activity if the offender complies with all conditions imposed pursuant to the program. 
(5)  The offender will likely respond to rehabilitative treatment or counseling. 
(6)  The need for restitution for the victim from the offender outweighs the interest of the state and city for incarceration of the offender. 
(7)  The city judge may waive any of the standards specified in this subsection (c) if just or special circumstances dictate. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-51. - Requirements. 
(a)  A recommendation by the city prosecutor is required for participation in the pretrial diversion program. Upon application by an offender for admission into the pretrial diversion program, and prior to admission thereto and as a part of the evaluation process of the city prosecutor, the city prosecutor may require the offender to furnish information concerning past criminal history, education history, work record, family history, medical or psychiatric treatment or care prescribed or received, psychological test taken, and any other information concerning the offender which the city prosecutor believes has a bearing on the decision whether or not the offender should be admitted to the program. 
(b)  The city prosecutor may require the offender to submit to any type of test or evaluation process or interview the city prosecutor deems appropriate in evaluating the offender for admittance into the program. The costs of any test or evaluation shall be paid by the offender or as otherwise agreed to or provided for by this act. The offender shall provide the city prosecutor written consent to allow the city prosecutor to receive any educational, work, medical, psychiatric, psychological, or other records deemed necessary by the city prosecutor for the evaluation process. 
(c)  Following the decision of the city judge to admit the offender into the pretrial diversion program, but prior to entry, the city prosecutor and the offender shall enter into a written agreement stating the conditions of the participation of the offender in the program. The agreement shall include, but not be limited to, all of the following: 
(1)  A voluntary waiver of the right of the offender to a speedy trial. 
(2)  An agreement to the tolling, while in the program of periods of limitations established by statutes or rules of court. 
(3)  An agreement to the conditions of the program established by the city prosecutor. 
(4)  If there is a victim of the charged crime, an agreement to the restitution repayment within a specified period of time and in an amount to be determined by the city prosecutor taking into account circumstances of the offender and the victim. 
(5)  A waiver in writing of the right of the offender to a jury trial. 
(6)  A truthful and complete statement by the offender as to the involvement of the offender in the offense charged, which statement shall be admissible in any criminal trial. 
(7)  Submission of a written plea of guilty to the offense or offenses charged or agreed upon included offenses, together with an agreement as to whether the case is to be dismissed upon successful completion of the program, and an agreement, if there be any, as to the recommended sentence should a sentence be imposed. 
(d)  In addition to those requirements set forth in subsection (c) of this section, or as a condition of continued participation in the program, the city prosecutor may require the offender to agree to any of the following terms or conditions: 
(1)  To participate in substance abuse treatment. 
(2)  To participate in an education setting to include, but not limited to, K-12, college, job training, trade school, GED classes, or basic education courses. 
(3)  If appropriate, to attempt to learn to read and write the English language. 
(4)  To financially support his or her children or pay any court ordered child support. 
(5)  To refrain from the use of drugs or alcohol or frequenting places where drugs or alcohol are sold or used. 
(6)  To not commit any criminal offense. 
(7)  To refrain from contact with certain named persons or premises. 
(8)  To maintain or seek employment. 
(9)  To not leave the state without prior written consent of the city prosecutor or supervision agency or personnel. 
(10)  To maintain a residence approved by the city prosecutor or supervising agency or personnel. 
(11)  To attend individual, group, financial, chemical addiction, family, mental health, sex offender, or anger management counseling. 
(12)  To pay all court costs, fees, fines, and worthless checks, and obey any other lawful court order associated with the offense or offenses for which the offender has entered the program, or any other case. 
(13)  To refrain from the possession or use of any deadly weapon or dangerous instrument as defined in Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-1-2. 
(14)  To pay supervision fees and application fees pursuant to this act. 
(15)  To observe curfews or home detention or travel constraints as set out in agreement signed by the offender. 
(16)  To have restitution, court costs, fees, child support, and any other moneys withheld or garnished from the wages or salary of the offender or withheld from any Alabama income tax due the offender, or from any available insurance policy, or forfeited from any other real or personal property of the offender, and applied to the above. 
(17)  To be admitted to a drug or alcohol treatment program on an inpatient or outpatient basis or receive other treatment alternatives for substance abuse. 
(18)  To submit to periodic or random drug testing as part of the program and other terms and conditions related to substance abuse as the city prosecutor may direct. 
(19)  To waive in writing the right of the offender to a probation hearing in the event of termination or withdrawal from the program. 
(20)  To any other terms or conditions as the city prosecutor or his or her designee and the offender may agree to in the above-stated agreement, it being the purpose of this act to allow the city prosecutor broad discretion in designing a program specifically for each offender and his or her particular circumstances. 
(21)  When applicable, to be required to pay supervision fees to the agency or entity responsible for monitoring and verifying the compliance of the offender with the terms of the program set forth by the city prosecutor. The fees shall be paid by the offender to the supervising entity in a timely manner. 
(22)  Community service with an approved community service, charitable or nonprofit organization. The prosecutor shall compile a list of approved organizations for each participant. Participants who wish to complete this requirement with an organization not on the prosecutor's list must have any such organization preapproved by the prosecutor. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-52. - Fees. 
(a)  An offender may be assessed a nonrefundable application fee when the offender is approved for the pretrial diversion program. The amount of the assessment for participation in the program shall be in addition to any court costs, fees, and assessments for the crime victim's compensation fund, department of forensic sciences assessments, drug, alcohol, or anger management treatment required by law, and any costs of supervision, treatment, and restitution for which the offender may be responsible. The offender will be assessed a $7.00 fee for the creation, maintenance, and administration of the pretrial diversion database which shall be remitted to the Office of Prosecution Services in Montgomery, Alabama within 30 days of entry of the offender into the pretrial diversion program. A schedule of payments for any of these fees may be established by the city prosecutor. 
(b)  The following maximum applications fees shall be applied to offenders accepted in the program: 
(1)  Driving under the influence offenses (DUI), up to $2,500.00; 
(2)  Domestic violence offenses up to $1,000.00; 
(3)  Other misdemeanor offenses up to $500.00; 
(4)  Traffic offenses not including DUI up to $350.00; 
(5)  Violations up to $100.00. 
(c)  The amount of the application fee for each offender shall be established by the city prosecutor and approved by the municipal court judge. 
(d)  All fees assessed and collected by the pretrial diversion program shall be allocated to the general fund of the city to defray the administration costs of the program and for use for any other municipal purpose. 
(e)  An applicant offender may not be denied access into the pretrial diversion program based solely on the inability of the offender to pay the application fee. Application fees may be reduced, but not waived, for just cause, including indigency of the offender, at the discretion of the city. Any determination of the indigency of the offender for purposes of program fee mitigation shall be made by the city but such mitigation shall be done only upon the determination by the city that there is no reasonable likelihood within the reasonably foreseeable future that the offender will have the ability to pay the application fee. 
(f)  Application fees required by this act shall be collected by the court clerk of the city municipal court. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-53. - Approval of the court. 
(a)  Upon acceptance of an offender into the pretrial diversion program by the city prosecutor, the city prosecutor and the offender shall submit the written application of the offender together with the statement of facts of the offender, the acceptance of the offender by the city prosecutor, and the agreement between the city prosecutor and the offender to the court presiding over the affected case of the offender for the approval of the court. The offender shall also enter a plea of guilty to the charge or charges involved. If the court rejects the agreement and guilty plea, any money paid by the offender in satisfaction of the application fee shall be refunded to the offender. The offender shall still be liable for any actual expenses already incurred by the city prosecutor or any agency or service provider in furtherance of the application and evaluation process and the same will be deducted from any money so refunded to the offender. 
(b)  Upon approval of the agreement and acceptance of the guilty plea, the court shall expressly retain jurisdiction of the case, any other provision of law notwithstanding, any may withdraw and file the case or otherwise place it on an administrative docket until such time as the court has been notified that the offender has fulfilled the terms of the agreement, has been terminated from the program, or otherwise withdrawn from the program. Imposition of punishment by the court shall be deferred until the offender has successfully completed the program or is terminated from the program. 
(c)  In the event the offender is terminated from the program, the court shall impose appropriate punishment in the same manner as with any plea of guilty or finding of guilty and shall not be bound by the terms of agreement as to what punishment to impose. 
(d)  Upon successful completion of the program by the offender, the city prosecutor shall notify the court in writing of that fact together with a request that the court enter an order of disposition of the case pursuant to the agreement between the offender and the city prosecutor. 
(e)  Regardless of whether the offender successfully completes the program or withdraws from or is terminated from the program, the offender will still be liable for and required to pay any and all court costs and fees, restitution, victim's compensation fund assessment, and any and all other fees and assessments, in the same manner as if the offender had not applied for entry into the program and had been found guilty of the offense or offense involved. No costs, fees, restitution, or assessments shall be waived or remitted, absent an express agreement to that effect between the city prosecutor and the offender, without a finding by the court that the offender does not have the reasonable ability to pay the same within the reasonably foreseeable future. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-54. - Violations. 
(a)  After any violation of any program terms or conditions or upon any breach of any program agreement by the offender, the city prosecutor may do any of the following: 
(1)  Continue the agreement with or without modification. 
(2)  Terminate the offender from the pretrial diversion program. 
(3)  Require the offender to adopt a new agreement as a condition of continued participation. 
(b)  The city prosecutor may waive a violation for good cause shown why the offender should stay in the program. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-55. - Liability. 
(a)  The city, or its officers or employees, shall have no liability, criminal or civil, for any injury or harm to the offender while the offender is a participant in any pretrial diversion program administered pursuant to this article. The city prosecutor may require written agreed upon waivers of liability as a prerequisite for admittance into the pretrial diversion program. 
(b)  Absent wantonness, gross negligence, or intentional misconduct, the city, or its officers or employees, shall have no liability, criminal or civil, for the conduct of any offender while participating in the pretrial diversion program or of any service provider or its agents that are contracted to or who have agreed to provide services to the pretrial diversion program. 
(c)  The city judge, or his or her staff shall have no liability, criminal or civil, for any injury or harm to the offender while the offender is a participant in any pretrial diversion program administered pursuant to this article. The city prosecutor may require written agreed upon waivers of liability as a prerequisite for admittance into the pretrial diversion program. 
(d)  Absent wantonness, gross negligence, or intentional misconduct, the city judge, or his or her staff, shall have no liability, criminal or civil, for the conduct of any offender while participating in the pretrial diversion program or of any service provider or its agents that are contracted to or who have agreed to provide services to the pretrial diversion program. 
(e)  The city prosecutor, or his or her staff shall have no liability, criminal or civil, for any injury or harm to the offender while the offender is a participant in any pretrial diversion program administered pursuant to this article. The city prosecutor may require written agreed upon waivers of liability as a prerequisite for admittance into the pretrial diversion program. 
(f)  Absent wantonness, gross negligence, or intentional misconduct, the city prosecutor, or his or her staff, shall have no liability, criminal or civil, for the conduct of any offender while participating in the pretrial diversion program or of any service provider or its agents that are contracted to or who have agreed to provide services to the pretrial diversion program. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Sec. 34-56. - Severability. 
    This program is established pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-90. The provisions of this act are severable. If any part of this act is declared invalid or unconstitutional, that declaration shall not affect the part which remains. 
(Ord. No. 2014-1, § 1, 1-21-14 ) 
Chapter 38 - ELECTIONS[1] 
  

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- City council, § 2-31 et seq.; mayor, § 2-151 et seq. 
State Law reference- Municipal elections, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-46-1 et seq. 

Sec. 38-1. - Compliance with state law. 
    General municipal elections held in the city shall be conducted pursuant to the provisions of state law. 
(Code 1974, § 11-1) 
Sec. 38-2. - Single-member council districts designated. 
(a)  The city is divided into five single-member council districts to be designated as District 1, District 2, District 3, District 4 and District 5. 
(b)  The redistricting plan, as approved by the U.S. Department of Justice on February 29, 2012, is hereby adopted as the City of Eufaula Voting District Plan. 
(Ord. No. 1992-7, §§ I, II, 5-20-92; Ord. No. 2012-2, §§ I-III, 5-7-2012) 
Editor's note- Legal descriptions of the five districts are not set out herein, but are on file with the city. 
State Law reference- Single-member districts authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-63. 
Sec. 38-3. - Election of councilmembers; terms of office. 
    At the municipal election in 1988 and every four years thereafter, the qualified electors in each of the districts of the city who are entitled to participate in such election shall elect one councilmember to the city council for the district. Each councilmember so elected shall be a bona fide elector of and must actually reside in the district of his qualification and election. Each such councilmember shall hold office for a period of four years and until his successor shall be elected and qualified or until such councilmember shall resign, die, move his residence outside of the district or otherwise be removed from office. 
(Code 1974, § 11-3) 
State Law reference- Elections by district, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-63. 
Sec. 38-4. - Election of mayor; term of office. 
    At the municipal election to be held in 1988 and each four years thereafter, the qualified electors of the city, at large, who are entitled to participate in such election shall elect a mayor who must be a bona fide elector of and must actually reside in the city limits. The mayor shall hold such office for a period of four years and until his successor shall be duly elected and qualified or until the mayor shall resign, die, move his residence outside the city limits or otherwise be removed from office. 
(Code 1974, § 11-4) 
Sec. 38-5. - Qualifying fee. 
(a)  A qualification fee in the amount of $50.00 is fixed and imposed upon all candidates seeking election as mayor of the city, except as provided in this section. 
(b)  A qualification fee in the amount of $50.00 is fixed and imposed upon all candidates seeking election as councilmember of the city, except as provided in this section. 
(c)  Such qualification fee shall be paid to the city clerk and deposited to the general fund of the city at or prior to the time of taking out qualification papers by any such candidates. 
(d)  Any person desiring to qualify who is not financially able to pay the required fee may qualify, provided such prospective candidate furnishes the clerk with an affidavit stating that he is financially unable to pay the required fee fixed by this section. 
(Ord. No. 1992-8, §§ 1-4, 6-1-92; Ord. No. 1996-9, §§ 1-4, 6-21-96) 
State Law reference- Authority to set qualifying fee, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-46-2. 
Chapter 42 - FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 42-1. - Fire hydrants-Use and maintenance. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to use any of the fire hydrants of the city except the city firefighters or employees of the waterworks and sewer board or the city's officers and employees. It shall be the duty of the waterworks and sewer board to maintain public fire hydrants from cutoff valves to and including hydrants. Maintenance shall be done in accordance with the International Fire Code, 2006 Edition. 
(Code 1974, § 12-13; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
Sec. 42-2. - Same-Obstructing. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place any building material or any other obstruction whatever within 15 feet of any public fire hydrant, and any person so offending shall, on conviction thereof, be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 12-14) 
Sec. 42-3. - Fire district. 
    The territory of the city within the following boundaries shall be known and designated as the fire district: 
     Begin at the northwest corner of the intersection of Barbour Street and Livingston Street; run thence west along the north side of Barbour Street to a point 250 feet west of the northwest corner of the intersection of Barbour Street and Eufaula Street; run thence north to a point 250 feet north of Broad Street and 250 feet west of Eufaula Street; run thence east to the east side of Eufaula Street; run thence north along the east side of Eufaula Street to the southwest corner of St. James Street; run thence east along the south side of St. James Street to the east side of Randolph Street; run thence south along the east side of Randolph Street to the southwest corner of Church Street; run thence east along the south side of Church Street to the west side of Orange Street; run thence south along the west side of Orange Street to the south side of an alley running bewteen Church Street and Broad Street; run thence east to the west side of Livingston Street; run thence south to the point of beginning. 
(Code 1974, § 8-1) 
Note- Formerly § 18-33. 
Secs. 42-4-42-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FIRE DEPARTMENT[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2. 
State Law reference- Fire departments, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-140 et seq. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 42-31. - Established. 
    There is created and established a fire department which shall consist of a chief, captains, lieutenants, fire medics, engineers and fire fighters in a number of positions as authorized and designated by the city council. 
(Code 1974, § 12-1; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
State Law reference- Fire department authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-140. 
Sec. 42-32. - Fire chief's appointment, term and qualifications. 
    The fire chief shall be elected by the council at its first regular meeting in October of each year, and his term of office shall be for one year and until his successor is elected and qualified. The fire chief must have the qualifications of both an emergency medical technician (EMT) and a firefighter. 
Sec. 42-33. - Duties. 
    The fire department shall be charged with preventing fires within the corporate city limits and with the detecting, combating and extinguishing of fires when the fires occur and with the protection of property and persons against damage and accident incident to such fires. 
(Code 1974, § 12-2; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
Sec. 42-34. - Powers and duties of chief. 
(a)  The chief of the fire department shall have general command, supervision and control of the fire department. When answering fire alarms he shall have sole direction of the operations of the department. He shall locate the apparatus and firefighters as they arrive, and they shall render such service as he may designate. All members and employees of the department shall give strict obedience to his orders. He shall have authority, subject to the approval of the city council, to make such rules and regulations for the management of the department as may be necessary to promote the efficiency of the department and protect the city against fire. 
(Code 1974, § 12-3; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
State Law reference- Designation of chief of fire department by city council, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-43-5. 
Sec. 42-35. - Substitutes for chief. 
    In case of the absence of the chief of the fire department from a fire, the ranking officer at the fire shall be in command and shall exercise the power and authority of the chief at such fire. 
(Code 1974, § 12-6; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2008-7, adopted October 20, 2008, changed the title of section 42-35 from "Substitutes for chief or assistants at fires" to read as herein set out. 
Sec. 42-36. - Inspection of hydrants and water pressure. 
    The waterworks and sewer board shall be responsible for an annual inspection and on-going maintenance of fire hydrants within the city. They will see that hydrants are kept in good order and are ready for instant use. They will notify the fire department in the event that there is a deficiency in the system such as a hydrant being out of service. The water distribution system shall be maintained in accordance with the International Fire Code 2006. 
(Code 1974, § 12-7; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
Sec. 42-37. - Duties of firefighters at fire. 
    Firefighters may give such orders at the scene of a fire as are necessary to preserve public peace and safety, expedite extinguishment of the fire and safeguard property. 
(Code 1974, § 12-10) 
Sec. 42-38. - Duty of citizens to assist at fires. 
    The chief of the fire department or the ranking officer may at any fire command such assistance from the inhabitants of the city for the extinguishment of fires and the preservation of order thereat as may be necessary, and any person refusing to comply with such orders for assistance shall be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 12-8) 
Sec. 42-39. - Clearing bystanders from vicinity of fires. 
    The chief of the fire department or the ranking officer may at all fires order a space to be cleared of all persons to such a distance around the building or fire or from the vicinity thereof as may be necessary in his judgment to the efficient working of the fire department or to the safety of bystanders, and any person other than the owner or occupant of or person interested in the property on fire who shall fail or refuse to obey such order shall, on conviction thereof, be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 12-9) 
Sec. 42-40. - Riding on apparatus. 
    No person, without authorization of the chief of the fire department, shall ride on the apparatus of the fire department in going to or returning from a fire. 
(Code 1974, § 12-11) 
Sec. 42-41. - Exploding fireworks, firecrackers, etc., prohibited; exception. 
    The possession, firing, or exploding in the city limits of fireworks, firecrackers, roman candles, bombs, torpedoes. and any and all other devices or instruments of like kind and description is hereby prohibited, except in a public display or special event with a demonstration or display of fireworks under proper fire department supervision after application made to and permit issued by the fire department and the mayor of the City of Eufaula and specifically authorized by the city council. Fireworks used, possessed, displayed, or sold in violation of this section shall be subject to seizure and destruction in addition to the provisions of section 1-6. 
(Ord. No. 2003-3, 4-21-03; Ord. No. 2017-11 , 12-18-2017) 
Sec. 42-42. - Sale of fireworks, firecrackers, etc., prohibited. 
    The sale or keeping for sale within the city limits of Eufaula, Alabama of fireworks, firecrackers, roman candles, bombs, torpedoes and any and all other devices or instruments of like kind and description is hereby prohibited. 
(Ord. No. 2003-3, 4-21-03) 
Secs. 42-43-42-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - RESCUE SQUAD 

Sec. 42-51. - Purpose. 
    The rescue squad of the city, as provided for in this article, is declared to be carrying on a governmental function in the carrying out of its duties in the transporting of and rendering medical assistance to persons who are wounded, injured, killed or sick. 
(Code 1974, § 12-67) 
Sec. 42-52. - Created; composition; term. 
    There is created the city rescue squad, to consist of as many members as meets the required qualifications for membership, each of whom is to serve for an indefinite term so long as such member abides by the rules and regulations set by the board of directors of the rescue squad. 
(Code 1974, § 12-68; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
Sec. 42-53. - Board of directors-Composition; meetings; election of officers. 
    There shall be a board of directors of the rescue squad of seven members to assist in the establishment of rules, regulations and standards necessary to carry out the provisions of this article. The board shall meet at least two times each year and at the call of the fire chief. The fire chief shall be an ex officio member of the board. The members of the board shall annually elect one of its members to serve as chairman, one as vice-chairman and one as secretary. 
(Code 1974, § 12-69) 
Cross reference- Boards, commissions, and authority, § 2-241 et seq. 
Sec. 42-54. - Same-Appointment; terms of service; qualifications. 
(a)  The board of directors of the rescue squad shall be appointed by the city council and shall serve three-year staggered terms. 
(b)  Four members of the board shall be persons having special or professional qualifications in the provision of health care, disaster or civil preparedness or special or professional expertise in the area of financial management or accounting; three members shall be appointed from the community at large. 
(Code 1974, § 12-70) 
Sec. 42-55. - Same-Promulgation of rules and regulations. 
    The board of directors of the rescue squad so selected shall make such rules and regulations regarding the selection of new members and the method of operation of the organization as it shall see fit, subject to the approval of the city council. The board shall have the authority to employ such persons as may be required to carry on the business of the squad, subject to the approval of the council. 
(Code 1974, § 12-71) 
Sec. 42-56. - Division of fire department; cooperation with other agencies; employment, compensation by city; funding by city; fees. 
(a)  The rescue squad shall be a division of the city fire department and under the direction and supervision of the fire chief. The rescue squad shall at all times cooperate with the fire chief and the firefighting division of the fire department and with the police department and with all other law enforcement departments of the county and state governing the carrying on of its work. 
(b)  When a member of the rescue squad is pressed into public service, he shall be deemed to be an employee of the rescue squad until such functions have been completed. Members of the rescue squad shall be compensated by the rescue squad. 
(c)  The rescue squad is authorized to charge fees for its services as per a schedule approved by the board of directors. 
(Code 1974, § 12-72; Ord. No. 2008-7, 10-20-08) 
Secs. 42-57-42-75. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - FIRE PREVENTION CODE[2] 

Footnotes:

Sec. 42-76. - Adopted. 
(a)  The International Fire Code, 2006 edition, [and the International Fire Code, 2006 edition, Appendices A-G] published by the International Code Council, LLC, of which not less than three copies are filed in the office of the city clerk/treasurer, is fully adopted and incorporated in this section as fully set forth at length in this section.

    Wherever the word "municipality" is used in the fire prevention code adopted in this article, it shall be held to mean the city, a municipal corporation.

Sec. 42-79. - Violations; penalties; failure to comply. 
109.3 Violation penalties. Persons who shall violate a provision of this code or shall fail to comply with any of the requirements thereof or who shall erect, install, alter, repair or do work in violation of the approved construction documents or directive of the fire code official, or of a permit or certificate used under provisions of this code, shall be guilty of a Misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of not more than $500.00 dollars or by imprisonment not exceeding 6 months, or both such fine and imprisonment. Each day that a violation continues after due notice has been served shall be deemed a separate offense. 
111.4 Failure to comply. Any person who shall continue any work after having been served with a stop work order, except such work as that person is directed to perform to remove a violation or unsafe condition, shall be liable to a fine of not less than $50.00 dollars or more than $100.00 dollars. 
(Code 1974, § 12-39; Ord. No. 2008-3, § 1, 3-17-08)
