ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 70-1. - Parks and recreation board. 
    There shall be a parks and recreation board for the city which shall be a corporation, incorporated under the laws of the state. The board shall be governed and the six members of the board of directors elected by the city council by the certificate of incorporation dated March 3, 1972. 
(Code 1974, § 2-220) 
State Law reference- Public park and recreation boards, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-60-1 et seq. 
Secs. 70-2-70-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARK RULES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 70-26. - Vehicles and livestock in parks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drive or cause to be driven any kind of vehicle or any kind of livestock on the city parks or any portion thereof, except in or along the roads or streets provided by the city for public travel. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10) 
Sec. 70-27. - Dispensing alcoholic beverages at Lakepoint Resort State Park on Sundays. 
    Alcoholic beverages may be dispensed on the premises of Lakepoint Resort State Park on Sundays between the hours of 1:00 p.m. and 12:00 midnight at events held by the organization sponsoring a convention, meeting, seminar or similar type function. 
(Code 1974, § 4-20.1) 
Cross reference- Alcoholic beverages, ch. 10. 
Secs. 70-28-70-40. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - OLD TOWN CREEK PARK AND BARBOUR CREEK NORTH BOAT LANDING 

Sec. 70-41. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Park means the property under lease from the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(1)c.) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 70-42. - Applicability. 
    This division is applicable to the water resource development project under lease from the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers by the city parks and recreation board. All other federal, state and city laws and ordinances remain in full force when applicable. In a conflict between this section and any other city law or ordinance, this section shall control. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1) 
Sec. 70-43. - Policy. 
(a)  It is the policy of the city parks and recreation board to manage Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing in the best interest of the public by providing safe and healthful recreational pursuits while protecting and enhancing the resources. 
(b)  These facilities are available to the public without regard to sex, race, creed, color or national origin. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(1)a., b.) 
Sec. 70-44. - Violations. 
    Any person who violates the provisions of this division may be punished in accordance with the provisions of section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(17)) 
Sec. 70-45. - Fees. 
    Fees for the use of Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing shall be posted at designated areas. Failure to pay authorized recreational use fees is prohibited. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(16)) 
Sec. 70-46. - Vehicles. 
(a)  This section pertains to all vehicles, including but not limited to automobiles, trucks, motorcycles, minibikes, bicycles and three-wheelers. 
(b)  Vehicles shall not be parked at Old Creek Town Park or Barbour Creek North Boat Landing in violation of posted restrictions or in such a manner as to endanger property or the environment. The owner of any such vehicle in violation shall be presumed to have parked it. 
(c)  The operation or parking of a vehicle off the roadways is prohibited except at locations and times designated by the parks and recreation director. Taking any vehicle through, around or beyond a restrictive sign, recognizable barrier, fence or traffic control barrier is prohibited. 
(d)  Vehicles shall be operated only in accordance with posted regulations. 
(e)  No person shall operate any vehicle in a careless, negligent or reckless manner so as to endanger park property or other environmental features. 
(f)  Vehicles should be used only for passage into or out of the park area. 
(g)  Speed limit within the park is posted at 20 miles per hour. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(2)) 
Sec. 70-47. - Vessels. 
    Water skis and similar devices are permitted in nonrestricted areas at Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing, except that they may not be used in a careless, negligent or reckless manner. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(3)) 
Sec. 70-48. - Aircraft. 
    The operation of aircraft on land in Old Creek Town Park or Barbour Creek North Boat Landing is prohibited, without prior approval of the parks and recreation director. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(4)) 
Sec. 70-49. - Picnicking. 
(a)  Picnicking is permitted in designated areas of Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing. 
(b)  Picnickers shall keep their site free of trash and litter during the period of occupancy and shall remove all personal equipment and clean their site prior to departure. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(5)) 
Sec. 70-50. - Camping. 
    At Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing, camping is authorized only at sites designated and approved by the director of parks and recreation. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(6)) 
Sec. 70-51. - Sanitation. 
(a)  Garbage, trash, rubbish, litter or other waste materials generated in the park grounds at Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing must either be deposited in receptacles designated for this purpose or removed from the park. 
(b)  The use of containers to dump or dispose of household or commercial waste is strictly prohibited by city ordinance. 
(c)  Glass beverage containers are prohibited from use at any location within the park. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(7)) 
Sec. 70-52. - Fires. 
    Fires at Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing shall be confined to fireplaces, grills and other areas designated for that purpose. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(8)) 
Sec. 70-53. - Animals. 
(a)  No person shall bring horses, cattle or other livestock into the picnic, swimming or recreation areas at Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing. 
(b)  No person shall bring dogs, cats or other pets into any area of the park unless penned, caged or on a leash under six feet in length. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(9)) 
Sec. 70-54. - Destruction of property. 
    At Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing, destruction, injury, defacement or any change in public property, including but not limited to constructed facilities, natural formations, historical and archaeological features and vegetative growth, is strictly prohibited. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(12)) 
Sec. 70-55. - Abandonment of personal property. 
    Personal property of any kind shall not be abandoned or left unattended at Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(13)) 
Sec. 70-56. - Lost and found articles. 
    All articles found at Old Creek Town Park or Barbour Creek North Boat Landing should be deposited by the finder at the parks and recreation office at 545 East Barbour Street (city hall). 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(14)) 
Sec. 70-57. - Advertisements. 
    Advertising in any manner whatsoever without prior approval of the parks and recreation director is prohibited at Old Creek Town Park and Barbour Creek North Boat Landing. 
(Code 1974, § 16-10.1(15)) 
Chapter 74 - SECONDHAND GOODS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 22. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 74-1-74-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - GARAGE SALES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 74-26. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Conduct of sale means the sale is to be conducted by the applicant and members of his immediate household only. 
    Garage sales means and includes all sales entitled "garage sale," "lawn sale," "attic sale," "rummage sale," "yard sale" or "flea market sale" which are advertised by any means whereby the public at large is or can be made aware of the sale. 
    Goods includes any goods or other property capable of being the object of a sale regulated under this article. 
    Items to be sold means the legal property of the applicant or members of his immediate household, surplus to his needs, and do not include any items purchased by or consigned to the applicant or members of his immediate household for resale. 
(Code 1974, § 201/2-21) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 74-27. - Penalty. 
    Any person conducting a garage sale without being properly licensed therefor or who shall violate any of the other terms and regulations of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 201/2-26) 
Secs. 74-28-74-40. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

Sec. 74-41. - Required; fee. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct a garage sale in the city without first filing with the city clerk/treasurer the information specified in this division and obtaining from the city clerk/treasurer a license to do so, to be known as a "garage sale license." The fee for such license shall be $5.00. 
(Code 1974, § 201/2-22) 
Sec. 74-42. - Information to be filed. 
    The information to be filed with the city clerk/treasurer pursuant to this division shall be as follows: 
(1)  Name of person, corporation or partnership conducting the sale. 
(2)  Name of owner of the property on which the sale is to be conducted and consent of the owner, if the applicant is other than the owner. 
(3)  Location at which the sale is to be conducted. 
(4)  Number of days of the sale. 
(5)  Date, nature of any past sale. 
(6)  Relationship or connection the applicant may have had with any other person, corporation or partnership conducting the sale and the date of the sale. 
(7)  Whether or not the applicant has been issued any other vendor's license by any local, state or federal agency. 
(8)  A sworn statement or affirmation by the person signing that the information therein contained is full and true and known to him to be so. 
(Code 1974, § 201/2-23) 
Sec. 74-43. - Limitations on number, duration; display. 
(a)  A garage sale license shall be issued to any one person only once within a 12-month period, and no such license shall be issued for more than four consecutive calendar days. 
(b)  Each license issued under this division must be prominently displayed on the premises upon which the garage sale is conducted throughout the entire period of the licensed sale. 
(Code 1974, § 201/2-24) 
Sec. 74-44. - Exceptions. 
    This division shall not apply to or affect the following persons or sales: 
(1)  Persons selling goods pursuant to an order or process of a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(2)  Persons acting in accordance with their powers and duties as public officials. 
(3)  Any person selling or advertising for sale an item of personal property which is specifically named or described in the advertisement and which separate items do not exceed ten in number. 
(4)  Churches, civic organizations, garden clubs, school-related clubs, etc. 
(Code 1974, § 201/2-25) 
Secs. 74-45-74-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - AUCTIONS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to regulate auctions, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-51-97, 34-4-6; auctioneers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 34-4-1 et seq. 

Sec. 74-66. - Exemptions. 
    The provisions of this article shall not apply to livestock auctions; stocks of goods sold as an entirety; sales under order of any court or under any other judicial process; or executors, administrators, guardians or attorneys at law in the execution of their trusts. 
(Code 1974, § 7-8) 
Sec. 74-67. - Auction of jewelry. 
    No person shall sell or offer for sale at auction jewelry of any kind, unless each article of jewelry so sold or offered for sale shall have attached to it a tag or label, specific and written in plain English, the kind of material it is made of. The tag or label must go with the purchase and be delivered to the purchaser as a true and correct description of the article so purchased. 
(Code 1974, § 7-2) 
Sec. 74-68. - Accepting false bids. 
    No auctioneer shall accept false bids from any person in the employ of himself or others, and no articles shall be given away, disposed of or offered to any person as a gift, premium, bonus or inducement to purchase any other article or commodity. 
(Code 1974, § 7-3) 
Sec. 74-69. - Making false bids. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to act as a by-bidder or what is commonly known as a "capper" or "booster" at any auction or to offer or make false bids on anything or any article held or offered for sale at such auction or pretend to buy anything at any auction sale in order in any manner to stimulate such sales by any deceit or misrepresentation in the making of bids. 
(Code 1974, § 7-4) 
Sec. 74-70. - False representations. 
    No auctioneer shall make any false representations as to the character, quality, condition, value or ownership of any property offered for sale or falsely represent that such property is in whole or in part bankrupt or insolvent stock or damaged goods or goods saved from fire. 
(Code 1974, § 7-5) 
Sec. 74-71. - Selling on streets or sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any auctioneer to sell wares or articles of any kind or description on the streets or sidewalks of the city or to store or place the wares or articles on such streets or sidewalks. 
(Code 1974, § 7-6) 
Sec. 74-72. - Noise. 
    Auctioneers shall not ring or cause to be rung in the streets a bell or cause to be beaten a drum or make any unusual noises for the purpose of drawing a crowd. 
(Code 1974, § 7-7) 
Chapter 78 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Superintendent of streets and sanitation, § 2-201 et seq.; utilities, ch. 94. 
State Law reference- Solid Wastes Disposal Act, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-1 et seq.; local solid waste management plans, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-47. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 78-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Containers means locally approved metal, heavy duty paper or plastic receptacles used for the disposal and storage of solid waste. 
    Litter means any quantity of uncontainerized paper, metal, plastic, glass or miscellaneous solid waste or other objects which may be classed as trash, debris, rubbish, refuse, garbage or junk. 
    Private property includes but is not limited to the following exterior locations owned by private individuals, firms, corporations, institutions or organizations: yards, grounds, driveways, entranceways, passageways, parking areas, working areas, storage areas, vacant lots, recreation facilities and bodies of water, including ponds, pools, streams and lakes. 
    Public property includes but is not limited to the following exterior locations: streets, street medians, road medians, catch basins, sidewalks, strips between streets and sidewalks, lanes, alleys, public rights-of-way, public parking lots, school grounds, municipal housing project grounds, municipal vacant lots, parks, beaches, playgrounds, other publicly owned recreation facilities and publicly owned lakes, rivers, creeks, streams and other bodies of water. 
(Code 1974, § 13-1) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 78-2. - Enforcement. 
    In the following departments, designated personnel are authorized to enforce sections of this chapter as stated: 
(1)  Police department. Regular officers are empowered to enforce any regulation of which violation may be observed in the normal course of patrol duty. 
(2)  Building department. In pursuance of their normal work, inspectors in the building department are authorized to enforce the following sections: 
a.  Section 78-39, litter control at construction or demolition projects and appropriate collection or disposal. 
b.  Section 78-70, approval of solid waste disposal and storage facilities at new buildings. 
(3)  Fire department. In pursuance of their normal work, inspectors in the fire department are authorized to enforce the following sections: 
a.  Sections 78-67(a) and 78-68, wherever violations of household solid waste containerization regulations constitute existing or potential fire hazards. 
b.  Sections 78-67(b) and 78-69, wherever a similar situation prevails with regard to commercial solid waste containerization. 
c.  Sections 78-40 and 78-42 through 78-44, wherever violations of clean property sections constitute existing or potential fire hazards. 
(4)  Parks and recreation director. Along with his regular duties, the parks and recreation director is authorized to enforce the following sections at parks, beaches and other recreation facilities over which the director has jurisdiction: 
a.  Section 78-32(a), littering by pedestrians. 
b.  Section 78-34, littering with handbills, leaflets, etc. 
(Code 1974, § 13-21) 
Secs. 78-3-78-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LITTER CONTROL[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Criminal littering, Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-7-29. 

Sec. 78-31. - Violations. 
    In any prosecution for violation of this article, each of the following creates a rebuttable presumption that the defendant is the person who committed the violation: 
(1)  Evidence that the defendant was the owner of the litter. 
(2)  Evidence that the defendant had possession or control of the litter immediately prior to its disposal in violation of this article. 
Sec. 78-32. - Pedestrians and motorists. 
(a)  Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, discard, place or deposit litter in any manner or amount on any public or private property within the corporate limits of the city, except in containers or areas lawfully provided therefor. 
(b)  Presumption. In a prosecution charging a violation of subsection (a) of this section from a motor vehicle, proof that the particular vehicle described in the complaint was the origin of the litter, together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was at the time of such violation the registered owner of the vehicle, shall constitute in evidence a rebuttable presumption that the registered owner was the person who committed the violation. 
(Code 1974, § 13-2) 
Sec. 78-33. - Dropping from aircraft. 
    No person in an aircraft shall throw out, drop or deposit within the city or its police jurisdiction any litter, handbill or any other object. 
(Code 1974, § 13-3) 
Sec. 78-34. - Distribution of commercial and noncommercial handbills. 
    It shall be the duty of every person distributing commercial and noncommercial handbills, leaflets, flyers or any other advertising and information material to take whatever measures that may be necessary to keep such materials from littering public or private property. 
(Code 1974, § 13-4) 
Sec. 78-35. - Placing on vehicles. 
    No person shall throw or deposit any commercial or noncommercial handbill in or upon any vehicle within the city or its police jurisdiction; provided, however, that it shall not be unlawful in any public place for a person to hand out or distribute, without charge to the receiver thereof, a noncommercial handbill to any occupant of a vehicle who is willing to accept it. 
(Code 1974, § 13-5) 
Sec. 78-36. - Truck loads or wheels. 
    No person shall drive or move any truck or other vehicle within the city or its police jurisdiction, unless such vehicle is so constructed or loaded as to prevent any load, contents or litter from being blown or deposited upon any street, alley or other public place. No person shall drive or move any vehicle or truck within the city or its police jurisdiction, the wheels or tires of which carry onto or deposit on any street, alley or other public place mud, dirt, sticky substances, litter or foreign matter of any kind. 
(Code 1974, § 13-6) 
Sec. 78-37. - Covering vehicles transporting loose materials. 
(a)  Required. It shall be unlawful for any person to transport any loose cargo by truck or other motor vehicle or airplane within the corporate limits of the city, unless the cargo is covered and secured in such manner as to prevent depositing of litter on public and private property. 
(b)  Persons liable for violation. The duty and responsibility imposed by subsection (a) of this section shall be applicable alike to the owner of the truck or other vehicle, the operator thereof and the person from whose residence or establishment the cargo originated. 
(c)  Presumption. In a prosecution charging a violation of subsection (a) of this section, lack of adequate covering and securing shall in itself constitute proof a violation has been committed. 
(Code 1974, § 13-7) 
Sec. 78-38. - Loading and unloading operations. 
(a)  Containers, removal. Any owner or occupant of an establishment or institution at which litter is attendant to the packing and unpacking and loading and unloading of materials at exterior locations shall provide suitable containers for the disposal and storage of such litter and shall make appropriate arrangements for the collection thereof. 
(b)  Cleaning of premises. It shall be the duty of the owner or occupant to remove at the end of the working day any litter that has not been containerized at these locations. 
(Code 1974, § 13-8) 
Sec. 78-39. - Construction or demolition projects. 
(a)  Accumulations prohibited. It shall be unlawful for the owner, agent or contractor in charge of any construction or demolition site to cause, maintain, permit or allow to be caused, maintained or permitted the accumulation of any litter on the site before, during or after completion of the construction or demolition project. 
(b)  Containers, removal. It shall be the duty of the owner, agent or contractor to have on the site adequate containers for the disposal of litter and to make appropriate arrangements for the collection thereof or for transport by himself to an authorized facility for final disposition. 
(c)  Proof of collection and disposal. The owner, agent or contractor may be required at any time to show proof of appropriate collection or, if transported by himself, of final disposition at an authorized facility. 
(Code 1974, § 13-9) 
Sec. 78-40. - Cleanliness of exterior private property. 
    It shall be the duty of the owner, agent, occupant or lessee to keep exterior private property free of litter. This section applies not only to removal of loose litter, but to materials that already are or become trapped at such locations as fence and wall bases, grassy and planted areas, borders, embankments and other lodging points. 
(Code 1974, § 13-10) 
Sec. 78-41. - Litter receptacles provided by public establishments. 
    To facilitate proper disposal of litter by pedestrians and motorists, such publicly patronized or used establishments and institutions as may be designated by the streets and sanitation department shall provide, regularly empty and maintain in good condition containers that meet standards prescribed by the department. This section shall be applicable but not limited to fast food outlets, shopping centers, convenience stores, supermarkets, service stations, commercial parking lots, mobile canteens, motels, hospitals, schools and colleges. 
(Code 1974, § 13-11) 
Sec. 78-42. - Cleanliness of vacant lots by nonresident owners. 
    It shall be the duty of every nonresident owner of a vacant lot or other vacant property to keep the lot or other property free of litter. 
(Code 1974, § 13-12) 
Sec. 78-43. - Cleaning of private property by city. 
(a)  Failure to remove litter after notice. If, after due warning, citation or summons, an owner, agent, occupant or lessee fails to remove litter from any private property, the streets and sanitation department is authorized to serve written notice on the owner or his appointed agent that if the condition is not corrected within ten days the property will be cleaned by the city and the owner or his appointed agent billed for the cost thereof. If the bill is not paid within 30 days, the city shall cause to be recorded in the city office of the judge of probate of the county a sworn statement showing the cost and expense incurred for the work done. The recordation of such sworn statement shall constitute a lien and privilege on the property and shall remain in full force and effect for the amount due in principal and interest, plus costs of court, if any, for collection until final payment has been made. The costs and expenses shall be collected in the manner fixed by law and shall be subject to a delinquency penalty of ten percent if not paid in full on or before the date the costs and expenses become delinquent. Sworn statements recorded in accordance with the provisions of this section shall be prima facie evidence that all legal formalities have been complied with and that the work has been done properly and satisfactorily and shall be full notice to every person concerned that the amount of the statement, plus interest, constitutes a charge against the property, designated or described in the statement and that the amount is due and collectible as provided by law. 
(b)  Contract. The owners of privately owned vacant lots may enter into contracts with the city to clean the lots, as needed, for a fee. 
(Code 1974, § 13-13) 
State Law reference- Nuisance abatement authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-47-117, 11-47-118. 
Sec. 78-44. - Keeping alleys and sidewalks clean. 
(a)  Required. It shall be the duty of owners, occupants, agents or lessees whose properties face on municipal alleys, sidewalks and strips between streets and sidewalks to keep those alleys, sidewalks and strips free of litter. 
(b)  Sweepings from sidewalks and strips. It shall be unlawful to sweep or push litter from sidewalks and strips into streets. Sidewalk and strip sweepings must be picked up and put into household or commercial solid waste containers. 
(Code 1974, § 13-14) 
Secs. 78-45-78-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - MUNICIPAL COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL SERVICE[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to provide for solid waste collection and disposal, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-47-135, 22-27-3. 

Sec. 78-66. - Established; frequency of service. 
(a)  There is established in the city a refuse collection, hauling, and disposal service to be operated as a part of the streets and sanitation department. It shall be mandatory for all part-time and full-time residents and/or the holder of any City of Eufaula business license to either participate in the municipal garbage disposal program or to participate in one provided by a licensed commercial garbage disposal operator. 
(b)  The collection, hauling and disposal of refuse shall be made by the sanitation department once per week in residential areas and at least once per week in business areas, and the charges imposed are based on such periodic collection, hauling and disposal. 
(c)  In the event a part-time or full-time resident and/or holder of any City of Eufaula business license who has not lawfully opted out of participation in the municipal garbage disposal system fails to pay a charge for said service, then the following procedures shall apply: 
(1)  The sanitation officer who shall be designated as such by the mayor, shall give said part-time or full-time resident and/or holder of any City of Eufaula business license an official ten day written notice of said delinquency which notice shall also provide notification of the right of a hearing before the sanitation officer to show justification, if any, why there has been a failure of compliance. The date, time, and place for said hearing shall be set out in said notice. 
(2)  In the event the part-time or full-time resident and/or holder of any City of Eufaula business license fails to attend said hearing and/or after said hearing date fails to bring said account current within five days of the date of said hearing, then a final written notice in substantially the form set out below shall be given: 
Dear ____________ : 
    You have not responded to the Legal Notice issued to you on ____________ regarding your delinquent account with the Municipal Refuse, Collection Hauling, and Disposal Service. Therefore, this office is notifying you of our intent to refer this matter to the Municipal Court of the City of Eufaula if you do not comply by bringing your delinquent account in the amount of $ ____________ current by 5:00 p.m. on ____________ . 
If you have any questions, please feel free to contact my office at 687-1236. 
Sincerely, 
____________ 
Sanitation Officer 
(3)  If the part-time or full-time delinquent resident and/or holder of any City of Eufaula business license fails to bring said account current within the time frame set out in the final notice, said part-time or full-time resident and/or holder of any City of Eufaula business license shall be in violation of this section and shall be punished as provided in Title 22-27-3(2) and 22-27-7, Code of Alabama 1975. Enforcement of this provision shall be by summons and complaint. 
(d)  For purpose of application of this section, a part-time or full-time resident shall be defined as an adult citizen residing part-time or full-time within the city limits of Eufaula who is the primary head of the household at said garbage pickup location. In the event there is more than one adult citizen residing part-time or full-time at said location and no single adult citizen is willing to designate himself or herself as the head of the household, then for purposes of enforcement of this section, the adult citizen who has signed up for water service with the utility furnishing water service to said home shall be deemed to be the head of the household. 
(Code 1974, § 13-19(a); Ord. No. 2001-7, 9-17-01) 
Sec. 78-67. - Depositing household, commercial solid waste in litter receptacles. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any resident to deposit household solid waste in any receptacle maintained on a sidewalk or at any other location for disposal of litter by pedestrians. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any owner, manager or employee of a commercial establishment or institution to deposit solid waste from that establishment or institution in any receptacle maintained on a sidewalk or at any other location for disposal of litter by pedestrians. 
(Code 1974, § 13-15) 
Sec. 78-68. - Household solid waste containerization, preparation for removal. 
(a)  A residence located in any area in which collection is by the city or approved contractors shall have sufficient container capacity to accommodate the normal volume of solid waste between collections. The size of the container, as prescribed by the streets and sanitation department, shall be not over 30 gallons in size. 
(b)  All items too large to fit into containers, such as but not limited to appliances, furniture and mattresses, shall be disposed of only by notifying the streets and sanitation department for pickup. 
(c)  All loose materials which normally fit into containers but which are excess as a result of special circumstances, such as holidays, shall be bundled and tied securely to prevent them from blowing or scattering and shall be placed beside the containers. 
(d)  Containers shall be kept covered at all times. 
(e)  Any container which does not conform to prescribed standards or which has defects likely to hamper collection or injure the person collecting the contents thereof or the public generally shall be replaced promptly by the owner or user of the container upon receipt of written notice of such defects from the streets and sanitation department. Failure to do so within five days of such notification shall constitute a violation of this section. 
(Code 1974, § 13-16) 
Sec. 78-69. - Commercial solid waste containerization, preparation for removal. 
(a)  All commercial establishments and institutions which generate solid waste for collection by the city or approved contractors shall abide by the container requirements prescribed by the streets and sanitation department. Containers shall not be more than 30 gallons in size, except such containers provided by the city, and shall be four, six or eight cubic yards in size. 
(b)  Containers shall be kept covered at all times. 
(c)  Any container which does not conform to prescribed standards or which has defects likely to hamper collection or injure the person collecting the contents thereof or the public generally shall be replaced promptly by the owner or user of the container upon receipt of written notice of such defects from the streets and sanitation department. Failure to do so within five days of such notification shall constitute a violation of this section. 
(Code 1974, § 13-17) 
Sec. 78-70. - Approval of solid waste disposal and storage facilities at new buildings. 
(a)  Before building permits shall be issued for construction of commercial buildings and multiple-dwelling units, plans for the adequacy, location and accessibility of solid waste containerization and storage facilities must be approved by the building official. 
(b)  No certificate of occupancy shall be issued for the premises until the streets and sanitation department's approval of these facilities has been obtained. 
(Code 1974, § 13-18) 
Sec. 78-71. - Dumpsters. 
    The dumpster containers provided by the city for commercial solid waste containerization and removal are for the specific use by those businesses paying for the service of those containers. It is unlawful for any person to dump refuse into any garbage container other than one owned by him or provided by the city for his use or for public use. 
(Code 1974, § 13-19(d)) 
Sec. 78-72. - Collection of dead animals. 
(a)  Generally. Dead animals in the corporate limits of the city not in excess of 50 pounds in weight will be picked up by the garbage collectors. No person having a dead animal on premises occupied or under the control of such person shall allow it to remain undisposed of for a period of longer than 12 hours. If the dead animals must be disposed of on a day other than the date designated as collection day, the streets and sanitation department shall be notified. All animals above 50 pounds must be removed within 12 hours by the owner, and it shall be unlawful for any person to throw or put into the streets, lanes, alleys, parkways or rights-of-way any dead animal. 
(b)  Places of business treating, handling or boarding animals. It shall be the duty of places of business making a business of treating, handling, keeping or disposing of animals to remove all dead animals from their premises to the city dump under the same regulations as apply in subsection (a) of this section. 
(Code 1974, § 13-20) 
Sec. 78-73. - Trash collection. 
(a)  All trash, except limbs and hedge cuttings less than four feet in length and less than eight inches in diameter, placed for collection, shall be in bags (tied at the top) and shall be placed behind the curb. It shall be unlawful to sweep or pile yard trash, limbs, or leaves in the gutter or median. 
(b)  During the period of October 1 through April 15 of each year, tree or shrubbery leaves are exempt from the requirement to be placed in 30-gallon bags or containers. Tree or shrubbery leaves placed behind the curb in orderly piles or rows will be picked up. Trash service shall be rendered on scheduled days, Monday through Friday. 
(c)  Brush, tree trunks and large limbs over four feet in length and eight inches in diameter may be picked up on scheduled days, Monday through Friday. The minimum charge for this service shall be $5.00, with a charge of $40.00 if the load fills the entire trash wagon, together with appropriate tipping fees. The public works department will estimate the weight of loads that do not fill the entire trash wagon and prorated tipping fees for tonnage will be calculated and added to the charges applied to resident without further notice. When the load fills the entire trash wagon, the entire cost of the tipping fee will be assessed to the resident. Stoves, refrigerators, freezers, sofas, mattresses, hot water heaters, and other appliances or household furnishings will be picked up at a charge of $5.00 per item. 
(d)  Residents will be requested to keep separate limbs, leaves and grass from all other trash pick up items. Failure to do so could result in the street and sanitation department from serving a residence or business until such items comply with this section. 
(e)  The street and sanitation department will not be responsible for picking up building materials left by private contractors and homeowners, or limbs and tree trunks left by commercial or nonprofit tree cutters. 
(Ord. No. 1997-5, 5-19-97; Ord. No. 2000-3, 4-17-00) 
Sec. 78-74. - Fees. 
(a)  The following charges shall be paid to the city by every family unit and for business establishments that do not generate a large amount of refuse that would require a large dumpster container for the collection, hauling and disposing of refuse: 
(1)  For each single-family dwelling unit using one or two 32-gallon containers, the charge shall be $14.00 per month; the cans shall not exceed 32-gallon capacity each. For each additional 32-gallon container, the charge shall be $1.00 per month, the containers not to exceed 32-gallon capacity. 
(2)  For each mobile home or apartment unit using one or two 32-gallon containers, the charge shall be $14.00 per month; the containers shall not exceed 32-gallon container, the charge shall be $1.00 per month, the containers not to exceed 32-gallons capacity each. 
(3)  For each single-family dwelling unit, mobile home, apartment unit or business, the charge shall be $2.75 per month for the purpose of collecting trash, limbs, leaves and other miscellaneous nonputridable waste. 
(4)  For businesses that do not generate a large amount of refuse that would require a large dumpster container, the rate structure shall be $14.25 for establishments using two 32-gallon containers and one-half this amount for each additional 32-gallon container, such containers not to exceed 32-gallon capacity. 
(5)  For businesses that require the use of large dumpster containers, the charge for regular service shall be set according to the following criteria:

(6)  Charges for extra dumps per dumpster container which are in addition to the regular charges in subsection (a)(5) of this section shall be based on the following rates: 
a.  Per two cubic yard container dump, $15.70.

(7)  When extra dumps do not require an extra trip by a garbage truck to the dumpster location, charges for extra dumps per container which are in addition to the regular charges in subsection (a)(5) of this section shall be based on the following rates: 
a.  Per four cubic yard container dump, $6.50. 
b.  Per six cubic yard container dump, $9.75. 
c.  Per eight cubic yard container dump, $13.00.

(b)  It shall be the duty of each commercial customer to advise the superintendent of the streets and sanitation department of the desired service. Should the superintendent of streets and sanitation determine at any time that the service being rendered is less or greater than that being paid for, it is the superintendent's duty to adjust the rate appropriately. It is the duty of the customer to notify the streets and sanitation department in writing of any desired change in service. Upon the receipt of this written request for a service change, the streets and sanitation department shall have up to 30 days to implement a billing change. 
(c)  Any person aggrieved by any determination of charges made by the superintendent of streets and sanitation shall have the right to appeal to the council or to a committee which may be established by the council for the purpose of hearing such appeals, by filing with the city clerk/treasurer a written application requesting a resurvey and computation of the volume of refuse produced upon the premises. Upon receipt of such application, it shall be the duty of the superintendent of streets and sanitation to promptly resurvey any premises and estimate the average monthly production of refuse upon the premises. However, no refund or extra charge shall be made for the month in which the application is filed. The superintendent shall have the right at any time to recheck or resurvey any premises and to reduce or increase the charge for the following months according to the volume of trash found to be produced or accumulated upon the premises. 
(d)  For any commercial premises in which there shall be, in addition to the commercial establishment, one or more living units with kitchen facilities, in addition to the commercial rates described in this section, the residential rate shall be paid for each unit. 
(Code 1974, § 13-19(b); Ord. No. 1990-27, § 1, 1-7-91; Ord. No. 1991-8, 10-16-91; Ord. No. 1994-6, 2-21-94; Ord. No. 1995-14, 10-16-95; Ord. No. 1997-5, 5-19-97; Ord. No. 1998-7, 5-18-98; Ord. No. 2001-5, 7-16-01; Ord. No. 2005-15, 11-21-05; Ord. No. 2009-3, 2-16-09, eff. 4-1-09; Ord. No. 2013-4, 12-16-13 ) 
State Law reference- Fees authorized, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 11-47-135, 22-27-5. 
Sec. 78-75. - Billing, collection. 
(a)  Bills for services under this article shall be due and payable during the month in which service is rendered. Statements for services rendered may be mailed by the waterworks and sewer board on its regular billing for water service, and, when so mailed, payment shall be made to the waterworks and sewer board of the fee for garbage service. 
(b)  If such bills for services rendered are not paid within 30 days, the city shall at the expiration of such 30-day period suspend such service, or proceed to recover the amount of such delinquency with interest in a civil action, or both. The person responsible for the payment of the cost of the garbage service shall first be notified by certified letter of the amount in arrears and at the same time the city may notify the county health department of such delinquency. 
(Code 1974, § 13-19(c); Ord. No. 1997-5, 5-19-97) 
Chapter 82 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND MISCELLANEOUS PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Superintendent of streets and sanitation, § 2-201 et seq.; smoking in public places, § 50-26 et seq.; traffic and vehicles, ch. 90. 
State Law reference- Municipal streets, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-49-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 82-1. - Placing goods, wares or containers on streets, sidewalks or alleys. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place, keep on or encumber any street, sidewalk or alley with any goods, wares, merchandise, empty boxes or barrels or any containers of any type for a longer time than is reasonably necessary for removal. 
(Code 1974, § 22-3) 
Sec. 82-2. - Skating on streets. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to use roller skates, other kind of skates or skateboards on, along, across or over any street, sidewalk or alley of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 22-4) 
Sec. 82-3. - Spitting on sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to spit or expectorate upon any sidewalk of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 22-5) 
Sec. 82-4. - Defacing pavements or curbstones. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to write, paint or print any letters, figures, signs, devices, pictures or marks on any of the pavements or curbstones of the city. This section shall not apply to traffic regulatory markings required or authorized by this Code or other ordinance of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 22-6) 
Sec. 82-5. - Defective or unsafe conditions of sidewalks or grass plots. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any property owner to allow the sidewalk paving in front or along the side of his property to remain in a broken, worn, damaged or defective condition or to permit, suffer, cause or allow any obstruction to remain thereon or on any grass plot adjacent to such sidewalk or to permit such sidewalk or grass plot to remain in an unsafe or dangerous condition to the traveling public or to pedestrians using the sidewalk or grass plot in the ordinary manner of travel thereon. 
(b)  It shall be the duty of the city engineer to give notice of any defective or dangerous condition of any sidewalk or grass plot to the owner of the property abutting upon that portion of the sidewalk or grass plot in which such dangerous, unsafe or defective condition exists. The notice shall also require the property owner to repair or replace the sidewalk or grass plot within five days of the date of such notice, and it shall thereupon be the duty of such property owner to make such repairs within such time. 
(c)  If the property owner fails to make repairs as required in subsection (b) of this section within five days from receipt of notice, it shall be the duty of the superintendent of streets and sanitation to proceed to make such repairs at the expense of the property owner and to report the repairs to the city council. The council shall thereupon assess the cost of making repairs to the property owner. The city shall have a lien for such cost as provided by Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-14-2. 
(Code 1974, §§ 22-7-22-9) 
State Law reference- Authority to so provide, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-49-2. 
Sec. 82-6. - Dangerous excavations or building materials in streets or sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to leave any excavation or any material while building or repairing any house or other structure on streets and sidewalks in such a condition as to endanger persons passing along the street or sidewalk. 
(Code 1974, § 22-11) 
Secs. 82-7-82-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - EXCAVATIONS 

Sec. 82-26. - Violations. 
    Violations of this article are punishable as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 22-13) 
Sec. 82-27. - Exceptions. 
    This article shall not apply to those streets within the city maintained by the state highway department, and no person shall excavate, cut into, take up or undermine such streets without first securing permission from the state highway department. 
(Code 1974, § 22-13) 
Sec. 82-28. - Permit required. 
    No person shall excavate, cut into, take up or undermine any street, sidewalk, alley or other public property without first having obtained a permit from the city clerk/treasurer. A separate permit must be obtained for the work done on each block or street. It shall be the duty of the city clerk/treasurer to issue permits to any person who files with him an application and complies with section 82-29. 
(Code 1974, § 22-12) 
Sec. 82-29. - Cash deposit. 
(a)  To ensure the proper replacing, repairing and repaving of any street, sidewalk or alley in the city, each person making any excavation, alteration or cutting into any paved street, sidewalk, alley or other public property or each person taking up any paving or undermining the street, sidewalk, alley or other public place in the city shall, prior to undertaking to excavate, alter, or cut the street, obtain a permit from the building official, who shall require a minimum cash deposit with the city clerk/treasurer of $250.00 for each such 12 linear foot excavation, which portion of the deposit shall be used by the city for the purpose of properly repaving such excavation. 
(b)  The applicant shall be responsible for properly backfilling such excavation with approved material and concrete as provided for in this article. 
(c)  Should the sums required in subsection (a) of this section, in the opinion of the building official, be insufficient to put the street, sidewalk, alley or public property back in the same condition, the building official shall have the right and authority to require a larger deposit than is required in subsection (a) of this section, as a condition to the building official issuing a permit. 
(d)  The applicant will be refunded one-half of the deposit when the work is complete and a satisfactory inspection report given by the building official. 
(e)  If the excavation is more than the minimum 12 linear feet, an additional $15.00 for each additional linear foot will be added to the minimum deposit of $250.00, with half of total deposit amount refunded to the applicant upon completion of the work and satisfactory report issued by the building official. If the applicant fails to satisfactorily perform the required work within five working days of making the cut, weather permitting, he shall forfeit the entire deposit. 
(Code 1974, § 22-13) 
Sec. 82-30. - Specifications. 
(a)  The applicant for an excavation permit will be required to follow the specifications set out in this section for the backfilling of trenches. 
(b)  The space around the pipe shall be filled with approved backfill material free of stones. The material shall be carried up to a point of not less than 12 inches above the top of the pipe. Approved backfill is to be placed by hand in six-inch layers and tamped around the pipe with a jumping jack or by an alternate method approved by the building official, care being taken not to damage or dislocate the pipe. This procedure shall continue until the backfill is at least 51/2 inches from the grade surface. Four inches of concrete will then be placed on top of the compacted backfill material to be within 11/2 inches of grade surface. The applicant will be required to notify the building official for an inspection of the compacted trench before proceeding with four inches of concrete. 
(Code 1974, § 22-13) 
Secs. 82-31-82-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PUBLIC ASSEMBLIES[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Offenses against public peace, order, and safety, § 66-321 et seq. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 82-51. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Church means any building or place of assembly used as a house of worship by any group or congregation of persons of whatever name or calling, whether Jewish, Roman Catholic, Greek Orthodox, Unitarian, Protestant or other. 
    Epithet means any adjective, term, phrase or expression which denotes or connotes a quality or attribute regarded as characteristic of a person. 
    Insulting or fighting words means those words which by their very utterance inflict injury or tend to incite an immediate breach of the peace by the addressee, including classical fighting words, words in current use less classical but equally likely to cause violence and other disorderly words, including profanity, obscenity and threats. 
    Lewd means obscene, lustful, indecent, lascivious, lecherous or immoral. 
    Near means within sight or hearing, but in any event shall not include a distance of more than 200 yards. 
    Obscene means that which is offensive to chastity of mind or to modesty, expressing or presenting to the mind or view something that delicacy, purity and decency forbids to be exposed. It shall also mean that which is indecent, lewd, licentious, foul, filthy, libidinous and of such character as to deprave and corrupt those whose minds are open to such immoral influences or calculated, with the ordinary person, to deprave his morals or to lead to impure purposes and tending to excite feelings of an impure or unchaste character stirring the sex impulses and leading to sexually impure and lustful thoughts. 
    Public assembly refers to any parade, march, formation, procession, picket, group of pickets, picket line, demonstration, movement, assemblage, muster or display of persons, animals, floats, motor vehicles or combinations thereof on the public sidewalks, streets, highways or other public ways, for the purpose of: 
(1)  Presenting a cause; 
(2)  Expressing an opinion to the general public on any particular issue; 
(3)  Protesting or influencing any state of affairs or decision rendered or to be rendered thereon, whether political, economic or social; or 
(4)  Celebrating, marking or commemorating any past, present or future event or occurrence, whether historical or otherwise; 
notwithstanding that such public assembly may be tranquil and devoid of noise, tumult and quarrelsome demeanor and does not disturb the public peace and regardless of whether the persons participating and engaging therein march, move about or patrol, display signs, placards, flags, banners, cards or combinations thereof or sing, shout, chant, cant, yell or clap their hands; provided, however, that a funeral procession and service shall not be considered a public assembly. 
    Residential district means any portion or part of the city that has been designated as a residential district under the zoning ordinance of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 16-104) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 82-52. - Penalty. 
    Whoever shall be guilty of any violation of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 16-105) 
Sec. 82-53. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this article is to: 
(1)  Promote the public convenience and control travel on the sidewalks, streets, highways and other public ways in the city by regulating the time, place, duration and manner of use thereof for public assemblies; 
(2)  Provide for the concomitant right of free speech and assembly; 
(3)  Safeguard practical and effective means whereby citizens may express opinions and enlighten the public on the nature and costs of matters of public concern and may petition for redress of grievances; 
(4)  Vest appropriate and limited regulatory power concerning such in the mayor; and 
(5)  Provide for punishment for violations of this article. 
(Code 1974, § 16-103) 
Sec. 82-54. - Provisions deemed cumulative. 
    The sections, provisions and violations of this article are cumulative and in addition to other provisions and violations of other provisions of this Code or ordinances of the city or of the common law or statutes of the state. 
(Code 1974, § 16-106) 
Sec. 82-55. - Offenses while participating, engaged in or observing public assembly. 
    Whoever, while participating or engaging in or observing a public assembly, does any of the following shall, on conviction, be deemed guilty of an offense: 
(1)  Addresses any lewd, obscene, profane, libelous, insulting or fighting word or words to another; 
(2)  Disobeys or disregards any traffic control device, signal or regulation, except when ordered to do so by an officer of the police department; 
(3)  Utters any abusive epithet toward any person; 
(4)  Willfully and intentionally urinates or defecates on any sidewalk, street, highway or public way; 
(5)  Encourages by word or act or both the commission of any crime or quasicrime; 
(6)  Assists, attempts or participates in cordoning off a sidewalk, street, highway or other public way or entrance to any building, public or private, denying thereby free access; 
(7)  Participates or engages in any illicit sex act; 
(8)  Willfully and intentionally lies prone or sits upon any sidewalk, street, highway or other public way so as to obstruct, impede, hinder, stifle, retard or restrain passage or traffic thereon; 
(9)  Assaults, spits on or at or throws any missile at any officer of the police department, any other law enforcement officer or any person summoned to assist any such officer; or 
(10)  Fails or refuses to disperse quickly and quietly at the permitted time. 
(Code 1974, § 16-107) 
Sec. 82-56. - Public assemblies in residential district areas. 
    The mayor shall refuse to issue a permit for any public assembly in any residential district area. It shall be a violation for any person to participate or engage in any public assembly in any such area. 
(Code 1974, § 16-108) 
Sec. 82-57. - Encouraging minors to participate. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to aid, abet, command, counsel or induce any minor to participate or engage in any public assembly, whether or not such public assembly shall be permitted or not permitted as provided by this article, unless prior to the participation or engagement of such minor in such public assembly the consent of the parent or legal guardian of such person shall have been obtained. If such participation or engagement occurs during a time at which such person would be required by law to be attending school, the prior consent of the principal of the school in which such person is enrolled or, if such person is not enrolled in school, the superintendent of the school system in which such person would be enrolled, shall have first been obtained. 
(Code 1974, § 16-109) 
Sec. 82-58. - Action upon assembly becoming violent; failure to disburse on order. 
(a)  Upon any public assembly becoming violent, any law enforcement officer of the city, county or state or any magistrate having jurisdiction within the city or the police jurisdiction thereof may audibly call to a halt such public assembly, declare the assembly to have become violent and order those participating therein to disperse. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person having been so ordered to willfully fail or refuse to disperse quickly and quietly. 
(c)  Whenever any public assembly shall have become unreasonably loud or boisterous or whenever any brick, bottle or other missile shall have been thrown from within the ranks of any public assembly or when the members or participants in any public assembly shall engage in fights or other affrays, it shall be presumed that such public assembly has become violent. 
(Code 1974, § 16-110) 
Secs. 82-59-82-70. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PERMIT 

Sec. 82-71. - Required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to participate or engage in or to aid, abet, command, counsel or induce any person to participate or engage in a public assembly in the city or in the police jurisdiction thereof, without there having first been obtained prior thereto a permit for such public assembly. 
(Code 1974, § 16-116) 
Sec. 82-72. - Issuance. 
    The mayor shall issue a permit required by this division in writing to any person, organized group, partnership, unincorporated association of persons or to any corporation organized and existing under the laws of the state or of any other state, provided such corporation is qualified to do business within the state, upon proper application therefor. The permit shall permit participation and engagement in a public assembly within the city on the terms and conditions and pursuant to the procedure declared in this division. 
(Code 1974, § 16-117) 
Sec. 82-73. - Application. 
    The application for public assembly permit shall contain the following items of information: 
(1)  The name, address and telephone number of the person seeking to conduct such public assembly. 
(2)  If the public assembly is proposed to be conducted for, on behalf of or by an organization, the name, address and telephone number of the headquarters of the organization and of the authorized and responsible heads of such organization. 
(3)  The name, address and telephone number of the person who will be the public assembly chairman and who will be responsible for its conduct. 
(4)  The date when the public assembly is to be conducted. 
(5)  The route to be traveled, the starting point and the termination point. 
(6)  The approximate number of persons who and animals and vehicles which will constitute such public assembly, the type of animals and description of the vehicles. 
(7)  The hours when such public assembly will start and terminate. 
(8)  A statement as to what portion of the public streets the public assembly will occupy. 
(9)  The location by streets of any assembly areas for such public assembly. 
(10)  The time at which units of the public assembly will begin to assemble at any such areas. 
(11)  The interval of space to be maintained between units of such public assembly. 
(12)  If the public assembly is designed to be held by and on behalf of or for any person other than the applicant, the applicant for such permit shall file with the mayor a communication in writing from the person proposing to hold the public assembly, authorizing the applicant to apply for the permit on his behalf. 
(13)  Any additional information which the mayor shall find reasonably necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should issue. 
(Code 1974, § 16-118) 
Sec. 82-74. - Execution of application. 
    The application for a permit required by this division must be executed in the name of the organized group, partnership, unincorporated association of persons or corporation by a person having the authority of a general agent thereof, and such execution shall constitute a representation by the person so executing the application that he has such authority. The execution of such application by a person who has not such authority shall be deemed a violation and shall be punishable as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 16-119) 
Sec. 82-75. - Contents; violation of conditions prohibited. 
(a)  The permit required by this division shall contain terms and conditions in substantial conformity with the items of information in the application, and the mayor or other person acting for him shall modify, where possible, any item of information which, left unmodified, would necessitate the refusal of the permit. No other term or condition shall be placed in the permit except such as is reasonably necessary for the safety and protection of those engaging or participating in such public assembly for the maintenance of adequate police, fire and ambulance protection throughout the municipality and for the reasonable convenience of the public use of the public sidewalks, streets, highways and other ways. 
(b)  It shall be a violation for any person participating or engaging in such public assembly to disregard or fail or refuse to obey any term or condition in the permit, and it shall further be the duty of every person engaging in a public assembly to ascertain the terms and conditions of the permit allowing such assembly. 
(Code 1974, § 16-120) 
Sec. 82-76. - Delivery of application; permit deemed granted if not acted upon. 
    Every application for a permit required by this division shall manually be delivered to the city clerk/treasurer or to his designated representative, in the office of the city clerk/treasurer, by the person executing the application. The person delivering such application shall, upon demand, be given a written receipt for the application, identifying it and showing its time of delivery. The person executing and delivering such application and no other shall appear at the office of the city clerk/treasurer not less than six days after delivering the application and not less than 48 hours prior to the requested commencement of such public assembly and then and there request the permit applied for. If at the time of such request no action shall have been taken either granting or denying the permit, the permit shall be considered to have been granted. 
(Code 1974, § 16-121) 
Sec. 82-77. - Location near churches. 
    The mayor shall refuse to issue a permit for any public assembly at or near any church, unless the local governing body of the church shall consent in writing to the issuance of the permit. However, nothing contained in this section shall be construed to prohibit the normal religious services at any church nor any meeting of all or part of the membership of any such church and persons invited by members of such church from meeting at such church or upon the grounds of such church. Nothing contained in this section shall prohibit a parade or other public assembly from merely passing by, at or near any church so long as such passing by is not for the purpose of disturbing a worship service at such church. 
(Code 1974, § 16-122) 
Sec. 82-78. - Refusal. 
    The mayor shall refuse to issue a permit for a public assembly unless each of the following conditions is apparent from clear and convincing evidence or is evident from the application itself: 
(1)  The conduct of the public assembly will not substantially interrupt the safe and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route. 
(2)  The conduct of the public assembly will not require the diversion of so great a number of police officers of the city properly to police the line of movement and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection to the city. 
(3)  The conduct of such public assembly will not require the diversion of so great a number of ambulances as to prevent normal ambulance service to portions of the city other than that to be occupied by the proposed line of march and areas contiguous thereto. 
(4)  The concentration of persons, animals and vehicles at assembly points of the public assembly will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of or ambulance service to areas contiguous to such assembly areas. 
(5)  The conduct of such public assembly will not interfere with the movement of firefighting equipment enroute to a fire. 
(6)  The conduct of the public assembly is not reasonably likely to cause injury to persons or property, to provoke disorderly conduct or create a disturbance. 
(7)  The public assembly is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays en route. 
(8)  The public assembly is not to be held for the sole purpose of advertising any product, goods or event and is not designed to be held purely for private profit. 
(Code 1974, § 16-123) 
Chapter 86 - TAXATION[1] 
Footnotes:

Cross reference- Finance, § 2-291 et seq.; businesses, ch. 22. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 86-1-86-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - AD VALOREM TAXES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Property taxes, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-1 et seq. 

Sec. 86-26. - Tax year; taxes based on state and county assessments; date due and delinquent. 
    The municipal tax year for city ad valorem taxes shall commence on October 1 of each year and end on the next succeeding September 30. Such taxes shall be based and due on state and county assessments for the preceding tax year and shall be due for the tax year on October 1 of each tax year and shall be due and delinquent at the time when state and county taxes for the preceding tax year are due and delinquent. 
(Code 1974, § 15-18) 
State Law reference- Authority to so provide, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-40. 
Sec. 86-27. - Levy of taxes; copy to county tax assessor. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-42. 
(Code 1974, § 15-19) 
Sec. 86-28. - County tax collector to collect. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-43. 
(Code 1974, § 15-20) 
Sec. 86-29. - Lien for taxes. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-44. 
(Code 1974, § 15-21) 
Sec. 86-30. - Commission of tax assessors and tax collectors. 
    See Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-51-74. 
(Code 1974, § 15-22)

ARTICLE III. - LICENSE TAXES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 86-51-86-68. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - TOBACCO PRODUCTS-TAXES ON SALE, STORAGE OR DELIVERY[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2000-6, §§ 1-8, adopted May 15, 2000, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, inclusion as ch. 86, art. III, §§ 86-69-86-76 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Cross reference- Smoking in public places, ch. 50, art. II. 

Sec. 86-69. - Repeal of prior tobacco tax ordinance. 
    Ordinance No. 1986-6 and all other ordinances, or parts of ordinances, which are in conflict with this division are hereby repealed. 
    This division shall not be construed to repeal any of the provisions of the general business license ordinance or privilege license ordinance of the City of Eufaula, Alabama, but shall be held to be cumulative. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 1, 5-15-00) 
Sec. 86-70. - Definitions. 
    Unless the context clearly indicates a different meaning, the following words and phrases wherever used in this division shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them: 
    Containers: (1) The original boxes from which cigars are customarily sold at retail, and (2) the individual packages or cans in which cigarettes and tobacco products are customarily sold at retail. 
    Dealer: Any wholesale dealer, retail dealer or storer as herein defined. 
    Retail dealer: Any person, other than a wholesale dealer, who sells or delivers tobacco products within the municipality. 
    Retail price: The retail selling price of the tobacco products before adding the amount of the tax assessed herein or any other tobacco tax imposed under the laws of the state. 
    Sold and sale: Any transfer of title or possession, or both, exchange or barter, conditional or otherwise, in any manner or by any means whatsoever for a consideration or any agreement therefor, including rewards, prizes or premiums of tobacco products given as a result of operation on punch boards, shooting galleries or other activities. 
    Store and stored: Refer to the storage or warehousing of tobacco products in any manner, or the withdrawal or use of the same for any purpose other than the resale or reshipment outside the municipality. 
    Storer: A person who stores tobacco products in the municipality. 
    Tobacco products: Cigarettes, cigars, and smoking tobacco, smokeless tobacco, any form of tobacco product, or any of them. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 2, 5-15-00) 
Sec. 86-71. - Tax imposed in corporate limits; amount. 
    In addition to all other taxes now imposed by law, every wholesale, jobber, dealer or distributor who sells, stores or delivers any tobacco products for sale within the City of Eufaula, Alabama shall pay a license tax to the City of Eufaula and every retailer who sells, stores or delivers any tobacco products for sale within the City of Eufaula that were not purchased through a wholesaler, jobber, dealer, or distributor who sells, stores or delivers tobacco products for sale within the City of Eufaula shall pay a license tax to the City of Eufaula and a license tax is hereby fixed and levied, which license tax shall be in the following amounts for the sale, storage and/or delivery of the following named tobacco products in the corporate limits of the City of Eufaula, Alabama. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 3, 5-15-00) 
Sec. 86-72. - Tax on cigarette transactions in the City Of Eufaula, Alabama. 
    In addition to all other taxes now imposed by law, every person who sells, stores or delivers any tobacco products shall pay a license tax to the City, which license tax is fixed and levied in the following amounts for the sale, storage, or delivery of the following named tobacco products in the city: 
(1)  All cigarettes made of tobacco or any substitute therefor-$0.13 for each package. 
(2)  All cigars made of tobacco or any substitute thereof-$0.13 for each. 
(3)  All other tobacco products-$0.13 per pack. 
(4)  Rolling papers-$0.13 per pack. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 4, 5-15-00; Ord. No. 2004-7, 5-17-04) 
Sec. 86-73. - Required records and reports. 
    Every wholesaler, jobber, dealer or distributor shall, at the time of selling or delivering any tobacco products within the city limits of the City of Eufaula, Alabama, have an invoice and duplicate thereof, which shall show full and complete details of the sale or delivery of such tobacco products and shall give said duplicate invoice to the retailer dealer. Every such wholesaler, jobber, dealer, distributor, and retail dealer shall retain these invoices and all other records of the purchase, sale, exchange or receipt of tobacco products for a period of two years after each transaction. All such invoices, all cancelled checks and other records pertaining to any such purchase, sale, exchange or receipt of tobacco products shall be subject to inspection by an agent of the city on request. Said agent shall have power and authority to enter upon the premises of any wholesaler, jobber, dealer or distributor at all reasonable times for the purpose of examining such invoices, cancelled checks or other records. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 5, 5-15-00) 
Sec. 86-74. - Monthly statement and payment. 
    The tax levied hereunder on all tobacco products shall be due and payable in monthly installments on or before the 20th day of the month next succeeding the month in which the tax accrued. If said tax is not paid by said due date, then an additional sum (a late charge) equal to ten percent of said tax shall also be due. On or before the 20th day of each month, every wholesaler, jobber, dealer or distributor who sells, stores or delivers any tobacco products for sale within the City of Eufaula, Alabama and every retailer who sells, stores or delivers any tobacco products for sale within the City of Eufaula that were not purchased through a wholesaler, jobber, dealer, or distributor who sells, stores or delivers tobacco products for sale within the City of Eufaula Alabama: 
1.  Shall file with the city clerk a true and correct monthly statement in writing (on a form approved by the city clerk) of all tobacco products sold or delivered during the preceding month, for which he is or shall be liable for the payment of the license tax; and 
2.  Shall in each and every instance, upon the filing of said statement, furnish the city clerk additional information, in writing, as the clerk may require as to the sale or delivery of any tobacco products covered by such statement; and 
3.  Shall at the time of making such statement, pay to the city clerk the amount of the tobacco license tax for the preceding month. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 6, 5-15-00) 
Sec. 86-75. - Violation of ordinance; punishment. 
    Any of the following shall constitute a violation of this division: 
(a)  The omission or failure to timely file any monthly statement required by section 86-74(1) of this division. 
(b)  The omission or failure to timely provide any information requested pursuant to section 86-74(2) of this division. 
(c)  Any false information included in the monthly statement required by section 86-74(1) or with the other information requested pursuant to section 86-74(2) of this division. 
(d)  The failure to pay the amount of tax due under this division on the date the same is due. 
    Any act or omission declared above to be a violation of this division shall be a continuing offense or violation of this division and each day during which such act or omission continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
    Any person who commits an act or omission declared above to be a violation of this division shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not less than $50.00 nor more than $500.00 and/or may be sentenced to jail for a period not exceeding six months, at the discretion of the court. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 7, 5-15-00) 
Sec. 86-76. - Construction of division. 
(a)  This division shall not be construed to tax interstate commerce or any business of the United States Government or any branch or agency thereof. 
(b)  This division shall not be construed to apply to tobacco products stored for the purpose of resale or reshipment outside the municipality and which are actually so resold or reshipped. 
(c)  This division shall not be construed to repeal any of the provisions of the general license code of the municipality, but shall be held to be cumulative. 
    The provisions of this division are severable. If any part of the division is declared invalid or unconstitutional, such declaration shall not affect the part which remains. 
    All ordinances or parts thereof which conflict with this division are hereby repealed. 
(Ord. No. 2000-6, § 8, 5-15-00) 
Chapter 90 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Streets, sidewalks, and other public places, ch. 82. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 90-1. - Definitions. 
    The definitions as set forth in Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-1-1.1 are adopted as definitions for this chapter. 
(Code 1974, § 23-2) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 90-2. - Applicability of traffic laws. 
    Every person riding a motorcycle, bicycle, motor scooter, motorbike or an animal and every person driving any animal upon the public streets and highways in the city and within the police jurisdiction thereof shall be subject to the provisions of this chapter and all laws and ordinances of the city applicable to the driver of a vehicle, except those provisions which, by their very nature, can have no application. 
(Code 1974, § 23-5) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 32-5A-5, 32-5A-260. 
Sec. 90-3. - Use of coasters, toy vehicles and similar devices. 
    No person upon riding in or by means of any coaster, toy vehicle or similar device shall go upon any roadway, except while crossing a street on a crosswalk, and when so crossing such person shall be granted all of the rights and shall be subject to all of the duties applicable to pedestrians. This section shall not apply upon any street while set aside as a play street as authorized by this Code or other ordinance of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 23-7) 
Sec. 90-4. - Bicycle operation on sidewalk. 
    No person shall operate a bicycle on any sidewalk located in a business district. 
Secs. 90-5-90-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 90-26. - Police enforcement; authority of police officers and firefighters to direct traffic. 
    It shall be the duty of the police department to enforce all traffic laws. Officers of the police department are authorized to direct all traffic, whether in person or by means of visible or audible signal or sign in conformity with the laws of the city. For a fire or other emergency or to expedite traffic or safeguard pedestrians, officers of the police or fire department may direct traffic, as conditions may require. 
(Code 1974, § 23-8) 
State Law reference- Authority to regulate traffic by means of traffic officers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5-1(d); obedience to police officers and firefighters, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-4. 
Sec. 90-27. - Blood test of suspected intoxicated drivers. 
    The city designates the Drager Alcotest 7110 test, commonly known as the "breath test," to be used for the purpose of determining the alcohol content of the blood of a person lawfully arrested for any offense arising out of acts alleged to have been committed while the person was driving a motor vehicle upon the public highways of this state or the public streets within the city limits or police jurisdiction of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 23-22; Ord. No. 1993-14, § 1, 8-2-93; Ord. No. 1993-16, § 1, 9-7-93; Ord. No. 2000-5, 4-17-00) 
State Law reference- Driving under influence of alcohol, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-191; intoxication tests, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-194. 
Sec. 90-28. - Certain traffic ordinances not affected by Code.
