    Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code shall be construed as repealing or otherwise affecting any ordinance of the city prescribing traffic regulations on specific streets in the city or police jurisdiction, such as but not limited to ordinances establishing areas or spaces where parking is prohibited or limited, designating one-way streets or alleys, designating intersections for the control of traffic by signs or signals or establishing truck routes, and all such ordinances are recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out at length in this Code. 
(Code 1974, § 23-1) 
Sec. 90-29. - Impounding vehicles when violating laws; manner of removal. 
(a)  Any vehicle being driven by a driver who has been issued a citation for driving without first obtaining a driver's license or driving with any license suspended will be declared an obstruction to traffic and a public nuisance, and any police officer of the city is hereby authorized to remove such vehicle by means of rotation wrecker service after said officer has conducted a detailed inventory of the vehicle. The completed inventory sheet will be presented to the wrecker driver for his signature and the inventory left in the vehicle. Wrecker companies will transfer any such vehicle to their designated holding facility where the vehicle and inventory will be impounded until such time that the owner and/or a licensed driver reports to that location and pays the towing and/or storage fees. The police officer will take appropriate actions to ensure the occupants of said vehicle are not left stranded in an unsafe location. 
(b)  This section shall not apply to a traffic stop nor accident where a passenger in the vehicle or the vehicle's owner is present at the traffic stop or accident, is duly licensed and is not under any disability that would prevent him from operating the vehicle, and agrees to take possession of the automobile. 
(c)  The disposition of any vehicle not picked up by its owner from the wrecker service shall be as provided in this article. 
(Ord. No. 2007-11, 9-4-07) 
Secs. 90-30-90-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - VEHICLE OPERATION GENERALLY 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 90-51. - Cutting through driveways. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any vehicle over or across any driveway leading from one street to another for the purpose of evading stop signs or traffic lights located at street intersections. 
(Code 1974, § 23-19) 
Sec. 90-52. - Driving through funeral or other procession. 
    No driver of a vehicle shall drive between the vehicles comprising a funeral or other authorized procession while they are in motion. This section shall not apply at intersections where traffic is controlled by traffic control signals or police officers. 
(Code 1974, § 23-16) 
Sec. 90-53. - Drivers in a procession. 
    Each driver in a funeral or other procession shall drive as near to the righthand edge of the roadway as practical and shall follow the vehicle ahead as close as is practical and safe. 
(Code 1974, § 23-17) 
Secs. 90-54-90-70. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - SPEED LIMITS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Speed limits, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-170 et seq.; authority to fix speed limits, Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 32-5-1(e), 32-5A-173. 

Sec. 90-71. - Designation. 
    The police department, under direction of the chief of police, shall from time to time designate, by posted signs or markers, speed limits within the city or the police jurisdiction which may vary from the speed limit established in section 90-72. When any such sign or marker is posted, it shall be unlawful for any person to drive a vehicle at a greater speed than that so designated. 
(Code 1974, § 23-50) 
Sec. 90-72. - General speed limit established. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 25 miles per hour on any street or alley in the city or the police jurisdiction, except such limits as specifically provided for in this article or as posted as provided in section 90-71. 
(Code 1974, § 23-58) 
Sec. 90-73(a). - Speed zones of 65 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 65 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 69.43 thence northerly to mile post 75.184 (north city limits). 
(Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Sec. 90-73(b). - Speed zones of 55 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 55 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 59.69 (south city limits), thence northerly to mile post 63.80 (AL 30). 
(2)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 69.24 (Gammage Road) thence northerly to mile post 69.43. 
(3)  Alabama Highway No. 6 (U.S. 82), mile post no. 235.75 from the west city limits thence easterly for a distance of 2.0 miles. 
(4)  Alabama Highway No. 30, mile post no. 11.65 from the west city limits easterly for a distance of 5.80 miles. 
(Code 1974, § 23-51; Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2015-2 , adopted March 16, 2016, renumbered § 90-73 as § 90-73(b). 
Sec. 90-74. - Speed zones of 50 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 50 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city. 
(1)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 63.80 (AL 30) thence northerly to mile post 64.90 (Old Dale Road). 
(2)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 68.65 (Lake Drive) thence northerly to mile post 69.24 (Gammage Road). 
(3)  Alabama Highway No. 30, from a point 5.80 miles east of the west city limits thence easterly for a distance of 0.20 mile. 
(Code 1974, § 23-52; Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Sec. 90-75. - Speed zones of 45 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 45 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  Alabama Highway No. 6 (U.S. 82), from a point 2.00 miles east of the west city limits thence easterly for a distance of 0.30 mile. 
(2)  Five Mile Road (Barbour County Road 36), from the intersection with Clayton Highway (Highway 30) to the city limits. 
(3)  The Adjustment Center Road, from the intersection of Clayton Highway east to the Adjustment Center. 
(4)  State Docks Road, from 0.2 mile past the intersection of South Randolph Avenue and State Docks Road to the north property line of the state docks. 
(5)  Cottonhill Road, commencing at a point 1.2 miles from the intersection of the Clayton Highway and ending at the city limits. 
(Code 1974, § 23-53; Ord. No. 1991-7, § 1, 9-18-91) 
Sec. 90-76. - Speed zones of 40 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 40 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 64.90 (Old Dale Road) thence northerly to mile post 65.71 (Edgewood Drive). 
(2)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 67.87 (Cotton Avenue [North]) thence northerly to mile post 68.65 (Lake Drive). 
(3)  Alabama Highway No. 6 (U.S. 82), from a point 2.3 miles east of the west city limits thence easterly to the intersection of Alabama Highway No. 1 (U.S. 431, Eufaula Avenue North) and Alabama Highway No. 6 (U.S. 82 West) for a distance of 0.30 mile. 
(4)  Alabama Highway No. 30, from a point 6.00 miles east of the west city limits thence easterly to the intersection of Alabama Highway No. 1 a distance of 0.70 mile. 
(5)  Leroy Road from the intersection of Bakerhill Highway to the intersection of U.S. Highway 431 South. 
(Code 1974, § 23-54; Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Sec. 90-77. - Speed zones of 35 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 35 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 65.71 (Edgewood Drive) thence northerly to mile post 66.59 (Washington Street). 
(2)  Country Club Road, from the intersection of Barbour Street and Broad Street to the entrance of Eufaula Country Club. 
(3)  Fox Ridge Road, from its intersection with Country Club Road to the city limits. 
(4)  Gammage Road, from its intersection with U.S. Highway 431 to the city limits. 
(5)  Cotton Hill Road, from its intersection with Clayton Highway to the city limits. 
(6)  The Adjustment Center Road, from the second intersection on Clayton Highway eastward to the Adjustment Center. 
(7)  Cotton Hill Road, commencing at its intersection with Clayton Highway and ending at a point approximately 1.2 miles from such intersection. 
(Code 1974, § 23-53; Ord. No. 1991-7, § 1, 9-18-91; Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Sec. 90-78. - Speed zones of 30 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 30 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 67.08 (St. James Place) thence northerly to mile post 67.87 (Cotton Avenue [North]). 
(2)  Alabama Highway No. 6 (U.S. 82), from South Orange Street thence easterly to the Alabama-Georgia state line for a distance of 0.40 mile. 
(Code 1974, § 23-56; Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Sec. 90-79. - Speed zones of 25 miles per hour. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle at a greater speed than 25 miles per hour in the following listed zones of the city: 
(1)  Alabama State Route 1 (U.S. 431) from mile post 66.59 (Washington Street) thence northerly to mile post 67.08 (St. James Place). 
(2)  Alabama Highway No. 6 (U.S. 82), from the intersection of U.S. Highway 431 South and U.S. Highway 82 East thence easterly to South Orange Street for a distance of 0.20 mile. 
(Code 1974, § 23-57; Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Sec. 90-80. - Speed limits on private and public access areas and parking lots. 
(a)  No person shall operate any automobile, truck, motorcycle, or other self-propelled vehicle upon any legally posted public or private parking lots or public or private access areas thereto in excess of 15 miles per hour. 
(b)  All ordinances of the city pertaining to traffic are hereby amended to include legally posted private or public parking lots and private or public access areas thereto. If an offense occurs on a legally posted private or public parking lot or private or public access area thereto and such offense is a violation on a street or highway, then such offense is a like violation on such legally posted private or public parking lot, and private or public access thereto. 
(Ord. No. 1995-11, § 1, 9-11-95) 
Secs. 90-81-90-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - TRUCK ROUTES 

Sec. 90-91. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Truck includes all types and models of trucks, including but not limited to motor tractors, motor tractors with trailers attached, trucks or tractors with mobile homes attached, but shall not include pickup trucks. 
(Code 1974, § 23-94) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 90-92. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person violating any of the terms and provisions of this division shall, on conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 23-100) 
Sec. 90-93. - Exemptions. 
    This article shall not apply to any truck proceeding over the streets of the city to or from a place of business in the city, which business is the owner or lessee of the truck. 
(Code 1974, § 23-99) 
Sec. 90-94. - Designated. 
    The following streets and avenues and parts thereof are designated as through truck routes for trucks traveling in any direction through the city: 
(1)  All streets or portions of streets constituting U.S. Highway 82, U.S. Highway 431, Alabama Highway 30, Alabama Highway 131, Alabama Highway 95, Alabama Highway 36, Alabama Highway 165. 
(2)  State Docks Road. 
(3)  Broad Street from Colby Street to Central of Georgia Railroad. 
(4)  Gammage Road. 
(5)  Cotton Hill Road. 
(6)  Dale Road from West Washington Street to Barbour Street and Boundary Street to U.S. Highway 431. 
(Code 1974, § 23-95; Ord. No. 2015-2 , 3-16-2015) 
Sec. 90-95. - Use of designated routes; exceptions. 
    All trucks entering the city destined to any point outside of the city and not taking on or discharging any goods, wares or merchandise within the city limits shall travel exclusively on the truck routes established in this division. Such trucks that have thereon goods, wares or merchandise consigned or shipped or to be delivered to businesses within the city shall leave the truck routes at the point nearest to their destination and proceed by the most direct and shortest route to the destination and return to the designated truck routes and shall then travel exclusively along such designated truck routes through the city. 
(Code 1974, § 23-96) 
Sec. 90-96. - Signs. 
    The chief of police shall cause to be erected and maintained at points where through truck routes enter the city at all junctions, points and turns where necessary such signs and such directions at such locations as shall be approved by the chief of police directing truck traffic in accordance with the provisions of this division. 
(Code 1974, § 23-97) 
Sec. 90-97. - Trucks not on designated routes. 
    Any truck traveling the streets of the city, which streets are not on the designated truck routes, may be stopped by the police and the driver of the truck, at the request of the police, shall produce evidence that his load is or that he has goods, wares or merchandise consigned to a business in the city. Upon the failure of the driver to furnish such evidence, the driver shall be subject to prosecution for violating this division. However, nothing in this section would prevent the driver from producing other type of evidence that he has a load of goods, wares or merchandise on his truck consigned to a business in the city. 
(Code 1974, § 23-98) 
Sec. 90-98. - Special requirements for trucks and buses with more than two axles and all tractor-trailers. 
(a)  Trucks and buses with more than two axles and all tractor-trailers shall use the right lane only of all four-laned roadways within the city limits of Eufaula except when the left-hand blinking turn signal is engaged and the truck is preparing to make a left-hand turn. 
(b)  Trucks and buses with more than two axles and all tractor-trailers shall be prohibited from parking in all R-1, R-2, R-3, R-2A, R-4 and Estate District zones within the city. Excluded from this provision are ICC licensed common carrier trucks with more than two axles that are engaged in the loading and/or unloading of residential household furniture and appliances. 
(c)  The provisions of this section are severable. If any part of this section is declared invalid or unconstitutional, such declaration shall not affect the part which remains. 
(d)  Any persons found to be in violation of this section shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-6 of the Code of Ordinances of the City of Eufaula. 
(Ord. No. 1998-15, §§ 1-4, 12-21-98) 
Secs. 90-99-90-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to regulate parking, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5-1(e); stopping, standing and parking generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-136 et seq. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 90-151. - Fines. 
(a)  The following schedule for the summary disposition of motor vehicle stopping, standing and parking offenses is established: 
(1)  Stopping, standing or parking of vehicles outside business or residence district in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-136, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... $   10.00 
(2)  Stopping, standing or parking a vehicle on the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or curb of a street in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 15.00 
(3)  Parking, standing or stopping a vehicle within an intersection in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 25.00 
(4)  Stopping, standing or parking a vehicle on a crosswalk in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 15.00 
(5)  Stopping, standing or parking a vehicle between a safety zone and the adjacent curb or within 30 feet of points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone, unless a different length is indicated by signs or markings, in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 15.00 
(6)  Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic, in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 10.00 
(7)  Upon any bridge or other elevated structure in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 15.00 
(8)  On any railroad tracks in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 25.00 
(9)  At any place where official signs prohibit stopping, in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 10.00 
(10)  Standing or parking a vehicle, whether occupied or not, except momentarily to pick up or discharge a passenger, at any of the following locations in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 25.00 
a.  In front of a public or private driveway. 
b.  Within 15 feet of a fire hydrant. 
c.  Within 20 feet of a crosswalk at an intersection. 
d.  Within 30 feet upon the approach to any flashing signal, stop sign, yield sign or traffic control signal located at the side of the roadway. 
e.  Within 20 feet of the driveway entrance to any fire station and on the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station within 75 feet of such entrance (when properly signposted). 
f.  At any place where official signs prohibit standing. 
(11)  Parking a vehicle, whether occupied or not, except temporarily for the purpose of and while actually engaged in loading and unloading merchandise or passengers, in violation of the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-5A-137, as adopted for the city in section 66-1 ..... 15.00 
(12)  Unlawful parking in violation of this division ..... 10.00 
(13)  Unlawfully parking in a handicapped parking space in violation of division 2 of this article ..... 25.00 
(b)  If a parking violation is covered by two or more of the fines provided in this section, the larger fine shall be applicable. 
(Code 1974, § 23-71) 
Sec. 90-152. - Designation of manner of parking and time limits. 
(a)  The police department, under the direction of the chief of police, shall from time to time designate by markers on the public ways of the city and by signs, when in the judgment of the chief it shall be necessary, both the manner and parking time limit on any of the public ways within the city or the police jurisdiction thereof. 
(b)  When any such public way shall be so marked, any person violating either the manner of parking or the time limit shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(c)  In addition, any vehicle of any kind or type whatever parked or allowed to be parked or allowed to remain parked in violation of any regulation made pursuant to this section shall be removed by the police department to a place designated by the chief of police. The owner of such vehicle or the person entitled to the possession thereof shall be entitled to reclaim the vehicle only after having paid to the city clerk/treasurer the reasonable charges for the removal of the vehicle and the storage thereof. Any vehicle so removed shall, at the time of such removal, be considered abandoned or stolen property and listed and disposed of as such under article V, if not otherwise reclaimed within the time allowed by such provisions. 
(Code 1974, § 23-66) 
Sec. 90-153. - Parking in areas marked with yellow paint prohibited; designation of fire zones on private property. 
    No person shall park a motor vehicle in any designated area when such prohibited area is properly marked with yellow paint. With the consent of the property owner, the fire chief is authorized to designate certain areas in front of the buildings as fire zones by marking such curbs with yellow paint and posting as fire zones. The cost of signs, paint, and installation by the city shall be paid to the city by the owner prior to installation. It shall be unlawful for any unauthorized person to park a vehicle in an area designated as a fire zone. 
(Code 1974, § 23-65; Ord. No. 1994-9, 6-6-94) 
Sec. 90-154. - Passenger vehicle parking in alley. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to park and leave unattended any passenger vehicle in any of the public alleys within the city limits, except for purposes of loading and unloading. 
(Code 1974, § 23-68) 
Sec. 90-155. - Parking commercial vehicles or taxicabs in traffic lane for loading and unloading. 
    No taxicab shall be permitted to park or stand on any street, alley or other public place in the city at any hour of the day or night for a longer period of time than is actually necessary to receive or discharge passengers. 
    Each taxicab shall have a license tag conspicuously displayed thereon where it can be clearly seen. Each taxicab shall be marked "Taxi" in letters printed on each side thereof which are plainly visible and not less than two inches in height. There must be displayed within the taxicab a copy of fares for the benefit of the public. 
(Code 1974, § 23-69; Ord. No. 2003-3, 4-21-03) 
Sec. 90-156. - Parking on curbs or parks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to park or permit to be parked any vehicle on, upon or over the curb of any street or in or on the parks lying between any streets in the city or in the grassy area between the curb and/or the edge of the roadway and any hard surface sidewalk. This section shall not apply to public utility or to governmental emergency or work vehicles or to city or water department vehicles when being used for an official city or utility purpose. 
(Code 1974, § 23-70; Ord. No. 1997-2, 4-21-97) 
Sec. 90-157. - Parking vehicles in custody of garage or repair service on street; parking for repairs. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to leave any motor vehicle, which is in the custody or under the control of any garage or repair service, parked on any street for more than one day at any one time. No motor vehicle shall be parked on any street at any time for the purpose of repairing such vehicle. 
(Code 1974, § 23-64) 
Secs. 90-158-90-170. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - HANDICAPPED PARKING[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 1999-12, adopted October 18, 1999, repealed ch. 90, art. IV, div. 2, §§ 90-171-90-176 in its entirety. Subsequently, said ordinance added §§ 90-171-90-180 to read as herein set out. Formerly, said division pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Code 1974, §§ 23-73-23-78. 

Sec. 90-171. - Handicapped individual defined. 
    For the purposes of this article, the term "handicapped individual" shall mean any person who has a permanent or temporary (for a period up to one year) physical impairment or permanent mental impairment which limits mobility to the extent that the individual would have difficulty safely walking alone or walking without physical pain a distance of 50 feet or more. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-172. - Distinctive decal authorized; required; medical proof, etc. 
    Any person who submits to the judge of probate medical proof satisfactory to said issuing authority that he or she is a disabled individual as herein defined, shall be issued either a distinctive license plate or a decal and a special identification placard displaying the international system of access thereby designating the driver of the vehicle or the passenger as being a disabled person. The distinctive license plate, decals and placards provided herein shall be prepared by the judge of probate and shall be issued in the same manner as motor vehicle license plates. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-173. - Unlimited parking periods, exceptions. 
    The disabled individual to whom valid distinctive license plates, and/or decals or placards, are issued shall be allowed to park for unlimited periods in parking zones designated for disabled persons, provided, however, that such disabled persons shall pay parking fees the same as any other person. The provisions of this section shall not apply to zones where stopping, standing or parking is prohibited to all vehicles, or zones which are reserved for special types of vehicles, nor will these provisions apply where there is a local ordinance prohibiting parking during heavy traffic periods during morning, afternoon, or evening rush hours, or where parking would clearly present a traffic hazard. In designated disabled loading zones, disabled persons shall be limited to one hour parking, as these loading zones are not intended for unlimited parking usage. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-174. - False representation or misuse of parking privileges unlawful. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person who is not a disabled individual, as herein defined, to willfully and falsely represent himself or herself as a disabled person to obtain the distinctive license plate and/or decal or placard or to misuse or abuse the parking privilege protected by this division, or to own a vehicle bearing distinctive license plate and/or decals when not entitled to do so under the provisions of this division, or to park an automobile having a handicapped tag or decal or to use a handicap placard unless the person to whom said handicapped license plate, decal or special identification placard is issued is physically present in the automobile at the time said automobile is actually parked in any zone designated for "Handicap Only" or "Disabled Only" parking. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-175. - Unauthorized use unlawful. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to park any vehicle in any zone designated for "Handicap Only" or "Disabled Only" parking, not bearing the distinctive license plate and/or decal or placard or to park any vehicle in violation of any part of this division or in violation of any state statute. It shall also be unlawful for any person to park any vehicle or to allow the placement of any material or other equipment which would block an access ramp or curb cut. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person who does not have a distinctive handicapped decal or placard or "temporarily handicapped" placard as provided for in section 90-172, to park a motor vehicle in a parking place designated for the handicapped at any place of public accommodation, amusement or resort or any other place to which the general public in invited, even though located on private property, and upon conviction thereof, shall be fined as hereinafter provided. 
(c)  Any authorized municipal, county or state law enforcement officer may go onto private property to enforce the provisions of this section. 
(d)  The provisions of this section shall be held in pari materia with all other provisions of law related to illegal handicapped parking violations; provided however, that all municipal laws or parts of municipal laws which conflict with the provision of this section are hereby repealed. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-176. - Parking spaces designated. 
    The police chief is authorized to designate marked parking spaces for the exclusive parking of motor vehicles of handicapped individuals or temporarily handicapped individuals as defined by Code of Ala. 1975, Section 32-6-330. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-177. - Revocation or cancellation of authorization for use of decals and placards. 
    The use of any decals or placards for parking in handicapped spaces within the city may be revoked or cancelled for abuse, misuse or unauthorized use by persons other than the authorized handicapped individual. In such event the revoked or cancelled permit shall not be valid in the city. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-178. - Handicapped spaces on private property. 
    With the consent of the property owner, the police chief is authorized to designate certain parking spaces in privately owned parking areas to be posted as parking for the handicapped under the provisions of this division and subject to the same regulations. The cost of the sign and installation by the city shall be paid to the city by the owner prior to delivery or installation of any such sign. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-179. - Penalties for unlawful acts. 
    Any person committing any act declared to be unlawful by this division shall be guilty of an offense against the city, and shall, upon conviction, be punished as follows: 
*1st offense: $50.00 *2nd offense 100.00 *3rd offense 500.00 (*plus applicable court costs)  
    In addition, any automobile unlawfully occupying a parking zone designated for disabled or handicapped persons may be towed away at the owner's expense. 
    Such fines shall be paid in the same manner as other municipal fines for driving violations, except that the fines may not be paid without a court appearance by the person charged. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Sec. 90-180. - Effective date. 
    The effective date of this division shall be 12:01 a.m. on the 18th day of October, 1999. 
(Ord. No. 1999-12, 10-18-99) 
Secs. 90-181-90-200. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - ABANDONED VEHICLES[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Cross reference- Health and sanitation, ch. 50. 
State Law reference- Abandoned vehicles, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-13-1 et seq. 

Sec. 90-201. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Property means any real property within the city or its police jurisdiction which is not a street or highway. 
    Street or highway means the entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel. 
    Vehicle means a machine propelled by power other than human power designed to travel along the ground by use of wheels, treads, runners or slides and transport persons or property or pull machinery and shall include, without limitation, an automobile, truck trailer, motorcycle, tractor, buggy and wagon. 
(Code 1974, § 23-32) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 90-202. - Violations. 
    Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be penalized as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 23-39) 
Sec. 90-203. - Abandonment prohibited; presumption of abandonment. 
    No person shall abandon any vehicle within the city or its police jurisdiction. It shall be presumed that any vehicle that has been left at any place on a street or highway within the city or its police jurisdiction for a period of 72 hours consecutively is an abandoned vehicle. 
(Code 1974, § 23-33) 
Sec. 90-204. - Leaving wrecked, nonoperating vehicle on street. 
    No person shall leave any partially dismantled, nonoperating, wrecked or junked vehicle on any street or highway within the city or its police jurisdiction. 
(Code 1974, § 23-34) 
Sec. 90-205. - Discarded, wrecked or junked vehicles on private property. 
    No person in charge or control of any property within the city or its police jurisdiction, whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow any partially dismantled, nonoperating, wrecked, junked or discarded vehicle to remain on such property longer than 72 hours. No person shall leave any such vehicle on any property within the city or its police jurisdiction for a longer time than 72 hours. However, this section shall not apply to a vehicle in an enclosed building, a vehicle on the premises of a business enterprise operated in a lawful place and manner when necessary to the operation of such business enterprise or a vehicle in an appropriate storage place or depository maintained in a lawful place and manner by the city. 
(Code 1974, § 23-35) 
Sec. 90-206. - Removal or impoundment of vehicles. 
    The chief of police or any member of his department designated by him is authorized to remove or have removed any vehicle left at any place within the city or its police jurisdiction which reasonably appears to be in violation of this article or to be a lost, stolen or unclaimed vehicle. Any vehicle so taken up and removed shall be stored in a suitable place provided by the city to protect it from deterioration. A permanent record giving the date of the taking of each vehicle, the place where found and taken and a description of the vehicle shall be kept by the chief of police. 
(Code 1974, § 23-36) 
Sec. 90-207. - Public sale of impounded vehicles. 
    At least every six months, the chief of police shall sell at public auction to the highest bidder for cash the vehicles authorized in this article to be removed and taken up and which shall have been taken up and stored for a period of three months or more. The sales shall be made after notice of the time and place therefor shall have first been given by publication once a week for two successive weeks in a newspaper of general circulation published in the city. The first publication shall be at least 20 days before the sale. Each vehicle shall be sold separately, and a notation in the storage record book shall be made of the amount received for each vehicle. The person making the sale shall have the right to reject any and all bids if the amount bid is unreasonably low and shall have the right to continue the sales from time to time if no bidders are present. After deducting and paying all expenses incurred in the removal, taking up, storing, maintaining and selling of the vehicle, the balance if any shall be paid into the general fund of the city. 
(Code 1974, § 23-37) 
Sec. 90-208. - Redemption of impounded vehicles prior to sale. 
    The owner of any vehicle taken up and stored as provided in this article may redeem the vehicle at any time prior to its sale by paying the reasonable expense of taking the vehicle in charge, its maintenance and storage and a pro rata amount of the cost of publication. 
(Code 1974, § 23-38) 
Chapter 94 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Solid waste, ch. 78. 
State Law reference- Municipal utilities, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-50-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 94-1. - Waterworks and sewer board. 
    There is created a waterworks and sewer board for the city as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-50-230 et seq. The board shall be composed of five members appointed by the city council to serve for six years pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-50-234. 
(Code 1974, §§ 25-42, 25-43) 
Cross reference- Boards, commissions, and authorities, § 2-241 et seq. 
Secs. 94-2-94-15. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WATER[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Plumbing code, § 18-286 et seq.; health and sanitation, ch. 50; sale or distribution of unsanitary water, § 50-1. 

Sec. 94-16. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person violating any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(Code 1974, § 25-35) 
Sec. 94-17. - Connection of residences to public water system. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to reside in any residence or building designed for occupancy or used as a single-family residence, unless such building or residence is connected to and supplied with water from the public water system in the city by the mains or pipes of the public water system in the city. It shall be unlawful for any person to let or rent any such residence or building, unless the residence or building is so connected and supplied. However, this section shall not apply when the lot or parcel of land upon which the residence or building is situated is more than 100 feet from the nearest water supply main or pipe located within a public way or right-of-way which abuts or adjoins such lot or parcel of land upon which is situated the residence or building. 
(Code 1974, § 25-26) 
Sec. 94-18. - Connection of apartments to public water supply. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to reside in any apartment in any building which is designed for occupancy or used as a single-family residence, unless such apartment is connected to and supplied with water from the public water system in the city by the mains or pipes of the public water system in the city. It shall be unlawful for any owner, agent or person to let or rent any such apartment in any apartment building, unless the apartment is so connected and supplied. 
(Code 1974, § 25-27) 
Sec. 94-19. - Use of wells and springs. 
    It shall be unlawful to construct, maintain, use or permit to be used any spring, well, cistern or other excavation as a source of domestic water supply for any dwelling, building or premises located within 100 feet of the water main or pipe, as provided in section 94-17. 
(Code 1974, § 25-28) 
Sec. 94-20. - Unauthorized extension of service. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, in any manner whatever, to extend or alter any service or other pipe or attachment of any kind connecting or through which water from the public water system in the city is furnished from the water mains or pipes or source of supply. 
(Code 1974, § 25-18) 
Sec. 94-21. - Use of water from fire hydrant. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to take, carry away or use any water from the public water system in the city from a fire hydrant or fireplug in a public way, except for use in fighting fire, without authority from the waterworks and sewer board. 
(Code 1974, § 25-30) 
Sec. 94-22. - Obstructing fire hydrants and stopcocks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct access to any fire hydrant, stopcock or other fixture connected with the supply of water from the public water system in the city by placing thereon stone, brick, lumber, dirt or any other material or to permit any other material to be placed thereon by those in his employ. 
(Code 1974, § 25-31) 
Sec. 94-23. - Fire hydrants for use of fire department. 
    The fire hydrants are for the use of the fire department and for the extinguishment of fires and must be used by firefighters only and for no other purpose, except upon written permission of an official or employee of the waterworks and sewer board acting in accordance with regulations of the waterworks and sewer board. 
(Code 1974, § 25-32) 
Sec. 94-24. - Tapping mains or cutting off water. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, except an official or employee of the waterworks and sewer board acting in accordance with regulations of such board, to tap any main forming a part of the public water system in the city or to connect any service pipe therewith or to turn on or shut off water from the main, except in case of accident or emergency. 
(Code 1974, § 25-34) 
Sec. 94-25. - Use after shutoff. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to cause or suffer any premises of which he is in charge or control to be supplied with water from the public water system in the city after such water has been rightfully shut off. 
(Code 1974, § 25-14) 
Sec. 94-26. - Turning on water after shutoff. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person other than an authorized officer of the waterworks and sewer board or employee of the board, in the course of his duty, to turn on water from the public water system in the city after the water has been turned off by the authorized agents of the waterworks and sewer board. 
(Code 1974, § 25-15) 
Sec. 94-27. - Use without metering. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to connect a tub, pipe, other instrument or contrivance to any pipe used for supplying water from the public water system in the city or in any manner to change, alter, extend, connect or disconnect any pipe, meter or attachment through or by which the water is or is about to be furnished or supplied in such manner that any water from the public water system in the city is or can be used or consumed without passing through and properly registering upon the meter or other measuring instrument provided for registering the quantity used or consumed. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to turn on the flow of water from the public water system in the city through any of the pipes or mains of the public water system in the city with the intent or purpose of obtaining the use of such water without paying for the water. 
(Code 1974, § 25-16) 
Sec. 94-28. - Interference with equipment. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to, in any manner, destroy, alter, impair or prevent the proper action of any meter or other instrument used to measure the consumption of water from the public water system in the city or to connect, disconnect, reconnect or in any manner interfere with, damage or destroy any main, pipe, meter, valve, stopcock or other appliance, machinery or equipment of the public water system in the city. 
(Code 1974, § 25-17) 
Sec. 94-29. - Diversion of water from system. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person having charge or control of any pipe supplied with water from the public water system by the public water system to allow or permit any person to take, draw or use any water therefrom prior to the time of passage of such water through a meter used for measuring consumption. 
(Code 1974, § 25-21) 
Sec. 94-30. - Evidence of violations. 
    Proof that any of the acts specified in this article were done or permitted on the premises in charge of the accused or that the accused received the benefit of any of such acts shall be prima facie evidence that the accused committed, aided or abetted in the commission of such acts. 
(Code 1974, § 25-22) 
Sec. 94-31. - Contamination of water supply. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to in any way defile or contaminate or attempt to defile or contaminate the water from the public water system in the city in any reservoir, pipe, main, public fountain or stream connected with the approved public water supply of the waterworks and sewer board. 
(Code 1974, § 25-25) 
Secs. 94-32-94-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SEWERS AND SEWAGE DISPOSAL[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference- Plumbing code, § 18-286 et seq.; health and sanitation, ch. 50. 
State Law reference- Municipal sewers, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-50-51. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 94-51. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Board means the waterworks and sewer board of the city. 
    BOD, denoting biochemical oxygen demand, means the quantity of oxygen utilized in the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure of five days at 20 degrees Celsius, expressed in milligrams per liter. 
    Building drain means that part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five feet (1.5 meters) outside the outer face of the building wall. 
    Building sewer means the extension from the building drain to the public sewer or other place of disposal. 
    CFR is an abbreviation for Code of Federal Regulations. 
    Combined sewer means a sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage. 
    Garbage means solid wastes from the domestic and commercial preparation, cooking and dispensing of food and from the handling, storage and sale of produce. 
    Industrial wastes means the liquid wastes from industrial manufacturing processes, trade or business, as distinct from sanitary sewage. 
    Natural outlet means any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body of surface water or groundwater. 
    OSHA is an abbreviation for Occupational Safety and Health Administration. 
    pH means the logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per liter of solution. 
    Properly shredded garbage means the wastes from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of food that have been shredded to such a degree that all particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1.27 centimeters) in any dimension. 
    Public sewer means a sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal rights and which is controlled by public authority. 
    Sanitary sewer means a sewer which carries sewage and to which stormwater, surface water and groundwater are not intentionally admitted. 
    Sewage means a combination of the water-carried wastes from residences, business buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such groundwaters, surface waters and stormwaters as may be present. 
    Sewage treatment plant means any arrangement of devices and structures used for treating sewage. 
    Sewer means a pipe or conduit for carrying sewage. 
    Sewer works means all facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of sewage. 
    Slug means any discharge of water, sewage or industrial waste which in concentration of any given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any period of duration longer than 15 minutes more than five times the average 24-hour concentration or flow during normal operation. 
    Storm drain or storm sewer means a sewer which carries stormwaters and surface waters and drainage, but excludes sewage and industrial wastes, other than unpolluted cooling water. 
    Superintendent means the general manager of the waterworks and sewer board or his authorized deputy, agent or representative or the board's engineer. While superintendent can also be the board's engineer, the board's engineer does not mean the superintendent. 
    Suspended solids means solids that are in suspension in water, sewage or other liquids and which are removable by laboratory filtering. 
    Water board means the waterworks and sewer board. 
    Watercourse means a channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or intermittently. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. I, 11-21-90) 
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 94-52. - Violations. 
(a)  Any person found to be violating any provision of this article shall be served by the board with written notice stating the nature of the violation and providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory correction thereof. The offender shall, within the period of time stated in such notice, permanently cease all violations. 
(b)  Any person who shall continue any violation beyond the time limit provided for in subsection (a) of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished as provided in section 1-6. 
(c)  Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall become liable to the waterworks and sewer board for any expense, loss or damage occasioned the board by reason of such violation. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. VIII, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-53. - Unlawful disposal or discharges; connection to public sewer. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to place, deposit, or permit to be deposited in any insanitary manner on public or private property within the city, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any human or animal excrement, garbage or other objectionable waste. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet within the city or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city any sewage or other polluted waters, except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with this article. 
(c)  Except as provided in this article, it shall be unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool or other facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage. 
(d)  The owner of every house, building or property used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purposes situated within the city and abutting on any street, alley or right-of-way in which there is now located or may in the future be located a public sanitary or combined sewer of the city is required at his expense to install suitable toilet facilities therein and to connect such facilities directly with the proper public sewer in accordance with this article within 90 days after date of official notice to do so, provided that the public sewer is within 150 feet (30.6 meters) of the property line and the sewer can be reached through gravity flow. A monthly fee equal to the minimum charges for sewer shall be charged to all property owners within the city whose nearest property line is located within 150 feet of the public sanitary sewer or combined sewer and who have not become connected to the public sanitary sewer or combined sewer within 90 days of official notice. The monthly service fee shall not be charged to property owners who cannot be served through gravity flow or cannot be connected in an economically feasible manner as determined by the superintendent. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. II, § 4, 11-21-90; Ord. No. 2003-2, 2-17-03) 
Sec. 94-54. - Private sewage disposal. 
(a)  The disposal of sewage by means other than the use of the available sanitary sewer system shall be in accordance with local county and state law. The disposal of sewage by private disposal systems shall be permissible only in those instances where service from the available sanitary sewer system is not available. 
(b)  The board shall have authority to approve or reject private sewage disposal facilities in accordance with a standard set of plans and specifications for installation of such facilities. Permits for these facilities should be issued when approved, and periodic inspections should be made by the plumbing inspector or the local health department, depending on who issues the permits. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. III, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-55. - Right of entry. 
(a)  The superintendent and other duly authorized employees of the board bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all properties for the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling and testing in accordance with the provisions of this article. The superintendent or his representatives shall have no authority to inquire into any processes, including metallurgical, chemical, oil, refining, ceramic, paper or other industries, beyond that point having a direct bearing on the kind and source of discharge to the sewers or waterways or facilities for waste treatment. 
(b)  While performing the necessary work on private properties referred to in subsection (a) of this section, the superintendent or duly authorized employees of the board shall observe all safety rules applicable to the premises established by the company, and the company shall be held harmless for injury or death to the board employees. The board shall indemnify the company against loss or damage to its property by board employees and against liability claims and demands for personal injury or property damage asserted against the company and growing out of the gauging and sampling operation, except as such may be caused by negligence or failure of the company to maintain safe conditions as required in section 94-98. 
(c)  The superintendent and other duly authorized employees of the board bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all private properties through which the board holds a duly negotiated easement for the purposes of but not limited to inspection, observation, measurement, sampling, repair and maintenance of any portion of the sewer works lying within the easement. All entry and subsequent work, if any, on the easement, shall be done in full accordance with the terms of the duly negotiated easement pertaining to the private property involved. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. VII, 11-21-90; Ord. No. 2003-2, 2-17-03) 
Secs. 94-56-94-65. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS 

Sec. 94-66. - Permit. 
(a)  No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or opening into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the superintendent. 
(b)  There shall be two classes of building sewer permits: 
(1)  Residential and commercial service; and 
(2)  Service to establishments producing industrial wastes. 
(c)  In either class, the owner or his agent shall make application on a special form furnished by the board. The permit application shall be supplemented by any plans, specifications or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of the superintendent. 
(d)  A permit and inspection fee shall be charged for a residential, commercial or industrial building and shall be paid to the board at the time the application is filed. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, §§ 1, 2, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-67. - Costs borne by owner; indemnification. 
    All costs and expenses incident to the installation and connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the owner. The owner shall indemnify the board from any loss or damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, § 3, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-68. - Separate sewer for each building. 
    A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every building. However, where one building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining alley, court, yard or driveway, the building sewer from the front building may be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building sewer. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, § 4, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-69. - Use of old building sewers. 
    Old building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only when they are found, on examination and test by the superintendent, to meet all requirements of this article. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, § 5, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-70. - Specifications. 
(a)  The size, slope, alignment, materials of construction of a building sewer and the methods to be used in excavating, placing of the pipe, jointing, testing and backfilling the trench shall all conform to the requirements of the building and plumbing codes or other applicable rules and regulations of the water board. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification thereof, the materials and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the A.S.T.M. and W.P.C.F. Manual of Practice No. 9 shall apply. 
(b)  Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building at an elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which any building drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved means and discharged to the building sewer. 
(c)  The connection of the building sewer into the public sewer shall conform to the requirements of the building and plumbing codes or other applicable rules and regulations of the city or the procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the A.S.T.M. and W.P.C.F. Manual of Practice No. 9. All such connections shall be made gastight and watertight. Any deviation from the prescribed procedures and materials must be approved by the superintendent before installation. 
(d)  Except in cases where the superintendent shall otherwise approve, in writing as a permit condition, all connections to existing sewers shall be made by employees of the board. The connecting building sewers installed by the board shall include tap or wye and sufficient building service line to extend the building sewer to at least three feet beyond the street's traveled way, pavement, curb or sidewalk, on the side of those facilities nearest the proposed building to be served. At that point the board will install a plug, pending extension of the building sewer by the permittee. The board shall charge a fee for its costs in making the sewer connection and building sewer extension. The fee shall be payable when the permit is obtained. 
(e)  Building sewers shall be of PVC (SDR 35 or stiffer), extra strength VC, cast/ductile iron or CISP and shall have a minimum diameter of four inches. Building sewers with less than two feet of cover shall be iron. Larger diameter pipe may be required by the superintendent if estimated flows so indicate. Minimum building sewer slope shall be one-eighth inch per foot, with one-fourth inch per foot the normal slope. Fittings shall be designed for use with the pipe so grout joints are not necessary. O-ring or gasket joints for PVC or rubber shall be used. Cleanouts shall be subject to approval by the superintendent. Cleanouts shall be placed a minimum of 75 feet apart, with one being located at the property line or at the point of connection with the lateral from the public sewer line. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, §§ 6, 7, 9, 10, 13, 11-21-90; Ord. No. 1991-5, § 1, 7-1-91) 
Sec. 94-71. - Excavations. 
    All excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately guarded with barricades and lights to protect the public from hazard. Streets, sidewalks, parkways and other public property disturbed in the course of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the city. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, § 12, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-72. - Connection of other drains. 
    No person shall make connection of roof downspouts, exterior foundation drains, areaway drains or other sources of surface runoff or groundwater to a building sewer or building drain which in turn is connected directly or indirectly to a public sanitary sewer. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, § 8, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-73. - Inspection and connection. 
    The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify the superintendent when the building sewer is ready for inspection and connection to the public sewer. The connection shall be made under the supervision of the superintendent or his representative. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. IV, § 11, 11-21-90) 
Secs. 94-74-94-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - DISCHARGE RESTRICTIONS 

Sec. 94-91. - Drainage into sewers. 
    No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any stormwater, surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, uncontaminated cooling water or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer nor shall a person discharge sanitary or industrial wastewater to any storm sewer or natural waterway runoff. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 1, 11-21-90; Ord. No. 2003-2, 2-17-03) 
Sec. 94-92. - Stormwater. 
    Stormwater and all other unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to such sewers as are specifically designated as storm sewers or to a natural outlet approved by the state department of environmental management or the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency. Industrial cooling water or unpolluted process waters may be discharged, on approval of the state department of environmental management or the Environmental Protection Agency, to a storm sewer or natural outlet. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 2, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-93. - Prohibited discharges. 
    No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following described waters or wastes to any public sewers: 
(1)  Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or explosive liquid, solid or gas. 
(2)  Any waters or wastes containing toxic poisonous solids, liquids or gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other wastes, to interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance or create any hazard in the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant. 
(3)  Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or having any other corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment and personnel of the sewer works. 
(4)  Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of such size capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers or other interference with the proper operation of the sewer works, such as but not limited to ashes, cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar, plastics, wood, unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and fleshings, entrails and paper dishes, cups, milk containers, etc., either whole or ground by garbage grinders. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 3, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-94. - Discharge of harmful substances. 
    No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged the following described substances, materials, waters or wastes if it appears likely in the opinion of the superintendent that such wastes can harm either the sewers, sewage treatment process or equipment, have an adverse effect on the receiving stream or can otherwise endanger life, limb, public property or constitute a nuisance. In forming his opinion as to the acceptability of these wastes, the superintendent will give consideration of such factors as the quantities of wastes in relation to flows and velocities in the sewers, materials of construction of the sewers, nature of the sewage treatment process, capacity of the sewage treatment plant, degree of treatability of wastes in the sewage treatment plant and other pertinent factors. The substances prohibited are: 
(1)  Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than 150 degrees Fahrenheit (65 degrees Celsius). 
(2)  Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease or oils, whether emulsified or not, in excess of 100 mg/l or containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures between 32 and 150 degrees Fahrenheit (0 and 65 degrees Celsius). 
(3)  Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation and operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths horsepower (0.76 hp metric) or greater shall be subject to review and approval of the superintendent. 
(4)  Any waters or wastes containing strong acid iron pickling wastes or concentrated plating solutions, whether neutralized or not. 
(5)  Any waters or wastes containing iron, chromium, copper, zinc, cyanide and similar objectionable or toxic substances or wastes exerting an excessive chlorine requirement to such degree that any such material received in the composite sewage at the sewage treatment works exceeds the limits established by the superintendent or the state department of environmental management or the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency for such materials. 
(6)  Any waters or wastes containing phenols or other taste- or odor-producing substances, in such concentrations exceeding limits which may be established by the superintendent as necessary, after treatment of the composite sewage to meet the requirements of the state, federal or other public agencies of jurisdiction for such discharge to the receiving waters. 
(7)  Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or concentration as may exceed limits established by the superintendent in compliance with applicable state or federal regulations. 
(8)  Any waters or wastes having a pH in excess of 9.5. 
(9)  Materials which exert or cause: 
a.  Unusual concentrations of inert suspended solids (such as but not limited to fuller's earth, lime slurries and lime residues) or of dissolved solids (such as but not limited to sodium chloride and sodium sulfate). 
b.  Excessive discoloration, such as but not limited to dye wastes and vegetable tanning solutions. 
c.  Unusual BOD (above 270 mg/l), chemical oxygen demand or chlorine requirement in such quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment works. 
d.  Unusual volume of flow or concentration of wastes constituting slugs. 
(10)  Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amenable to treatment or reduction by the sewage treatment processes employed or are amenable to treatment only to such degree that the sewage treatment plant effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over discharge to the receiving waters. 
(11)  Waters or wastes containing suspended solids in excess of 320 mg/l. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 4, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-95. - Authority over prohibited wastes. 
(a)  If any waters or wastes are discharged or are proposed to be discharged to the public sewers, which waters contain the substances or possess the characteristics enumerated in section 94-94 and which, in the judgement of the superintendent or the state department of environmental management or the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency, may have a deleterious effect upon the sewer works, processes, equipment or receiving waters or which otherwise create a hazard to life or constitute a public nuisance, the superintendent may: 
(1)  Reject the wastes; 
(2)  Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the public sewers; 
(3)  Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; and/or 
(4)  Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating the wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charges under the provisions of section 94-100. 
(b)  If the superintendent permits the pretreatment or equalization of waste flows, the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be subject to the review and approval of the board's engineer and the state department of environmental management or the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency and subject to the requirements of all applicable codes, ordinances and laws. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 5, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-96. - Interceptors. 
    Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of the superintendent, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes containing grease in excessive amounts or any flammable wastes, sand or other harmful ingredients, except that such interceptors shall not be required for private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall be of a type and capacity approved by the superintendent and shall be located to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 6, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-97. - Maintenance of facilities. 
    Where preliminary treatment or flow-equalizing facilities are provided for any waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at his expense. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 7, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-98. - Control manholes. 
    When required by the superintendent, the owner of any property serviced by a building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable control manhole, together with such necessary meters and other appurtenances in the building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and measurement of the wastes. Such manholes, when required, shall be accessibly and safely located and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by the superintendent. The manhole shall be maintained by him to be safe and accessible at all times. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 8, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-99. - Measurements, tests and analyses. 
    All measurements, tests and analyses of the characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made in this article shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of Standard Methods for the Examination of Water and Wastewater, published by the American Public Health Association, and shall be determined at the control manhole provided or upon suitable samples taken at the control manhole. If no special manhole has been required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is connected. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily accepted methods to reflect the effect of constituents upon the sewer works and to determine the existence of hazards to life, limb and property. The particular analyses involved will determine whether a 24-hour composite of all outfalls of a premises is appropriate or whether a grab sample shall be taken. Normally, but not always, BOD and suspended solids analyses are obtained from 24-hour composites of all outfalls whereas pH's are determined from periodic grab samples. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 9, 11-21-90) 
Sec. 94-100. - Special agreements. 
    No statement contained in this article shall be construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the board and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by the board for treatment, subject to payment therefor, by the industrial concern. 
(Ord. No. 1990-17, art. V, § 10, 11-21-90)
